Hajj — Pilgrimage

Deputyship in Hajj: Permanent Inability and Recovery
Intra-Hanafi dispute on condition for Hajj deputyship and effect of recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid deputyship in Hajj according to the Hanafi school and contrast the two intra-Hanafi positions on the effect of subsequent recovery of the principal.

Core Idea
Hajj deputyship hinges on permanent inability – if recovery was possible, the deputyship is conditional.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq explains the critical condition for deputyship in Hajj: the principal must be permanently unable until death. It then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens if the principal recovers after appointing a deputy? The apparent view from al-Mukhtasar and Fatḥ al-Qadīr holds that any recovery invalidates the deputyship. The author rejects this and presents the detailed, preferred view that distinguishes between conditions from which recovery is expected and those from which it is not.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the shift in topic
The passage begins with a rule about intention in financial deputyship to contrast with Hajj. Note that financial deputyship is always permitted and intention of the principal governs. This sets up the more restrictive rule for Hajj.
The financial deputyship discussion is a prelude; the main topic is Hajj.
2
Locate the condition statement
Find the phrase 'والشرط العجز الدائم إلى وقت الموت' (the condition is permanent inability until the time of death). This is the core rule. Identify that the inability must be continuous and expected to last until death.
The word 'دائم' is key – it means perpetual, not temporary.
3
Understand the rationale
Hajj is a personal obligation once in a lifetime. Deputyship is a concession (rukhṣa) for those who cannot perform it themselves due to permanent inability. If one can recover, the concession does not apply because the obligation remains personally binding.
The text says 'رخص له الاستنابة رحمة وفضلاً' – a mercy and favor.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is a difference of opinion: the apparent view from al-Mukhtasar and Fatḥ al-Qadīr makes no distinction between recoverable and non-recoverable illnesses; recovery always invalidates the deputyship. The author declares this 'not correct' and presents the detailed view that distinguishes.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf within the Ḥanafī school.
5
Apply the tarjih
The detailed view is preferred (muftā bihī) and supported by authorities like al-Nahr, al-Tanwīr, and al-Shurunbulāliyya. The practical difference: a blind person who recovers does not need to repeat Hajj; a sick person who recovers from a curable illness must perform Hajj himself.
The ruling for chronic conditions like blindness and zamāna (infirmity) is that the deputyship remains valid even if the condition later ceases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العقاب لا التخفيف في طريق الإسقاط . وإذا جازت النيابة في المالية مطلقاً فالعبرة لنية الموكل لا لنية الوكيل، وسواء نوى الموكل وقت الدفع إلى الوكيل أو وقت دفع الوكيل إلى الفقراء أو فيما بينهما، ولهذا قال في الفتاوى الظهيرية من فصل مصارف الزكاة: رجل دفع إلى رجل دراهم ليتصدق بها على الفقراء تطوعاً فلم يتصدق المأمور حتى نوى الأمر عن الزكاة من غير أن يتلفظ به، ثم تصدق المأمور جاز عن الزكاة وكذا لو استمر ذلك العذر أو زال صرح به في المحيط وفتاوى قاضيخان والمبسوط، وصرح في معراج الدراية بأنه إذا حج الأعمى غيره ثم زال العمى لا يبطل الإحجاج ا هـ . وقيد بالعجز الدائم لأنه لو أحج وهو صحيح ثم عجز واستمر لا يجزئه لفقد الشرط، ويشكل عليه ما في التجنيس وفتاوى قاضيخان وغيرهما أنه لو قال الله علي ثلاثون حجة» فأحج ثلاثين نفساً في سنة واحدة إن مات قبل أن يجيء وقت الحج جاز عن الكل لأنه لم تعرف قدرته بنفسه عند حاشية الدر المختار أن المال من معتبر في الحج اعتباراً قوياً بحيث لا يتأتى ولا يتحصل إلا به غالياً فكان كالجزء قوله (بل الحق التفصيل الخ) نقله في النهر وأقره وتابعه في متن التنوير وحققه في الشرنبلالية. وقال الإمام قاضيخان في شرحه على الجامع الصغير : ثم إنما يصح الأمر إذا كان الأمر عاجزاً بنفسه عجزاً لا يرجى زواله كالعمى والزمانة، وإن كان عجزاً يرجى زواله كالحبس والمرض إن دام إلى الموت يقع موقعه وإن زال كان الحج على الأمر على حاله قوله (بطلت حجته الذي في الخانية والفتح والنهر (حجة» بدون ضمير، وقوله «وعلى هذا
Punishment is not alleviation in the path of dropping. And when deputyship is allowed in financial acts absolutely, then consideration is given to the intention of the principal, not the intention of the agent. It is equal whether the principal intends at the time of giving to the agent or at the time of the agent's payment to the poor or in between. Thus said in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya from the section on the categories of zakat: 'A man gave dirhams to a man to give them as charity to the poor voluntarily, and the agent did not give in charity until the principal intended it for zakat without uttering it, then the agent gave in charity; it is valid for zakat.' Similarly, if he ordered him to manumit a slave voluntarily, and the principal intended it for expiation before the agent's manumission of the voluntary [enslavement], it is valid. Thus, the eligibility of the deputy is not considered, even if a Muslim appoints a dhimmi to pay zakat, it is valid, as in Kashf al-Asrar Sharh Usul Fakhr al-Islam. His statement: 'And the condition is permanent inability until the time of death' i.e., the condition for the permissibility of deputyship in the combined [act] is that the principal is unable in a continuous inability until his death, because Hajj is an obligation of a lifetime. Since his address is attached to it due to the existence of the condition, it is incumbent upon him to perform it himself in the first year of capability. If he delays, he sins and the performance by himself becomes established in his liability for the duration of his life. And if he is not qualified by the conditions, then if he becomes unable to do that in the duration of his life, he is permitted to appoint a deputy as mercy and favor. If he becomes able at a time in his life after having appointed a deputy due to an inability that befell him, the condition of the concession is void. Then the apparent meaning of what is in al-Mukhtasar is that there is no difference between an illness whose removal is hoped for and one whose removal is not hoped for, like chronic infirmity and blindness. Thus, if a chronically infirm or blind person performed Hajj [by deputy] and then recovered and regained sight, he is required to perform Hajj himself. And due to this, the investigator in Fath al-Qadir explicitly stated it, but it is not correct. Rather, the truth is the detail: if it was an illness whose removal is hoped for, and he performed Hajj [by deputy], then the matter is pending; if the inability continues until death, the obligation falls, otherwise not. If it was an illness whose removal is not hoped for, like blindness, and another performed Hajj for him, the obligation falls from him, whether that excuse continues or is removed. This is stated in al-Muhit, Fatawa Qadikhan, and al-Mabsut. And it is stated in Mi'raj al-Diraya that if a blind person's deputy performed Hajj and then the blindness is removed, the deputyship is not invalidated. And it is restricted to permanent inability because if a healthy person performs Hajj [by deputy] and then becomes unable continuously, it does not suffice due to the loss of the condition. And it is problematic what is in al-Tajnis and Fatawa Qadikhan and others that if one says 'I owe thirty Hajjs' and he appoints thirty persons in one year, if he dies before the time of Hajj comes, it is valid for all because his own ability at the time of Hajj was not known. If the time of Hajj comes and he is able, his Hajj is invalidated because a thing cannot be composed of its condition. It can be said that a thing not being composed of its condition is in real composites, not in legal ones. As in the margin of Miskin. And better is what is mentioned in the margin of al-Durr al-Mukhtar that wealth is considered in Hajj in a strong way such that it is generally not accomplished except with it, so it is like a part. His statement: 'Rather, the truth is the detail' is transmitted in al-Nahr and he approved it, and it is followed in Matn al-Tanwir and verified in al-Shurunbulaliyya. Imam Qadikhan said in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Then the order is only valid if the principal is unable himself with an inability whose removal is not hoped for, like blindness and chronic infirmity. If it is an inability whose removal is hoped for, like imprisonment and illness, if it continues until death, it takes effect, and if it is removed, the Hajj remains as it was.' His statement: 'his Hajj is invalidated' which is in al-Khaniyya, al-Fath, and al-Nahr: 'Hajj' without pronoun, and his statement: 'Upon this...'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the condition of permanent inability (ʿajz dāʾim) for deputyship in Hajj. The author first addresses a related point: in financial deputyship, the intention of the principal is what matters, even if the agent is a dhimmi, and the agent can apply the principal's change of intention. Then the main discussion: the condition for deputyship in Hajj is that the principal be continuously unable until death. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a person who recovers after appointing a deputy must perform Hajj again. The apparent view in al-Mukhtasar and Fath al-Qadir is that no distinction is made between recoverable and non-recoverable illnesses; recovery invalidates the deputyship. However, the author declares this incorrect and adopts the detailed position: if the illness was one from which recovery is expected (like a treatable disease), then it is contingent: if the inability continues until death, it suffices; if recovery occurs, it does not. If the illness was one from which recovery is not expected (like blindness or chronic disability), then the deputyship is valid even if recovery occurs later. This detailed view is supported by al-Muhit, Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Mabsut, and others. The passage also addresses a problem: if a healthy person becomes unable after appointing a deputy, it is not valid because the condition of inability was not present at the time of appointment. An apparent problem from al-Tajnis about a vow of thirty Hajjs is resolved by noting that in legal composites, the condition does not need to be present at the time of the act. The text concludes with a note that wealth is an integral part of Hajj.

Key Terms
العجز الدائم (al-ʿajz al-dāʾim): Permanent inability that is expected to last until death, used as the condition for valid deputyship in Hajj
الزمانة (al-zamānah): Chronic disability or infirmity, considered permanent inability
العمى (al-ʿamā): Blindness, considered permanent inability not expected to recover
التفصيل (al-tafṣīl): Detailed ruling distinguishing between illness with and without hope of recovery

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the detailed view (al-tafṣīl), what is the ruling if a blind person appoints a deputy for Hajj and then later regains his sight?
A) The deputyship is invalid and he must perform Hajj himself
B) The deputyship is valid and he does not need to repeat Hajj
C) It depends on whether he was aware of the recovery
D) The deputyship is valid but he must also perform Hajj himself

Key Takeaway
The condition for Hajj deputyship is permanent inability with no hope of recovery; if recovery was not expected, the deputyship remains valid even if recovery occurs later.

Condition of Permanent Incapacity for Proxy Hajj
Explaining the condition of permanent incapacity and the dispute over its continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid proxy Hajj in the Hanafi school and distinguish between the two positions on the continuity of incapacity.

Core Idea
Proxy Hajj requires permanent incapacity until death; for hopeful illness it is suspended, for hopeless it suffices even if cured.

The Hanafi school permits a person to appoint a deputy for Hajj only when he is permanently unable to perform it himself. But what if the incapacity is temporary? Classical texts debate whether a distinction should be made between diseases that are hoped to be cured and those that are not. This lesson explains the condition and the preferred Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for proxy Hajj
The text states that the condition is permanent incapacity (al-ajz al-da'im) that continues until death. This is because Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime obligation; the concession for deputyship only applies when there is no hope of performance throughout life.
Observe the reasoning (talil): Hajj is fard al-umr, so the obligation is established in the lifetime; incapacity triggers the rukhsa.
2
Understand the implication of temporary capability
If the principal becomes capable at any time after appointing a deputy, the condition for the concession is nullified. The text explicitly says: 'If he becomes capable at any time of his lifetime after he had appointed a deputy... the condition for the concession becomes nullified.'
This is the general rule; later we learn an exception for hopeless diseases.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
The apparent position in al-Mukhtasar and Fath al-Qadir makes no distinction: if the incapacity ceases, the proxy is invalid regardless of the nature of the disease. The author (Ibn Nujaym) rejects this as 'not correct'.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school, not between schools.
4
Analyze the preferred view (tafsil)
The correct view (al-haqq) distinguishes: if the disease is hopeless (e.g., blindness, paralysis), the proxy suffices even if the person later recovers; if the disease is hopeful (e.g., temporary illness), the proxy is suspended – if death occurs while incapacitated, it suffices, otherwise not.
The author cites multiple sources: al-Muhit, Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Mabsut, and Miraj al-Dirayah.
5
Apply the ruling to concrete cases
Test: A blind person appoints a deputy then regains sight – proxy valid (hopeless). A person with a fever appoints a deputy then recovers – proxy invalid (hopeful). If the fever patient dies while still ill – proxy valid.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) is the tafsil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والشرط العجز الدائم إلى وقت الموت) أي الشرط في جواز النيابة في المركب عجز المستنيب عجزاً مستمراً إلى موته لأن الحج فرض العمر فحيث تعلق به خطابه لقيام مشروط وجب عليه أن يقوم بنفسه في أول سني الإمكان، فإذا أخر أثم وتقرر القيام بنفسه في ذمته في مدة عمره، وإن كان غير متصف بالشروط، فإذا عجز عن ذلك في مدة عمره رخص له الاستنابة رحمة وفضلاً فحيث قدر عليه وقتاً من عمره بعد ما استنابه فيه لعجز لحقه ظهر انتفاء شرط الرخصة. ثم ظاهر ما في المختصر أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون المرض يرجى زواله أو لا يرجى زواله كالزمانة والعمى، فلو أحج الزمن أو الأعمى ثم صح وأبصر لزمه هذا يحج بنفسه، وبسبب صرح المحقق في فتح القدير به وليس بصحيح، بل الحق التفصيل؛ فإن كان مرضاً يرجى زواله فأحج فالأمر مراعى فإن استمر العجز إلى الموت سقط الفرض عنه وإلا فلا. وإن كان مرضاً لا يرجى زواله كالعمى فأحج غيره سقط الفرض عنه، سواء استمر ذلك العذر أو زال صرح به في المحيط وفتاوى قاضيخان والمبسوط، وصرح في معراج الدراية بأنه إذا حج الأعمى غيره ثم زال العمى لا يبطل الإحجاج ا هـ
His saying: (And the condition is permanent incapacity until the time of death) i.e. the condition for the permissibility of deputyship in the composite act is that the principal is permanently incapacitated continuously until his death, because Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime obligation. So when his address becomes attached to it due to the establishment of the condition, it becomes obligatory upon him to perform it himself in the first year of capability. If he delays, he commits a sin, and the obligation of performing it himself becomes established in his liability throughout his lifetime, even if he is not characterized by the conditions. So when he becomes incapable of that in his lifetime, he is granted a concession to appoint a deputy out of mercy and grace. So if he becomes capable at any time of his lifetime after he had appointed a deputy due to an incapacity that befell him, the condition for the concession becomes nullified. Then the apparent meaning in al-Mukhtasar is that there is no difference between a disease that is hoped to be cured and one that is not, such as chronic paralysis and blindness. So if a paralyzed or blind person appointed someone to perform Hajj and then recovered and regained sight, he would be required to perform Hajj himself. And due to this, the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir explicitly stated it, but it is not correct. Rather, the correct is the detail: if it is a disease hoped to be cured and he appointed someone, then the matter is suspended: if the incapacity continues until death, his obligation falls; otherwise no. And if it is a disease not hoped to be cured, like blindness, and someone else performs Hajj for him, his obligation falls, whether that excuse continues or ceases. This is explicitly stated in al-Muhit, Fatawa Qadikhan, and al-Mabsut. And it is explicitly stated in Miraj al-Dirayah that if a blind person appoints someone to perform Hajj and then his blindness ceases, the proxy Hajj is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the condition of permanent incapacity for proxy Hajj. The author explains that for deputyship in Hajj to be valid, the principal must be continuously incapable until death. This is because Hajj is a lifetime obligation (fard al-umr). Once the person becomes capable (even temporarily after appointing a deputy), the concession for deputyship is lifted. The text then addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school: the apparent position in Mukhtasar (probably by al-Quduri) holds no distinction between diseases that are hoped to be cured and those that are permanent; so if a blind person performs Hajj by proxy and later recovers sight, he must perform Hajj again. However, the author (likely Ibn Nujaym, the commentator of al-Bahr al-Raiq) says this is not correct. The correct position (al-haqq al-tafsil) distinguishes: if the disease is one that is hoped to be cured (e.g., a temporary illness), the proxy Hajj is suspended (mura'a) — if the person dies still incapacitated, it suffices; if he recovers, it does not. But if the disease is not hoped to be cured (e.g., blindness, chronic paralysis), then proxy Hajj suffices even if the person later recovers. The author cites multiple sources: al-Muhit, Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Mabsut, and Miraj al-Dirayah to support this distinction. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the detail (tafsil), as the text explicitly says the other view is not correct.

Key Terms
العجز الدائم (al-ajz al-da'im): Permanent incapacity that continues until death, the condition for valid proxy Hajj.
التفصيل (al-tafsil): The detailed ruling distinguishing between hopeful and hopeless diseases in proxy Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, if a person with a temporary illness (hoped to be cured) appoints a deputy and then dies while still incapacitated, what is the ruling?
A) The proxy does not suffice because the illness was temporary.
B) The proxy suffices because the person died still incapacitated.
C) The proxy is invalid because the illness was hopeful.
D) The proxy is suspended and must be repeated by the heirs.

Key Takeaway
The condition for proxy Hajj is permanent incapacity until death, but the mufta bihi distinguishes between hopeful (suspended) and hopeless (immediately valid) diseases.

Applications of the Incapacity Condition in Hajj by Proxy
Applying the condition of permanent incapacity to specific cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of permanent incapacity to determine the validity of proxy Hajj in cases of a healthy person who later becomes incapacitated, a vow of multiple Hajjs, and a woman without a mahram.

Core Idea
Permanent incapacity for proxy Hajj is judged at the time of standing at Arafah, not at appointment.

This passage applies the condition of permanent incapacity to several scenarios that test the boundaries of the rule. It resolves an apparent contradiction between two positions by distinguishing between the time of appointing a proxy and the time of the proxy's performance. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of Hajj by proxy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its apparent contradiction
Note that a healthy person who later becomes incapacitated cannot have a valid proxy Hajj because the condition of incapacity was absent at appointment. However, a person who vows 30 Hajjs and dies before the first Hajj time has all 30 valid. This creates a puzzle: why is one valid and the other not?
The contradiction is only apparent; the resolution lies in the timing of the incapacity condition.
2
Understand the distinction between real and legal composites
The text introduces the concept of 'legal composites' (al-murakkabat al-i'tibariyyah) versus real composites. For acts like Hajj, the condition (incapacity) is not an integral part of the act itself but a prerequisite for obligation. This allows the ruling to vary based on the timing of the condition.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle applied here.
3
Apply the timing principle: standing at Arafah
The condition of incapacity is evaluated at the moment of the proxy's standing at Arafah. If the principal is dead at that moment, the condition is fulfilled retrospectively. If alive and able, the proxy is invalid for that year. This resolves the 30 Hajjs case: each year's Hajj is judged separately.
The author clarifies that 'time of Hajj' means the day of Arafah, not the months of Hajj.
4
Evaluate the woman without mahram case
A woman without a mahram cannot appoint a proxy until she reaches a state of permanent incapacity (e.g., old age or illness), because the possibility of finding a mahram delays the obligation. If she appoints a proxy and then dies without a mahram, it is valid. This mirrors the sick person case.
The existence of a mahram is a condition for personal performance, not for proxy.
5
Confirm the continuous incapacity condition
The incapacity must continue until death. Examples: prisoner who dies in prison, or someone blocked by an enemy who remains until death. If the obstacle is temporary, the proxy Hajj is invalid. This reinforces that the condition is permanent, not merely present at appointment.
The text mentions both heavenly (sickness) and human-caused obstacles (imprisonment, enemy).

Source Text

وقيد بالعجز الدائم لأنه لو أحج وهو صحيح ثم عجز واستمر لا يجزئه لفقد الشرط، ويشكل عليه ما في التجنيس وفتاوى قاضيخان وغيرهما أنه لو قال الله علي ثلاثون حجة» فأحج ثلاثين نفساً في سنة واحدة إن مات قبل أن وأقره وتابعه في متن التنوير وحققه في الشرنبلالية. وقال الإمام قاضيخان في شرحه على الجامع الصغير : ثم إنما يصح الأمر إذا كان الأمر عاجزاً بنفسه عجزاً لا يرجى زواله كالعمى والزمانة، وإن كان عجزاً يرجى يكون في أشهر الحج فلا يتأتى التفصيل، وإن كان المكان بعيداً فأحج قبل الأشهر فهو قاصر الإفادة عما إذا كان قريباً فأحج في الأشهر الحرم فالأولى ما قلناه ووجه إشكاله على ما سبق أن وقت الإحجاج كان صحيحاً فإذا مات قبل وقته أجزأه، وقد تقدم أنه إذا أحج وهو صحيح ثم عجز لا يجزئه، ودفعه بأن المراد بعجزه بعد الإحجاج العجز بعد فراغ النائب عن الحج بأن كان وقت الوقوف صحيحاً فلا مخالفة كما لا يخفى. وعلى هذا المرأة إذا لم تجد محرماً لا تخرج إلى الحج إلى أن تبلغ الوقت الذي تعجز عن الحج فحينئذ تبعث من يحج عنها، أما قبل ذلك فلا يجوز لتوهم وجود المحرم، فإن بعثت رجلاً، إن دام عدم المحرم إلا أن ماتت فذلك جائز كالمريض إذا أحج عنه رجلاً ودام المرض إلى أن مات وأطلق في العجز فشمل ما إذا كان سماوياً أو بصنع العباد فلو أحج وهو في السجن فإذا مات فيه أجزأه وإن خلص منه لا. وإن أحج لعدوّ بينه وبين مكة إن أقام العدو على الطريق حتى مات أجزأه وإن لم يقم يجزئه . كذا في التجنيس
And he qualified it with permanent incapacity because if he appoints someone while he is healthy and then becomes incapacitated and it continues, it does not suffice for him due to the loss of the condition. And there is a problem with this from what is in al-Tajnis and Fatawa Qadikhan and others: that if he said, 'Upon me (is the obligation of) thirty Hajjs,' and he appoints thirty persons in one year, if he dies before the time of Hajj arrives, it suffices for all because his ability by himself at the time of the arrival of Hajj is not known. And if the time of Hajj arrives while he is able, his Hajj is invalidated because a thing is not composed of its condition. And it can be said: The thing not being composed of its condition applies to real composites, not to legal ones. Thus in the marginal notes of Miskin. And the best is what was mentioned in the marginal notes of al-Durr al-Mukhtar: that wealth is considered in Hajj with a strong consideration such that it is not possible nor accomplished without it generally, so it is like a part. His saying (but the correct is the detail etc.) is transmitted in al-Nahr and he approved it, and followed it in the text of al-Tanwir, and verified it in al-Sharnablaliyyah. And Imam Qadikhan said in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir: Then the command is only valid if the commander is himself incapacitated with an incapacity not hoped to be removed, like blindness and chronic paralysis. If it is an incapacity hoped to be removed, like imprisonment and illness, if it continues until death, it takes effect; if it ceases, the Hajj remains upon the commander as it was. His saying (his Hajj is invalidated) which is in al-Khaniyyah, al-Fath, and al-Nahr: (a Hajj) without a pronoun. And his saying: 'And upon this, every year that comes' i.e. that in the second year, if he dies before the arrival of the time of Hajj, it suffices for the remaining (twenty-nine), and if he dies after it while able, one Hajj is invalidated, and so on for the third and fourth years until the end. And he should intend by 'time of Hajj' the time of standing at Arafah, meaning if the day of Arafah comes while he is dead, all suffice; if he is alive, one is invalidated and the matter is suspended for the rest. And what is meant by 'time of Hajj' is not the months of Hajj, because the appointment of a proxy occurs in the months of Hajj, so the detail would not be possible. And if the place is distant and he appoints a proxy before the months, then it is deficient in benefit compared to if it were near and he appoints a proxy in the sacred months. So the best is what we said. And the face of the problem according to what preceded is that the time of appointing a proxy was when he was healthy, so if he dies before its time, it suffices him. And it has preceded that if he appoints a proxy while healthy and then becomes incapacitated, it does not suffice him. And its repulsion is that what is meant by his incapacity after the appointment is the incapacity after the proxy completes the Hajj, such that at the time of standing he was able, so there is no contradiction, as is not hidden. And upon this, the woman who does not find a mahram: she does not go out for Hajj until she reaches the time when she becomes incapable of Hajj; then she sends someone to perform Hajj on her behalf. As for before that, it is not permissible due to the possibility of the existence of a mahram. So if she sends a man, if the lack of a mahram continues until she dies, then that is permissible, like a sick person who appoints a man to perform Hajj on his behalf and the illness continues until he dies. And he gave an absolute ruling on incapacity, including whether it is heavenly or by human action. So if he appoints someone while in prison, then if he dies in it, it suffices him; if he is released, no. And if he appoints someone for an enemy between him and Mecca, if the enemy remains on the road until he dies, it suffices him; if not, it does not suffice. Thus in al-Tajnis.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage applies the condition of permanent incapacity to several scenarios. First, a healthy person who appoints a proxy and then later becomes permanently incapacitated: the proxy Hajj is not valid because at the time of appointment he was not incapacitated. However, this raises a problem from other Hanafi sources: if someone vows 30 Hajjs and appoints 30 proxies in one year, if he dies before the Hajj time (standing at Arafah), all 30 are valid because his ability at that future time was not known. The resolution is that the condition of incapacity is evaluated at the time of the proxy's performance, not the time of appointment. For the 30 Hajjs case, if the principal dies before the first Hajj time, all are valid; if he lives through it while able, only that one Hajj is invalidated and the rest depend on his state at their respective times. The author clarifies that 'time of Hajj' refers to the moment of standing at Arafah, not the entire months. Another scenario is a woman without a mahram: she must wait until she reaches a state of permanent incapacity (old age or illness) before she can appoint a proxy. If she appoints one earlier, the proxy is not valid because a mahram might become available. If she appoints one and then dies without a mahram still, it suffices. Similarly, a prisoner or someone blocked by an enemy: if the obstacle is permanent until death, the proxy Hajj is valid; if the obstacle is removed, it is not. These illustrate the principle that the incapacity must be continuous until death.

Key Terms
المركبات الاعتبارية (al-murakkabat al-i'tibariyyah): Legal composites (like Hajj) where the condition (incapacity) is not a part of the act itself.
المحرم (al-mahram): A male relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, required for women traveling for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only after she becomes permanently incapacitated (e.g., old age or illness).
C) Only if she is wealthy.
D) She can never appoint a proxy because she can go alone.

Key Takeaway
Permanent incapacity for proxy Hajj is evaluated at the time of the proxy's standing at Arafah, not at the time of appointment.

Conditions for Valid Proxy Hajj
Listing conditions for valid proxy Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for valid proxy Hajj according to the Hanafi school as listed in Badai' al-Sanai'.

Core Idea
Proxy Hajj is valid only for the permanently incapacitated, using the principal's wealth and explicit command.

Imam al-Kasani in Badai' al-Sanai' enumerates the conditions (shurut) under which one person may perform Hajj on behalf of another. This lesson walks through each condition, explaining why it is required and what happens if it is missing. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the rules of deputyship in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's state
The first condition: the principal must be permanently incapable of performing Hajj himself and must possess wealth. A healthy person, rich or poor, cannot appoint a proxy.
Wealth is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub), not a condition for proxy.
2
Confirm permanent incapacity
The incapacity must be permanent until death. Temporary illness does not justify proxy.
This condition distinguishes the Hanafi view from others.
3
Check the command (amr)
The principal must explicitly command the proxy, except in the case of the heir performing Hajj for a deceased person, which is considered an implied command.
An unauthorized proxy is not valid.
4
Verify intention and wealth
The principal must have the intention (niyyah) at the time of the proxy's ihram, and the Hajj must be performed using the principal's wealth. Volunteering one's own wealth does not suffice.
This ensures the obligation is tied to the principal's own resources.
5
Ensure the proxy rides
The proxy must perform Hajj riding. If he walks despite being commanded to ride, he must guarantee the expenses and repeat the Hajj riding.
The text cuts off here, but this is the final condition listed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في البدائع : وأما شرائط جواز النيابة فمنها أن يكون المحجوج عنه عاجزاً. عن الأداء بنفسه وله مال فلا يجوز إحجاج الصحيح غنياً كان أو فقيراً. لأن المال من شرائط الوجوب . ومنها العجز المستدام إن الموت. ومنها الأمر بالحج فلا يجوز الغير عنه بغير أمره إلا الوارث يحج عن مورثه فإنه يجزئه إن شاء الله تعالى لوجود الأمر حج دلالة. ومنها نية المحجوج عنه عند الإحرام. ومنها أن يكون حج المأمور بمال المحجوج عنه فإن تطوع الحاج عنه بمال نفسه لم يجز عنه حتى يحج بماله وكذا إذا أوصى أن يحج بماله فمات فتطوع عنه وارثه بمال نفسه لأن الفرض تعلق بماله، فإذا لم يحج بماله لم يسقط عنه الفرض. ومنها الحج راكباً حتى لو أمره بالحج فحج ماشياً يضمن النفقة ويحج عنه راكباً لأن
And it is mentioned in al-Badai': As for the conditions for the permissibility of deputyship, among them are: that the one on whose behalf Hajj is performed is incapable of performing it himself and has wealth, so it is not permissible to appoint a proxy for a healthy person, whether rich or poor, because wealth is a condition of obligation. And among them: permanent incapacity until death. And among them: the command to perform Hajj, so it is not permissible for others without his command, except the heir who performs Hajj on behalf of the deceased, for it suffices him, Allah willing, due to the existence of a command by implication. And among them: the intention of the one on whose behalf it is performed at the time of ihram. And among them: that the Hajj of the agent be with the wealth of the principal, for if the volunteer performs Hajj on his behalf with his own wealth, it does not suffice him until he performs Hajj with his wealth. Similarly, if he bequeathed that Hajj be performed with his wealth and he dies, and his heir volunteers with his own wealth, it does not suffice because the obligation is attached to his wealth; so if it is not performed with his wealth, the obligation is not lifted from him. And among them: performing Hajj riding, so if he commands him to perform Hajj and he performs it walking, he guarantees the expenses and performs Hajj for him riding, because...
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage from Imam al-Kasani's Badai' al-Sanai' lists the conditions for a valid proxy Hajj in the Hanafi school. The first condition is that the principal (the one being represented) is incapable of performing Hajj himself and has wealth. A healthy person, whether rich or poor, cannot appoint a proxy. This is because wealth is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) for Hajj, so if a person is healthy and poor, Hajj is not obligatory on him, so no proxy is needed. Second, the incapacity must be permanent until death, as discussed earlier. Third, the principal must command (order) the proxy; an unauthorized person cannot perform Hajj on someone else's behalf except the heir who does so for the deceased without explicit command, because the deceased's obligation is implied by his state. Fourth, the principal must intend (niyyah) for the proxy to perform Hajj at the time of ihram. Fifth, the Hajj must be performed with the principal's wealth; using another's wealth does not fulfill the obligation. Sixth, the proxy must perform Hajj riding (not walking); if he walks, he must guarantee the expenses and repeat the Hajj riding. The list is incomplete in the OCR, but these are the key conditions.

Key Terms
النيابة في الحج (al-niyabah fi al-hajj): Deputyship in Hajj, where one person performs Hajj on behalf of another.
الأمر بالحج (al-amr bi al-hajj): The principal's explicit or implicit command to the proxy to perform Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the conditions in Badai' al-Sanai', which of the following is a condition for valid proxy Hajj?
A) The principal must be healthy and wealthy.
B) The proxy must walk to Mecca.
C) The Hajj must be performed with the principal's wealth.
D) The proxy must be a relative of the principal.

Key Takeaway
Proxy Hajj is only valid if the principal is permanently incapacitated, commands the proxy, intends on his behalf, provides his own wealth, and the proxy rides.

Perpetual Incapacity at the Time of Standing in Hajj Deputyship
Explains the ruling on one who commissions a deputy then dies before the time of standing at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of perpetual incapacity for Hajj deputyship and apply it to scenarios involving death or obstruction at the time of standing at Arafah.

Core Idea
The validity of Hajj deputyship hinges on the principal's incapacity at the moment of standing at Arafah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq explains a critical nuance in Hajj deputyship: the principal must be perpetually incapacitated until the very moment of standing at ʿArafah. If he dies exactly at that time, the deputyship fulfills all past Hajj obligations; if he is alive, only one year is fulfilled and the rest remain pending. The author also resolves an apparent contradiction and extends the ruling to analogous cases like the woman without a mahram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is commissioning a deputy (tajhīz) for obligatory Hajj. The ruling is that it suffices for all past obligations only if the principal dies exactly at the time of standing at Arafah; otherwise only one year's obligation is fulfilled.
The key is that the incapacity must be perpetual at the critical moment.
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The author does not quote a direct scriptural proof but relies on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and rational reasoning (dalīl ʿaqlī): the ruling is based on the principle that what matters is the principal's state at the moment the deputy performs the rites.
The proof is not naqlī but 'aqlī, rooted in the concept of perpetual incapacity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The legal link is that deputyship compensates for an inability that is expected to persist forever. If the principal dies at the time of standing, his inability is definitively perpetual; if he is alive, the inability might end, so the deputyship covers only the current year.
This is why the time of standing is decisive, not the months of Hajj.
4
Note the ikhtilāf (dispute)
The Shāfiʿī school generally does not permit deputyship for a living person at all, whereas the Ḥanafī school allows it under conditions of perpetual incapacity.
The practical difference is that in the Shāfiʿī school, a living person cannot delegate Hajj, even if permanently incapacitated.
5
Evaluate the Ḥanafī tarjīḥ
The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) in the Ḥanafī school is that perpetual incapacity is a condition for deputyship to suffice for all years. This is from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
The author does not mention a specific tarjīḥ authority, but the ruling is consistent with the six core books.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He can perform it himself, so the condition is absent. And upon this, every year that comes... It is proper that 'time of Hajj' means the time of standing at Arafah, meaning: if the day of Arafah comes and he is dead, it suffices for all; if he is alive, one is invalidated and the rest are suspended. It is not meant by 'time of Hajj' the months of Hajj, because commissioning Hajj takes place in the months of Hajj, so the detail is not applicable. If the place is distant and he commissioned before the months, it is deficient in benefit compared to if it is near and he commissioned in the sacred months. The correct view is what we said. The apparent difficulty: previously that the time of commissioning was valid, then if he dies before its time it suffices; and it has preceded that if he commissions while healthy then becomes incapable, it does not suffice. The response: what is meant by his incapacity after commissioning is incapacity after the deputy completes Hajj, i.e., the time of standing is valid, so there is no contradiction. Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the condition of perpetual incapacity for Hajj deputyship. The author clarifies that the relevant time is the moment of standing at Arafah: if the principal dies exactly at that time, the entire series of Hajj obligations (for multiple years) is fulfilled; if alive, only one year's obligation is fulfilled and the rest remain pending. This resolves the apparent contradiction that a valid commissioning followed by death before the time suffices, whereas commissioning while healthy then becoming incapable does not. The key is that the incapacity must persist until the deputy completes the pilgrimage. The author then extends this logic to analogous cases: a woman without a mahram, a prisoner, and a person obstructed by an enemy. All these illustrate the principle that what matters is being unable to perform Hajj personally at the time of standing.

Key Terms
العجز المستدام (al-'ajz al-mustadam): Perpetual incapacity: a condition that continues until death or until the time of standing at Arafah, such that the principal cannot perform Hajj personally at any future time.
وقت الوقوف (waqt al-wuqūf): The time of standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; the critical moment for determining if the principal's incapacity is perpetual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The Hajj counts for only one year.

Key Takeaway
The decisive moment for perpetual incapacity in Hajj deputyship is the time of standing at Arafah: death exactly at that time fulfills all obligations; otherwise only one year is covered.

Six Conditions for Valid Hajj Deputyship
Lists and explains the conditions for valid deputyship in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for valid Hajj deputyship and explain the legal reasoning behind each condition.

Core Idea
Deputyship in Hajj requires the principal's perpetual incapacity, explicit commission (except heir), and the deputy must ride and use the principal's wealth.

This passage from al-Bada'i' by al-Kāsānī lists the six conditions that must be met for a deputized Hajj to be valid. Understanding these conditions ensures that the obligation of Hajj is fulfilled correctly when a Muslim cannot perform it personally. The conditions are derived from the Quran and Sunnah and reflect the Hanafi school's emphasis on precision in fulfilling obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Six Conditions
Read the Arabic text carefully and extract each condition mentioned. The passage uses phrases like 'minhā an yakūna...' for each condition. List them in order.
There are six distinct conditions: principal's incapacity, perpetual incapacity, commission, intention, use of principal's wealth, and riding.
2
Analyze the Rationale for Each Condition
For each condition, find the reason given in the text. For example, why wealth is required? Why riding? Understanding the rationale helps in applying the rules consistently.
Wealth is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujūb); the obligation is attached to the principal's wealth.
3
Examine the Exception for the Heir
The text states an exception: the heir may perform Hajj for the deceased without an explicit commission, because the command is implied. Understand why this exception exists and how it differs from other cases.
This is based on the implied command from the will (waṣiyyah) or the default obligation on the heir.
4
Study the Consequence of Violating the Riding Condition
If the deputy walks instead of riding, he is liable for expenses and must repeat the Hajj riding. Note the legal effect: the original obligation is not fulfilled, and the deputy must make amends.
The ruling shows that riding is not merely recommended but an obligatory element (wajib) of the deputized Hajj.
5
Refine Understanding with Fatḥ al-Qadīr's Clarification
The passage cites Fatḥ al-Qadīr to clarify that the majority of expenses must come from the principal's wealth, but if the deputy pays out of necessity, he can recover the amount. Relate this to general Hanafi principles on expenditures.
This aligns with the principle that the deputy acts as an agent and can seek reimbursement for necessary expenses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في البدائع : وأما شرائط جواز النيابة فمنها أن يكون المحجوج عنه عاجزاً. عن الأداء بنفسه وله مال فلا يجوز إحجاج الصحيح غنياً كان أو فقيراً. لأن المال من شرائط الوجوب . ومنها العجز المستدام إن الموت. ومنها الأمر بالحج فلا يجوز الغير عنه بغير أمره إلا الوارث يحج عن مورثه فإنه يجزئه إن شاء الله تعالى لوجود الأمر حج دلالة. ومنها نية المحجوج عنه عند الإحرام. ومنها أن يكون حج المأمور بمال المحجوج عنه فإن تطوع الحاج عنه بمال نفسه لم يجز عنه حتى يحج بماله وكذا إذا أوصى أن يحج بماله فمات فتطوع عنه وارثه بمال نفسه لأن الفرض تعلق بماله، فإذا لم يحج بماله لم يسقط عنه الفرض. ومنها الحج راكباً حتى لو أمره بالحج فحج ماشياً يضمن النفقة ويحج عنه راكباً لأن المفروض عليه هو الحج راكباً فينصرف مطلق الأمر بالحج إليه، فإذا ماشياً فقد خالف فيضمن ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن شرط الإجزاء كون أكثر النفقة من مال الأمر، فإن أنفق الأكثر أو الكل من مال نفسه وفي المال المدفوع إليه وفاء بحجه رجع به فيه إذ قد يبتلى بالإنفاق من مال نفسه لبعث الحاجة ولا يكون المال حاضراً فيجوز ذلك كالوصي والوكيل يشتري لليتيم ويعطي الثمن من مال نفسه فإنه يرجع به في مال اليتيم ا هـ . وبهذا علم أن اشتراطهم أن تكون النفقة من مال الآمر للاحتراز عن التبرع لا مطلقاً.
And it is mentioned in al-Badā'i': As for the conditions for the permissibility of deputyship: among them is that the person on whose behalf Hajj is performed must be incapable of performing it himself and must have wealth. So it is not permissible to deputize a healthy person, whether rich or poor, because wealth is a condition of obligation. And among them is perpetual incapacity until death. And among them is the commission to perform Hajj, so it is not permissible for another to perform it without his command, except the heir performing Hajj on behalf of the testator, for it suffices, God willing, because the command exists implicitly. And among them is the intention of the principal at the time of iḥrām. And among them is that the Hajj of the deputy must be with the wealth of the principal; if the hajjī volunteers with his own wealth, it does not count until he performs Hajj with the principal's wealth. Similarly, if he bequeaths that Hajj be performed with his wealth, then dies, and his heir volunteers with his own wealth, it does not count because the obligation is attached to his wealth. And among them is performing Hajj riding; even if he commissions him to perform Hajj and he performs it walking, he is liable for the expenses and must perform Hajj riding because the obligated Hajj is riding, so the absolute command to perform Hajj applies to that. So if he walks, he has contravened and is liable. And in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: Know that the condition for sufficiency is that the majority of expenses be from the principal's wealth. If he spends the majority or all from his own wealth and in the wealth given to him there is enough for his Hajj, he recovers it from the principal, because sometimes he may be forced to spend from his own wealth due to need and the money is not at hand. This is permissible, like the executor or agent who buys for the orphan and pays from his own wealth, then recovers from the orphan's wealth. From this it is known that their condition that the expenses be from the principal's wealth is to avoid voluntary charity, not absolutely.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions for valid deputyship in Hajj as recorded in al-Badā'i' by al-Kāsānī. The conditions are: (1) The principal must be incapable of performing Hajj himself and must possess wealth—a healthy person cannot be deputized regardless of financial status. (2) The incapacity must be perpetual, lasting until death. (3) The deputy must be commissioned by the principal; an exception is the heir performing Hajj for the deceased, where command is implied. (4) The principal must form the intention at the time of iḥrām. (5) The Hajj must be performed using the principal's wealth—volunteering from the deputy's own wealth does not suffice. (6) The deputy must perform Hajj riding; walking contravenes the obligation and requires liability and repetition. The author then cites Fatḥ al-Qadīr to clarify that the majority of expenses must come from the principal's wealth, but if the deputy pays from his own out of necessity, he can recover the amount from the principal's estate, analogous to an executor's practice.

Key Terms
النيابة (al-niyābah): Deputyship: the act of performing Hajj on behalf of another person who is unable to do it themselves.
الأمر بالحج (al-amr bi al-ḥajj): The commission or command given by the principal to the deputy to perform Hajj on his behalf.
العجز المستدام (al-ʿajz al-mustadām): Perpetual incapacity: the principal must be physically or financially unable to perform Hajj for the rest of his life.
الحج راكباً (al-ḥajj rākibā): Performing Hajj while riding (using a mount or vehicle), as opposed to walking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a deputy performs Hajj walking without a valid excuse?
A) The Hajj is valid and no liability.
B) The deputy is liable for expenses and must repeat Hajj riding.
C) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated regardless of liability.
D) The deputy is excused because he intended well.

Key Takeaway
The six conditions for valid Hajj deputyship ensure that the obligation is fulfilled exactly as intended, with the principal's wealth, commission, intention, and the normal mode of travel.

Deputyship in Hajj: Conditions and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute over Whom the Hajj Falls Upon
Distinguishes conditions for deputyship and debates ownership of the Hajj act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conditions for deputyship in obligatory and voluntary Hajj, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the Hajj falls on the principal or the deputy.

Core Idea
For obligatory Hajj, incapacity is required for deputyship; for voluntary, it is not. The dispute on whom the Hajj falls has no practical consequence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq tackles two key aspects of deputyship in Hajj. First, it clarifies that the condition of permanent incapacity applies only to obligatory Hajj (including the Hajj of Islam and vowed Hajj), while voluntary Hajj may be deputized even if the principal is capable. Second, it presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the actual Hajj falls on the principal (āmir) or the deputy (ma'mūr). The author, Ibn Nujaym, critically refines the well-known view while noting the later scholars' position, ultimately concluding that the difference has no practical effect on the discharge of the principal's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of Hajj and their conditions for deputyship
The passage first distinguishes between obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam and vowed Hajj) and voluntary Hajj. For obligatory Hajj, the principal must be permanently incapacitated; for voluntary, deputyship is allowed even if the principal is capable.
The condition of incapacity is only for obligatory Hajj.
2
Understand the effect of the principal's recovery after commissioning
If the principal recovers after commissioning for obligatory Hajj, the description of obligation is lost, but the Hajj remains valid as a voluntary act for the principal. This is unlike prayer, where invalidation of the description nullifies the act according to Imam Muhammad.
Hajj is broader than prayer in this regard.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on whom the Hajj falls
The well-known Hanafi position (zahir al-riwaya) holds that the Hajj falls on the principal. The later scholars (e.g., al-Kashf) and a narration from Imam Muhammad hold that it falls on the deputy, with the principal receiving reward for expenses.
The dispute is over the ownership of the act, not the validity.
4
Examine the evidence from the hadith of Khath'amiyyah
The hadith has two recitations: one with 'afahujju 'anhu' (I perform Hajj on his behalf) supporting the principal view, and another with 'afhijju 'anhu' (I send someone) supporting the deputy view. Both are within the Hanafi tradition.
The well-known recitation is the first.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah)
The author states there is no practical difference because both sides agree that the principal's obligation is discharged, the deputy does not become obligated, and the deputy must intend for the principal. The only condition is that the deputy must be a Muslim (ahlīyah).
The dispute is thus academic, not operational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإنما شرط عجز المنوب للحج الفرض لا النفل) لجواز الإبانة مع القدرة في حج النفل لأن المقصود منه الثواب فإذا كان له تركه أصلاً فله تحمل مشقة المال بالأولى. أطلقه فشمل حجة الإسلام والحجة المنذورة، وأشار به إلى أنه لو أحج الإسلام أو كان مريضاً ثم صح بطل وصف الفرضية لفقد شرطه وهو العجز وبقي أصل الحج تطوعاً للآمر لا أنه فاسد أصلاً صرح به الأسبيجابي والسرخسي وعلاء الدين البخاري في الكشف ولم يحكوا فيه خلافاً، فعلى هذا بين الصلاة والحج فرق على قول محمد فإنه يقول فيها إذا بطل وصفها بطل أصلها ولم ينقل عنه في الحج في ذلك لما أن باب الحج أوسع فلهذا يمضي في فساده كما يمضي في صحيحه . وأشار المصنف بجريان النيابة في الحج عند العجز في الفرض ومطلقاً في النفل أن أصل الحج يقع للأمر لحديث الخثعمية عميس من المهاجرات وهو أنها قالت: يا رسول الله إن فريضة الله في الحج على عباده أدركت أبي شيخاً كبيراً لا يثبت على الراحلة أفأحج عنه ؟ قال : نعم. متفق عليه. فقد أطلق كونه عنه وقولهما أفأحج عنه فيه روايتان فتح الهمزة وضم الحاء أي أنا أحرم عنه بنفسي وأؤدي الأفعال وهذا هو المشهور من الرواية. وروي بضم الهمزة وكسر الحاء أي آمر أحد يحج عنه . ذكره ره الهندي في شرح المغني وهو ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا كما في الهداية، وظاهر المذهب كما في المبسوط وهو الصحيح كما في كثير من الكتب. وذهب عامة المتأخرين كما في الكشف إلى أن الحج يقع عن المأمور وللآمر ثواب النفقة قالوا: وهو رواية عن محمد. وهو اختلاف لا ثمرة له لأنهم اتفقوا أن الفرض يسقط عن الآمر ولا يسقط عن المأمور وأنه لا أن بد من ينويه عن الأمر وهو دليل المذهب، وأنه يشترط أهلية النائب لصحة حتى لو أمر ذمياً لا يجوز وهو دليل الضعيف، ولم أر من صرح بالثمرة.
His statement: 'The condition of incapacity of the deputized person is for obligatory Hajj, not voluntary' because deputyship is permissible with ability in voluntary Hajj, since the purpose is reward. If he can leave it altogether, then he can bear the difficulty of spending a fortiori. He made it general, including the Hajj of Islam and the vowed Hajj. He indicated by it that if he commissioned for the Hajj of Islam or was sick then recovered, the description of being obligatory becomes invalid because the condition (incapacity) is lost, and the basic Hajj remains as voluntary for the principal, not invalid. This is stated by al-Usbijābī, al-Sarakhsī, and 'Alā' al-Dīn al-Bukhārī in al-Kashf, and they did not report any disagreement. Upon this, there is a difference between prayer and Hajj according to Muhammad's statement: he says in prayer that if its description becomes invalid, its essence becomes invalid, but this is not transmitted from him regarding Hajj because the chapter of Hajj is wider. Therefore, it proceeds in its invalid state as it proceeds in its valid state. The author indicated by the running of deputyship in Hajj at the time of incapacity in obligatory and absolutely in voluntary that the basic Hajj falls on the principal, based on the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, 'Umays, from the emigrants, who said: O Messenger of Allah, the obligation of Allah regarding Hajj on His servants has reached my father, an old man who cannot sit firmly on a mount. Should I perform Hajj on his behalf? He said: Yes. Agreed upon. He made it absolute, being on his behalf. And the phrase 'afahujju 'anhu' has two recitations: with fatha of the hamza and damm of the ha (meaning 'I will perform Hajj on his behalf') and this is the well-known narration. And it is also related with damm of the hamza and kasr of the ha (meaning 'order someone to perform Hajj on his behalf'). This was mentioned by Rah al-Hindī in Sharḥ al-Mughnī, and it is the apparent narration from our companions as in al-Hidāya, and the apparent madhhab as in al-Mabsūṭ, and it is the correct view as in many books. However, the majority of the later scholars, as in al-Kashf, hold that the Hajj falls on the deputy, and the principal gets the reward of the expenses. They say it is a narration from Muhammad. This is a difference without practical consequence, because they all agree that the obligation is lifted from the principal and not from the deputy, and that it is necessary that he intend it for the principal, which is the evidence of the madhhab, and that the eligibility of the deputy is a condition for validity, so that if he commissions a dhimmī, it is not valid, and this is the weak evidence. I have not seen anyone who stated the practical consequence.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage addresses two important issues. First, it distinguishes between obligatory and voluntary Hajj regarding the condition of incapacity: for obligatory Hajj, the principal must be perpetually incapacitated; for voluntary Hajj, deputyship is allowed even if the principal is capable, because one can voluntarily give reward to others. The author notes that if the principal recovers after commissioning for obligatory Hajj, the description of obligation lapses but the Hajj continues as a valid voluntary act for the principal, unlike prayer where invalidation of the description invalidates the whole act (according to Imam Muhammad). Second, it discusses the dispute over whom the actual Hajj falls upon—whether the principal (mā'mūr) or the deputy (ma'mūr). The well-known Hanafi position, based on the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, is that it falls on the principal. However, later scholars (like al-Kashf) hold it falls on the deputy, with the principal receiving reward for expenses. The author follows al-Hidāyah and al-Mabsūṭ in maintaining the principal is the one being replaced. He declares this difference to be without practical consequence because both sides agree that the obligation lifts from the principal and does not fall on the deputy, and that the deputy must intend to perform Hajj on behalf of the principal. He also notes the condition that the deputy must be a Muslim (ahlīyah), so commissioning a non-Muslim is invalid—a point he considers weak evidence.

Key Terms
حجة الإسلام (ḥijjat al-islām): The obligatory Hajj that is required once in a lifetime for every capable Muslim.
الحجة المنذورة (al-ḥijjat al-manḏūrah): A Hajj vowed as a nadhr (pledge) by a person, which becomes obligatory to fulfill.
الآمر (al-āmir): The principal who commissions someone to perform Hajj on his behalf.
المأمور (al-maʾmūr): The deputy who is commissioned to perform Hajj on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known Hanafi position, does the Hajj performed by a deputy fall upon the principal or the deputy?
A) The deputy, because he performs the actions.
B) The principal, because the deputy acts on his behalf.
C) Both equally share the reward.
D) It falls upon neither, only the expenses count.

Key Takeaway
The condition of incapacity for deputyship applies only to obligatory Hajj, and the intra-Hanafi dispute over whom the Hajj falls upon has no practical consequence for the discharge of the principal's obligation.

Condition of Incapacity for Deputation in Hajj; The Hajj Falls for the Principal
Explains the condition of incapacity for deputation in obligatory vs. optional Hajj, and the dispute over whether the Hajj falls for the principal or the deputy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of incapacity for deputation in obligatory vs. optional Hajj, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the Hajj falls for the principal or the deputy, including its practical consequence in oaths.

Core Idea
Deputation in obligatory Hajj requires the principal's incapacity; in optional, it does not. The Hajj falls for the principal.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author explains the crucial distinction between obligatory and optional Hajj regarding deputation. He also addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about who gets credit for the Hajj—the principal or the deputy. Understanding this will help you apply the correct ruling in practical cases and navigate apparent contradictions in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
State the condition of incapacity for deputation in obligatory Hajj versus optional Hajj. Note that for optional Hajj, the principal need not be incapable.
The condition is for the principal (manub), not the deputy.
2
Understand the effect of losing the condition
If the principal was incapable and then recovers, the obligatory description of the deputized Hajj becomes invalid, but the Hajj remains valid as nafl (supererogatory) for the principal.
This differs from prayer: according to Muhammad, loss of obligatory description invalidates the prayer.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah and its two possible readings (afahijju with different vowels). The well-known reading indicates the deputy performs the actions directly for the principal.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its dalala is also zanni due to the variant readings.
4
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
The earlier school (zahir al-riwayah) holds the Hajj falls for the principal; later scholars (e.g., Qadikhan) adopt a weak view attributing it to the deputy. Identify their proofs.
Both agree on the obligation falling from the principal and the need for the deputy's intention.
5
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply the dispute to oaths: if someone swears not to perform Hajj, according to the school he does not break his oath by performing Hajj as a deputy; according to the weak view he does, unless custom treats it as Hajj.
The author initially claims no consequence but then provides this example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرط عجز المنوب للحج الفرض لا للنفل ومن أحرم حج آمريه ضمن النفقة . حج المفروض عليه هو الحج راكباً فينصرف مطلق الأمر بالحج إليه، فإذا ماشياً فقد خالف فيضمن ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن شرط الإجزاء كون أكثر النفقة من مال الأمر، فإن أنفق الأكثر أو الكل من مال نفسه وفي المال المدفوع إليه وفاء بحجه رجع به فيه إذ قد يبتلى بالإنفاق من مال نفسه لبعث الحاجة ولا يكون المال حاضراً فيجوز ذلك كالوصي والوكيل يشتري لليتيم ويعطي الثمن من مال نفسه فإنه يرجع به في مال اليتيم ا هـ . وبهذا علم أن اشتراطهم أن تكون النفقة من مال الآمر للاحتراز عن التبرع لا مطلقاً. عنه وهو صحيح وهي أسماء حجة بنت قوله : (وإنما شرط عجز المنوب للحج الفرض لا النفل) لجواز الإبانة مع القدرة في حج النفل لأن المقصود منه الثواب فإذا كان له تركه أصلاً فله تحمل مشقة المال بالأولى. أطلقه فشمل حجة الإسلام والحجة المنذورة، وأشار به إلى أنه لو أحج الإسلام أو كان مريضاً ثم صح بطل وصف الفرضية لفقد شرطه وهو العجز وبقي أصل الحج تطوعاً للآمر لا أنه فاسد أصلاً صرح به الأسبيجابي والسرخسي وعلاء الدين البخاري في الكشف ولم يحكوا فيه خلافاً، فعلى هذا بين الصلاة والحج فرق على قول محمد فإنه يقول فيها إذا بطل وصفها بطل أصلها ولم ينقل عنه في الحج في ذلك لما أن باب الحج أوسع فلهذا يمضي في فساده كما يمضي في صحيحه . وأشار المصنف بجريان النيابة في الحج عند العجز في الفرض ومطلقاً في النفل أن أصل الحج يقع للأمر لحديث الخثعمية عميس من المهاجرات وهو أنها قالت: يا رسول الله إن فريضة الله في الحج على عباده أدركت أبي شيخاً كبيراً لا يثبت على الراحلة أفأحج عنه ؟ قال : نعم. متفق عليه. فقد أطلق كونه عنه وقولهما أفأحج عنه فيه روايتان فتح الهمزة وضم الحاء أي أنا أحرم عنه بنفسي وأؤدي الأفعال وهذا هو المشهور من الرواية. وروي بضم الهمزة وكسر الحاء أي آمر أحد يحج عنه . ذكره ره الهندي في شرح المغني وهو ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا كما في الهداية، وظاهر المذهب كما في المبسوط وهو الصحيح كما في كثير من الكتب. وذهب عامة المتأخرين كما في الكشف إلى أن الحج يقع عن المأمور وللآمر ثواب النفقة قالوا: وهو رواية عن محمد. وهو اختلاف لا ثمرة له لأنهم اتفقوا أن الفرض يسقط عن الآمر ولا يسقط عن المأمور وأنه لا أن بد من ينويه عن الأمر وهو دليل المذهب، وأنه يشترط أهلية النائب لصحة حتى لو أمر ذمياً لا يجوز وهو دليل الضعيف، ولم أر من صرح بالثمرة. وقد يقال أن الأفعال ذلك قبيل باب الإحرام فراجعه قوله (وهو دليل الضعيف) في حكمه عليه بالضعف شيء إذ قال في الفتح : إن عليه جمعاً من المتأخرين منهم صدر الإسلام والأسبيجابي وقاضيخان حتى نسب شيخ الإسلام هذا لأصحابنا قال في النهر وفي العناية وإليه مال عامة المتأخرين اهـ. وما عزاه إلى ما ذكره في شرح الجامع الصغير حيث قال : وهو أقرب إلى الفقه لكن صحح في فتاواه قاضيخان هو إنها تظهر فيمن حلف أن لا يحج فعلى المذهب إذا حج عن غيره لا يحنث، وعلى الضعيف يحنث إلا أن يقال إن العرف أنه قد حج وإن وقع عن غيره فيحنث اتفاقاً.
The condition of incapacity of the deputy is for obligatory Hajj, not for optional. And whoever performs Ihram for Hajj being ordered by two persons guarantees the expenses. The obligated Hajj is for the one riding, so the absolute command of Hajj applies to him. If he goes walking, he has opposed [the command] and thus guarantees. (End of quote). In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the condition for sufficiency is that most of the expenses are from the property of the principal. If he spends most or all from his own property, and the property given to him suffices for his Hajj, he may reclaim it from it, because he may be forced to spend from his own property due to the need arising and the money not being present, so that is permissible just as a guardian or agent buys for an orphan and pays the price from his own property, then he reclaims from the orphan's property. (End of quote). By this it is known that their stipulation that the expenses be from the principal's property is to avoid gratuitousness, not absolutely. [Text unclear] His statement: (The condition of incapacity of the deputy is for obligatory Hajj, not for optional) is due to the permissibility of appointment despite capability in optional Hajj because the purpose is reward; if he may abandon it entirely, then bearing the hardship of wealth is more appropriate. He made it absolute, so it includes Hajj al-Islam and vowed Hajj. And he indicated by it that if he performed Hajj al-Islam or was sick and then recovered, the description of obligation becomes invalid due to loss of its condition, which is incapacity, and the original Hajj remains as supererogatory for the principal, not that it is invalid originally. This was stated by al-Isbijabi, al-Sarakhsi, and 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari in al-Kashf, and they did not narrate any disagreement about it. Based on this, there is a difference between prayer and Hajj according to the statement of Muhammad, for he says regarding it: if its description becomes invalid, its origin becomes invalid, and it is not reported from him about Hajj in that regard because the chapter of Hajj is broader, so it proceeds in its invalidity as it proceeds in its validity. And the author indicated by the operation of deputyship in Hajj upon incapacity in obligatory and absolutely in optional that the original Hajj falls for the principal, due to the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah 'Umays from the Muhajirat: she said: O Messenger of Allah, the obligation of Allah regarding Hajj upon His servants has reached my father, an old man who cannot stay on the mount. May I perform Hajj on his behalf? He said: Yes. [Agreed upon]. He made it absolute as being on his behalf. And her statement 'Afahijju 'anhu' has two narrations: with fath of hamzah and damm of ha meaning I myself perform Ihram on his behalf and perform the actions, and this is the well-known narration. And it is narrated with damm of hamzah and kasr of ha meaning I command someone to perform Hajj on his behalf. This was mentioned by [Shah 'Abd al-Haqq] al-Hindi in his commentary on al-Mughni, and it is the apparent narration from our companions as in al-Hidayah, and the apparent school as in al-Mabsut, and it is the correct one as in many books. And the generality of the later scholars, as in al-Kashf, held that the Hajj falls for the deputy and the principal has the reward of the expenses. They said: it is a narration from Muhammad. This is a difference without practical consequence, as they agree that the obligation falls from the principal and does not fall from the deputy, and that he must intend it for the principal - and that is the proof of the school - and that eligibility of the deputy is required for validity, so that if he orders a dhimmi it is not permissible - and that is the proof of the weak view. And I have not seen anyone who states the practical consequence. It may be said that the actions... that chapter of Ihram, so refer to it. His statement (and that is the proof of the weak view) regarding his judgment that it is weak: there is something, for he said in al-Fath: A group of later scholars followed it, including Sadr al-Islam, al-Isbijabi, and Qadikhan, until Shaykh al-Islam attributed this to our companions. He said in al-Nahr and al-'Inayah: and the generality of the later scholars inclined to it. (End) And what he attributed to what he mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir where he said: It is closer to fiqh, but he corrected in his fatwas Qadikhan... It appears in the one who swore not to perform Hajj: according to the school, if he performs Hajj on behalf of another, he does not break his oath; according to the weak view, he breaks his oath, unless it is said that customarily he has performed Hajj, and even if it falls for another, he breaks his oath by agreement.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the condition of incapacity for deputation in Hajj. The author first states the rule: deputation in obligatory Hajj requires the principal to be incapable (unable to perform Hajj himself due to old age, illness, etc.), whereas in optional Hajj, even a capable person may appoint a deputy. This is because optional Hajj can be abandoned entirely, so bearing the expense of a deputy is easier. The passage then discusses that if a person was incapable and then recovered, the obligatory nature of the deputized Hajj becomes invalid, but the original Hajj remains as a supererogatory act for the principal, not invalid. The author distinguishes between prayer and Hajj: according to Imam Muhammad, if the obligatory description of prayer is lost, the prayer itself becomes invalid, but for Hajj, it remains valid as nafl because the rules of Hajj are broader. The proof is the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, where the Prophet allowed her to perform Hajj for her father. The passage then presents a dispute among Hanafi scholars: the earlier view (zahir al-riwayah) that the Hajj falls for the principal, and the later view (attributed to Muhammad) that it falls for the deputy, with the principal receiving reward. The author notes that this difference has no practical consequence because in both cases the obligation is lifted from the principal, the deputy must intend for the principal, and the deputy must be eligible. The weak view is discussed, and a practical example is given: if someone swore not to perform Hajj, according to the school he does not break his oath by performing Hajj for another, but according to the weak view he does, unless custom considers it as Hajj.

Key Terms
المنوب (al-manūb): The person on whose behalf Hajj is performed (the principal).
النائب (al-nā'ib): The person who performs Hajj on behalf of another (the deputy).
زاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative narrations from Imam Muhammad's six books (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).
الثمرة (al-thamarah): The practical consequence of a legal dispute; here, the effect on oath-breaking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs Hajj on behalf of another while capable himself, what is the ruling on the optional Hajj?
A) It is not permissible because deputation requires incapacity.
B) It is permissible because optional Hajj can be done by a deputy even if the principal is capable.
C) It is makruh.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Deputation in obligatory Hajj requires the principal's incapacity; in optional Hajj it does not. The Hajj falls for the principal according to the school, though a weak view attributes it to the deputy, with a practical consequence in oaths.

Hajj for Two Orderers: Nafl for Deputy, Guarantee Required
Explains the ruling on dual appointment and guarantee of expenses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a deputy is ordered by two people to perform Hajj and explain the reasoning for the guarantee of expenses.

Core Idea
When two orderers appoint one deputy, the Hajj falls for the deputy himself as nafl and he must repay both expenses.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a person is asked by two individuals to perform Hajj on their behalf. Can he do one Hajj for both? The Hanafi school rules that he cannot, because each orderer demanded exclusive dedication. Consequently, his Hajj becomes a supererogatory act for himself, and he must return the expenses to both. The passage also refines the reasoning behind this ruling, drawing on commentaries to clarify the legal logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine the ruling when a deputy is appointed by two orderers. The text states that the Hajj falls for the deputy himself (nafl) and he must guarantee the expenses (repay). Confirm the hukm and the consequence.
This is the settled Hanafi position.
2
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
Why does the Hajj fall for the deputy? Because each orderer required that the expenses be used exclusively for him. The deputy cannot prioritize one over the other, so his performance cannot be validly dedicated to either. Thus the Hajj is his own nafl act.
The reasoning is based on the condition of exclusivity and the incapability of specification.
3
Analyze the commentary's refinement
The author critiques the earlier phrasing in al-Hidayah. Examine how commentators like Ibn Kamal Pasha improved the argument, clarifying that the 'commanded Hajj' (al-hajj with definite article for covenant) must be for the orderer, and if the deputy fails, he is liable.
This step deepens understanding of the legal reasoning and shows how Hanafi scholars refined their own texts.
4
Distinguish temporal stages
Note that the deputy's capacity to change his intention changes over time. Before starting the actions (e.g., one circuit), he can still assign the Hajj to one orderer. After beginning, it becomes fixed for himself. This is based on the principle that actions cannot be unspecified.
This nuance is important for practical application.
5
Apply to a relevant scenario
Using the above principles, test a new case: a deputy performs Hajj for one orderer but without specification. Determine the ruling before and after starting actions.
Application reinforces the legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن حج عن آمريه ضمن النفقة لأن كل واحد منهما أمره بأن يخلص النفقة له من غير اشتراك ولا يمكنه إيقاعه عن أحدهما لعدم الأولوية فيقع عن المأمور نفلاً، ولا يجزئه عن الأمر لا الأول فاعتراض بعضهم منشؤه عدم المراجعة قوله لأن كل واحد منهما أمره الخ) عدل عن قول الهداية فهي عن الحاج ويضمن النفقة لأن الحج يقع عن حتى يخرج الحاج عن حجة الإسلام، وكل واحد منهما أمره أن يخلص الحج له الخ لما قال في يخرج» غاية لقوله فهي عن الحاج نفلاً. وهذا أولى ما رأيت فتدبره اهـ . قلت : وهذا أيضاً لا يخفى بعده وقد خطر لي جواب عن النسخة الأولى أظهر مما في النهاية بأن تجعل «ال» في «الحج» للعهد أي لأن الحج المأمور به ما يقع عن الآمر ، وقوله حتى لا يخرج تفريع عليه تأمل. ثم رأيت جوابي بعينه أجاب به العلامة ابن كمال باشا في شرحه على الهداية قوله فيقع عن المأمور تثلا هذا في النهر، والذي في شرح الباقاني أنه يخرج بها عن حجة الإسلام لكن قال في غاية البيان: إنه يقع الأمر من وجه بدليل أن الحاج لا يخرج عن حجة الإسلام ورأيت في الفتح ما يفيد ما ذكره الباقاني فإنه في الفتح ذكر صور الإبهام الأربعة الآتي ذكرها ثم قال : ومبنى الأجوبة على أنه إذا وقع عن نفس المأمور لا يتحول بعد ذلك إلى الآمر وأنه بعد ما صرف نفقة الآمر إلى نفسه ذاهباً إلى الوجه الذي أخذ النفقة له لا ينصرف الإحرام إلى نفسه إلا إذا تحققت المخالفة أو عجز شرعاً عن التعيين اهـ. ولا شك في أنه إذا أحرم عنهما تحققت المخالفة وعجز شرعاً عن التعيين فيقع الحج عن : وذكر في الفتح أيضاً بعد ذلك فيما لو أحرم عن أحدهما غير عين أن المخالفة. لم تتحقق بمجرد الإحرام ولا يمكن أن يصير للمأمور لأنه نص على إخراجها عن نفسه يجعلها لأحدهما فلا ينصرف إليه إلا إذا وجد أحد الأمرين اللذين ذكرناهما أي من تحقق المخالفة أو العجز عن التعيين، ولم يتحقق ذلك ما لم يشرع في الأعمال ولو شوطاً لأن الأعمال لا تقع لغير معين فتقع عنه وليس في وسعه أن يحولها إلى غيره وإنما جعل الشرع له ذلك في الثواب اهـ ومقتضاه أنه بعد شروعه في الأعمال تحققت المخالفة وامتنع تحويلها لغيره وبطل إخراجها عن نفسه، وإذا بطل إخراجها عن نفسه تقع عن فرضه لأن الفرض يصح بمطلق النية عندنا. وقد ذكر في الفتح أيضاً لو أمره بالحج فقرن معه عمرة لنفسه لا يجوز ويضمن اتفاقاً ثم قال: ولا يقع عن حجة الإسلام عن نفسه لأن
