الحجة نفسه .
His statement: (And whoever performs Hajj for two orderers guarantees the expenses, because each one of them ordered him to dedicate the expenses to him without sharing, and he cannot perform it for one of them due to lack of priority, so it falls for the deputy as nafl, and it does not suffice for either of the orderers. The objection of some arises from lack of review.) He deviated from the statement of al-Hidayah: 'so it is for the Hajj pilgrim and he guarantees the expenses because the Hajj falls for him until the pilgrim exits from Hajj al-Islam.' And each one of them ordered him to dedicate the Hajj to him. Because what was said in al-'Inayah: The commentators went that the evidence does not correspond to the conclusion. He said then the author of al-Nihayah said: But this reasoning is reasoning for a ruling not mentioned, and the appreciation of speech is: he guarantees the expenses because he opposed them, and he does not guarantee the expenses only if he agrees, because the Hajj... . He said in al-Sa'diyyah: There is no indication for this appreciation, and therefore he said in al-Nahr: I have not seen anyone more eloquent than them about the target, but I saw in an old reliable copy that the Hajj falls for the orderer with 'la' negative, and it is not a reasoning for the issue. And his statement 'until he does not exit' is a limit for his statement 'so it is for the Hajj pilgrim as nafl'. This is the best I have seen, so ponder it. (End) I say: This also is not free from remoteness, and a clearer answer occurred to me regarding the first version than in al-Nihayah: by making the definite article 'al' in 'al-hajj' for the covenant, i.e., because the commanded Hajj is that which falls for the orderer, and his statement 'until he does not exit' is a branch of it. Then I saw the same answer given by the learned Ibn Kamal Pasha in his commentary on al-Hidayah. His statement: it falls for the deputy; this appears in al-Nahr. And what is in Sharh al-Baqani that he exits thereby from Hajj al-Islam, but he said in Ghayat al-Bayan: It falls for the orderer from one aspect, as evidence that the pilgrim does not exit from Hajj al-Islam. And I saw in al-Fath what supports what al-Baqani mentioned, for in al-Fath he mentioned the four images of ambiguity mentioned later, then said: The basis of the answers is that if it falls for the deputy himself, it does not transfer thereafter to the orderer, and that after he spent the orderer's expenses on himself going to the place for which he took the expenses, his Ihram does not refer to himself unless opposition is actualized or he is legally incapable of specification. (End) There is no doubt that if he performed Ihram for them both, opposition is actualized and he is legally incapable of specification, so the Hajj falls for... And he mentioned in al-Fath also after that regarding if he performed Ihram for one of them without specification, opposition is not actualized by mere Ihram, and it cannot become for the deputy because he has specified its removal from himself and directed it to one of them, so it does not refer to him unless one of the two things we mentioned is found: actual opposition or incapacity of specification. And this is not actualized until he begins the actions, even one circuit, because actions are not performed for unspecified [person], so they fall for him and it is not within his power to transfer them to another; rather, the Lawgiver made that for him regarding reward. (End) Its implication is that after he begins the actions, opposition is actualized and it is prevented from being transferred to another, and his removal from himself becomes invalid. And if his removal from himself becomes invalid, it falls for his obligatory Hajj because obligation is valid with absolute intention according to us. And it is mentioned in al-Fath also: if he ordered him to perform Hajj and he combined with it Umrah for himself, it is not permissible and he guarantees by agreement. Then he said: It does not fall for Hajj al-Islam for himself because the least that falls is with absolute intention, and he has diverted it from himself in intention. And there is a consideration in it. (End) His statement 'and there is a consideration in it' means: because of what he presented: if opposition is actualized or he is legally incapable of specification, it falls for himself. There is no doubt that if he combined, opposition is actualized, so the Hajj falls for himself.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a ruling regarding a person appointed by two individuals to perform Hajj on their behalf. The author first states the ruling: if two persons (orderers) ask one man to perform Hajj for each of them, the deputy cannot perform it for both, as each ordered that the expenses be dedicated exclusively to him. Since the deputy cannot give priority to one over the other, his Hajj falls for himself as a nafl (supererogatory) act, and he must guarantee (i.e., repay) the expenses to both orderers. The author then notes a deviation from the phrasing in al-Hidayah, which said 'the Hajj falls for the pilgrim' (i.e., the deputy). Various commentators such as the author of al-'Inayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Sa'diyyah discuss the correct interpretation. The preferred understanding is that the phrase 'until he does not exit from Hajj al-Islam' indicates that the deputy's Hajj is nafl for himself, not fulfilling the orderers' obligations. The author then provides his own analysis: the definite article 'al' in 'al-hajj' refers to the specific Hajj commanded, which should be for the orderer. The author also discusses cases of ambiguity: if the deputy performs Ihram for both at once, opposition is actualized and the Hajj falls for himself. If he performs Ihram for one without specification, opposition is not actualized until he begins the actions (e.g., one circuit). Before that, he can change his intention. After starting actions, it falls for himself. The passage concludes with a related case: if the deputy combines Hajj with Umrah for himself, it is impermissible and he guarantees, but there is a difference of opinion whether it falls for his own obligatory Hajj or not. The author supports the view that if he has opposed, it falls for himself.

Key Terms
آمريه (āmirīhi): The two persons who ordered the deputy to perform Hajj for them.
ضمان النفقة (ḍamān al-nafaqah): Liability to repay the expenses given by the orderers because the deputy failed to perform Hajj for them.
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specification of the person on whose behalf the Hajj is intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if two persons order one deputy to perform Hajj for each, and the deputy performs Hajj once intending both?
A) The Hajj suffices for both orderers.
B) The Hajj falls for the deputy as nafl, and he must repay the expenses to both.
C) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The deputy can decide which orderer to credit the Hajj to.

Key Takeaway
A deputy appointed by two cannot perform a single Hajj for both; his Hajj is nafl for himself, and he must repay the expenses.

Agent's Liability When Performing Qiran Instead of Ifrad: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's liability for expenses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when an agent becomes liable for expenses (mukhalif) and identify the practical difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Deviation in type (jins) from the command makes the agent liable; the Sahibayn disagree.

In proxy Hajj, the agent must follow the principal's instructions precisely. A key intra-Hanafi disagreement arises when the agent performs qiran (combined Hajj and Umrah) instead of the commanded ifrad (separate rites). Is this a fundamental deviation that triggers liability for expenses? This lesson unpacks the arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The agent is commanded to perform ifrad of Hajj or Umrah alone. Instead, he performs qiran (both together). The question: is he non-compliant (mukhalif) and liable for expenses?
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Hanifa, the agent is liable because he changed the type (jins) of the ritual, analogous to an agent authorized to sell for dirhams who sells for dinars.
The text says: 'فهو ضامن للنفقة عنده' – he is liable for expenses according to him.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the agent is not liable. The text says 'خلافاً لهما' – contrary to them.
Their reasoning is not given, but impliedly they view qiran as still fulfilling the command in essence.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response via qiyas
The text likens the case to a sale agent: if commanded to sell for 1000 dirhams but sells for 1000 dinars, he violates the mandate. Similarly, ifrad and qiran differ in type (jins), not just value.
This analogy grounds Abu Hanifa's ruling in a clear legal principle: changing the type of the act constitutes mukhalafa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if agent performs qiran after being commanded ifrad, Abu Hanifa says the principal's Hajj is not valid and agent bears expenses; Sahibayn say the principal's Hajj may be valid and expenses not required.
This affects whether the agent must repeat the Hajj at his own cost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الحج : حج نفسه. عن حجة الإسلام ويضمن النفقة إن أنفق من مالهما لأنه صرف نفقة الأمر إلى أطلق في الأمرين فشمل الأبوين وسيأتي إخراجهما، وقيد بالأمر بهما لأنه لو أحرم عنهما بغير أمرهما فله أن يجعله عن أحدهما لأنه متبرع بجعل ثواب عمله لأحدهما أولهما فبقي على خياره بعد وقوعه سبباً لثوابه وأشار بالضمان إلى أنه لا يمكنه بأن يجعله عن أحدهما بعد ذلك، وقيد بكونه أحرم عنهما معاً لأنه لو أحرم عن أحدهما غير عين فالأمر موقوف، فإن عين أحدهما قبل الطواف والوقوف انصرف إليه وإلا انصرف إلى نفسه، ولا يكون مخالفاً بمجرد الإحرام المذكور لأن كلا أمره بحجة وأحدهما صالح لكل منهما صادق عليه ولا منافاة بين العام والخاص، ولا يمكن أن يصير للمأمور لأنه نص على إخراجها عن نفسه بجعلها لأحد الآمرين فلا ينصرف إليه إلا إذا وجد أحد الأمرين اللذين ذكرناهما ولم يتحقق بعد، فإذا شرع في الأعمال قبل التعيين تعينت له لأن الأعمال لا تقع لغير معين ثم ليس في وسعه أن يحولها إلى غيره وإنما جعل له الشرع ذلك إلى الثواب، ولولا الشرع لم يحكم به في الثواب أيضاً. ولو أحرم بحجة من غير تعيين فإنه يصح التعيين بعده لأحدهما بالأولى، وذكر في الكافي أنه ينبغي أن يكون مجمعاً عليه لعدم المخالفة. ولو أحرم مبهماً من غير تعيين ما أحرم به لآمر معين فإنه يجوز بلا خلاف وهو أظهر من الكل فصور الإبهام أربعة : في واحدة يكون مسألة الكتاب منطوقاً. وفي الثلاثة لا يكون مخالفاً أن يكون الإبهام إما في الأمر أو في النسك أو فيهما، ولو أهل المأمور بالحج بحجتين أحداهما عن نفسه والأخرى عن الأمر ثم رفض التي أهل بها عن نفسه تكون الباقية عن الآمر كأنه أهل بها وحدها. وأشار المصنف إلى أن المأمور في كل موضع يصير مخالفاً فإنه يضمن النفقة، فمنها ما إذا أمره بالإفراد بحجة أو عمرة فقرن فهو ضامن للنفقة عنده خلافاً لهما، ومنها ما إذا أمره بالحب فاعتمر ثم حج من مكة لأنه مأمور بحج ميقاتي وما أتى به مكي بخلاف ما إذا أمره بالعمرة فاعتمر ثم حج عن نفسه لم يكن مخالفاً والنفقة في مدة إقامته للحج في ماله لأنه أقام في منفعة نفسه بخلاف ما إذا حج أولاً ثم اعتمر للآمر فإنه يكون مخالفاً لأنه جعل المسافة للحج وأنه لم يؤمر به وإن كانت الحجة أفضل من العمرة لأنه خلاف من حيث الجنس كالوكيل بالبيع بألف درهم إذا باع بألف دينار. كذا في المحيط . وفي فتح القدير والحاج عن غيره إن شاء قال لبيك عن فلان وإن شاء اكتفى بالنية عنه، وليس للمأمور أن يأمر غيره بما أمر به عن الآمر وإن مرض في الطريق إلا أن يكون وقت الدفع قيل له اصنع ما شئت، فحينئذ له أن يأمر غيره به وإن كان صحيحاً، فلو أحج رجلاً فحج ثم أقام بمكة جاز لأن الفرض صار مؤدى والأفضل أن يحج ثم يعود إلى أهله ثم اعلم أن النفقة ما يكفيه لذهابه وإيابه وأنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون المحجوج عنه حياً أو ميتاً. وعامة النسخ هنا محرفة والصواب هذه قوله (فصور الإبهام أربعة) وهي أن يهل بحجة عنهما أو عن أحدهما على الإبهام أو بحجة من غير تعيين للمحجوج عنه أو يحرم عن أحدهما يعينه بلا تعيين لما أحرم : كذا به . في الفتح. فالثالثة الإبهام فيها عكس الرابعة وفي الحقيقة لا إبهام في الصورة الثالثة قوله (وفي الثالثة لا يكون مخالفاً كذا في أغلب النسخ ، وفي بعضها بزيادة قوله وهي أن يكون الإبهام إما في الأمر أو في النسك أو فيهما، والصواب إسقاطها إذ ليس من الصور ما يكون الإبهام فيها في النسك والآمر قوله لأنه مأمور بحج ميقاتي الخ يفهم منه أنه لو خرج إلى الميقات وأحرم منه لكن يرد عليه أنه لما اعتمر جعل سفره للعمرة ولم يؤمر به فيكون مخالفاً كما يفيده قوله الآتي «لأنه جعل المسافة الخ) وقدمنا الكلام على المسألة قبيل باب الإحرام فراجعه، وقدمنا شيئاً من ذلك قريباً في هذا الباب وفي اللباب الثالث عشر أي من الشروط عدم المخالفة فلو أمره بالإفراد أو العمرة فقرن أو تمتع ولو للميت لم يقع حجه عن الآمر ويضمن النفقة. وقال في شرحه: ولعل أنه مأمور بتجريد السفر للحج عن الميت فإنه المفروض عليه وينصرف مطلق الأمر إليه إلا أنه يشكل إذا أمره بإفراد العمرة ثم إتيان الحج بعده أو صرح بالتمتع في سفره أو تفويض الأمر إليه اهـ قوله (بخلاف ما إذا حج (أولا) مرتبط بقوله لم يكن مخالفاً قوله لأنه لو لم يظهر في الآخرة) تعليل البحر الرائق ج٣/ ٨٥
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Hajj: Hajj for oneself. Regarding the Hajj of Islam, and he guarantees the expenses if he spends from the wealth of both because he spent the expenses of the command absolutely regarding the two commands, so it includes the parents, and its exclusion will come later. He restricted it to being commanded by them because if he assumes ihram for them without their command, he may make it for one of them because he is voluntarily giving the reward of his action to one of them or both, so he retains his choice after it occurs as a means to its reward. He indicated by the guarantee that he cannot make it for one of them after that. He restricted it to assuming ihram for both together because if he assumes ihram for one unspecified, the matter is suspended. If he specifies one before tawaf and standing, it is diverted to him, otherwise it is diverted to himself. He is not non-compliant merely by the mentioned ihram because each commanded him with a hajj, and one hajj is suitable for each, truthful for him, and there is no conflict between the general and the specific. It cannot become for the commanded because he explicitly excluded it from himself by making it for one of the commanders, so it is not diverted to him unless one of the two conditions we mentioned occurs and it has not yet been realized. If he commences the actions before specification, it becomes specified for him because actions cannot occur for an unspecified person. Then it is not within his power to transfer it to another; the Lawgiver only granted him that regarding the reward. If not for the Law, it would not be ruled regarding the reward either. If he assumes ihram for hajj without specification, then specification after for one of them is more appropriate. It is mentioned in al-Kafi that it should be a matter of consensus due to no non-compliance. If he assumes ihram ambiguously without specifying what he assumes ihram for for a specified commander, then it is permissible without dispute and it is more obvious than all. So the forms of ambiguity are four: in one it is the subject of the book explicitly. In three he is not non-compliant: either the ambiguity is in the command, or in the ritual, or in both. If the commanded person enters ihram for two hajj, one for himself and one for the commander, then cancels the one he entered for himself, the remaining one is for the commander as if he entered ihram for it alone. The author indicated that wherever the commanded person becomes non-compliant, he guarantees the expenses. Among them: if he commands him to perform ifrad of hajj or umrah and he performs qiran, then he is guarantor of expenses according to him, contrary to the two. Among them: if he commands him to perform hajj (?) and he performs umrah then hajj from Makkah because he is commanded with a miqati hajj and he performed a Makkan one. Contrary to if he commands him with umrah and he performs umrah then hajj for himself, he is not non-compliant and the expenses during his stay for hajj are from his own wealth because he stayed for his own benefit. Contrary to if he performs hajj first then umrah for the commander, then he is non-compliant because he made the distance for hajj and he was not commanded with it even if hajj is superior to umrah because it is a difference in type, like an agent authorized to sell for one thousand dirhams if he sells for one thousand dinars. This is in al-Muhit. In Fath al-Qadir: the one performing hajj for another may say 'Labbayk for so-and-so' or suffice with intention for him. The commanded person may not command another for what he was commanded for the commander even if he falls ill on the way unless it is the time of departure, it is said to him 'do as you wish', then he may command another for it even if he is healthy. If he appoints a man to perform hajj and he performs hajj then stays in Makkah, it is permitted because the obligation has been fulfilled, but the best is to perform hajj then return to his family. Then know that the expenses are what suffice for his going and returning, and the one for whom hajj is performed is either alive or dead. Most copies here are corrupted; the correct is this: his saying (the forms of ambiguity are four): he assumes ihram for hajj for both of them or for one of them ambiguously, or for hajj without specifying the person for whom, or he assumes ihram for one of them by specification without specifying what he assumes ihram for: as in al-Fath. The third ambiguity is the opposite of the fourth and in reality there is no ambiguity in the third image. His saying (in the third he is not non-compliant) as in most copies, and in some with addition: the ambiguity is either in the command, or in the ritual, or in both. The correct is to drop it since there is no image where the ambiguity is in both the ritual and the commander. His saying (because he is commanded with a miqati hajj) indicates that if he goes out to the miqat and assumes ihram from it, but it is objected that when he performed umrah he made his journey for umrah and was not commanded with it so he becomes non-compliant as indicated by his later saying (because he made the distance...). We have already discussed the issue before the chapter of Ihram, so refer to it. We have already presented some of that recently in this chapter. In al-Lubab: the thirteenth condition is the absence of non-compliance. If he commands him with ifrad of hajj or umrah and he performs qiran or tamattu', even for a deceased person, his hajj does not fall for the commander and he guarantees the expenses. He said in his commentary: Perhaps he is commanded to make the journey exclusively for the deceased's hajj for it is obligatory upon him, and the absolute command is directed to that. However, there is difficulty if he commands him with ifrad of umrah then coming with hajj after it, or clearly states tamattu' in his journey, or delegates the matter to him. The end. His saying (contrary to if he performs hajj (first)) is linked to his saying 'he is not non-compliant'. He says (because if it does not appear in the Hereafter) justification - Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 3 p. 85.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings for an agent (ma'mur) who is commanded to perform Hajj on behalf of another (al-hajj an al-ghayr). The commentator, Imam Ibn Nujaym, clarifies the principles governing the agent's actions, especially when commanded by two persons, when there is ambiguity in intention, and when the agent deviates from the command. The text begins by discussing a scenario where two persons command the agent to perform Hajj for them. The agent cannot perform Hajj for both simultaneously. If he spends from his own wealth for both, he must guarantee the expenses because he wasted the money. However, if he assumes ihram without their command, he retains the right to designate one of them after the fact as the beneficiary of the reward, but the Hajj itself remains valid for himself. If he assumes ihram for both together by command, he is not considered non-compliant initially because he is fulfilling each command; but he must eventually specify one performance for one commander and compensate the other. The commentary then discusses cases of ambiguity (ibham) in the agent's intention. Four forms are identified: (1) ambiguity in the commander (he assumes ihram for both without specifying), (2) ambiguity in the ritual (he assumes ihram for hajj or umrah without specifying), (3) ambiguity in both, and (4) no ambiguity. The ruling is that if the commander is specified but the ritual is ambiguous, it is permissible without dispute. The main legal issue is the concept of 'mukhalafa' (non-compliance). When the agent acts contrary to the command, he becomes a guarantor (damin) of the expenses (nafaqa) and his Hajj does not count for the commander. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears: according to Imam Abu Hanifa (اﻋﻪ), if the agent is commanded to perform ifrad (separate Hajj or Umrah) and instead performs qiran (combined), he is liable for expenses. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold a different view. The text also discusses other cases, such as being commanded to perform Hajj from the miqat (miqati) but performing Umrah first from Makkah, which makes him non-compliant. The commentary references al-Muhit, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Kafi. It also mentions that the agent cannot delegate to another unless given permission. Overall, this passage is an expansion probe, clarifying the conditions for the validity of Hajj by proxy and the consequences of violating the principal's instructions.

Key Terms
مخالف (mukhalif): In this text, a person who deviates from the command of the principal (the one who appointed him for Hajj) in a manner that invalidates the proxy and makes him liable for expenses.
نفقة (nafaqa): Expenses incurred by the agent for travel, accommodation, and other necessities during the Hajj journey, which he must guarantee (ضمن) if he becomes non-compliant.
إبهام (ibham): Ambiguity in the intention of the agent regarding whether he is performing Hajj for himself or another, or which ritual (hajj or umrah) he intends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an agent is commanded to perform ifrad of Hajj but instead performs qiran, what is the ruling regarding the expenses?
A) The agent does not guarantee expenses because the reward is still for the principal.
B) The agent guarantees the expenses because he is non-compliant.
C) The principal must pay additional expenses.
D) The expenses are shared equally.

Key Takeaway
The agent must follow the exact type of ritual commanded; deviation in type (jins) from ifrad to qiran makes him liable for expenses according to Imam Abu Hanifa, with the Sahibayn dissenting.

When Does the Hajj Appointee Become a Violator? The Four Forms of Ambiguity
Explains the four forms of ambiguity and when the ma'mur becomes a violator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four forms of ambiguity (ibham) in the command for Hajj on behalf of another and apply the Hanafi rule that changing the type of ritual (jins) makes the appointee a violator who must guarantee expenses.

Core Idea
Changing the type of Hajj (qiran instead of ifrad) is a violation in kind, triggering guarantee of expenses.

In Hajj on behalf of another, the appointee must follow the commander's specific instructions. Any deviation may make him a violator (mukhalif) liable for expenses. This lesson unpacks the four forms of ambiguity in the command and the key cases where violation occurs, drawing on the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and highlighting an important intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Forms of Ambiguity (Ibham)
The text states there are four forms: (1) ambiguity in the person, (2) ambiguity in the ritual, (3) ambiguity in both, (4) no ambiguity. Only the first is explicitly covered in the matn; the sharh clarifies that in the other three the appointee does not become a violator.
Ambiguity in the command means the appointee has discretion; violation only occurs when the command is clear and he acts contrary.
2
Understand When Violation Occurs
The appointee becomes a violator if he acts contrary to a clear command regarding the type of ritual (Hajj vs Umrah) or a specific condition (e.g., miqat vs Makkan). This triggers a guarantee of expenses (nafaqah).
3
Analyze the Qiran vs Ifrad Dispute
If commanded for ifrad (separate Hajj or Umrah) but performs qiran, Abu Hanifa rules he is a violator and must guarantee expenses, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. The text adopts Abu Hanifa's view.
The analogy given is an agent told to sell for dirhams who sells for dinars – a change in the type of consideration.
4
Apply the Rule to Other Cases
Other examples: (a) commanded for Hajj but performs Umrah first then Hajj from Makkah – violator; (b) commanded for Umrah, performs Umrah then Hajj for himself – not a violator; (c) performs Hajj first then Umrah for the commander – violator.
The key is whether the journey was used for a purpose not commanded.

Source Text

Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The passage opens by stating the ruling that appointing a specific person for Hajj on behalf of another is permissible without dispute. The author then discusses the four forms of ambiguity (ibham) in the command: (1) ambiguity in the person, (2) ambiguity in the ritual (Hajj or `Umrah or both), (3) ambiguity in both, (4) no ambiguity. Only the first form is covered in the matn (the base text), but the sharh clarifies that in the other three forms the appointee does not become a violator (mukhalif). The core legal principle: if the appointed person acts contrary to the commander's specification, he becomes a violator and must guarantee the expenses (nafaqah) he consumed. The passage provides several examples: (a) If commanded for ifrad (separate Hajj or `Umrah) but performs qiran, he is a violator according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. (b) If commanded for Hajj but performs `Umrah first and then Hajj from Makkah, he is a violator because he was commanded for Hajj from the miqat. (c) If commanded for `Umrah, performs `Umrah then Hajj for himself, he is not a violator. (d) If he performs Hajj first then `Umrah for the commander, he is a violator because he used the journey for Hajj, which he was not commanded, and this is a violation in kind analogous to an agent told to sell for dirhams selling for dinars. The text ends with a quote from al-Muhit. The editorial notes that follow discuss textual variants and clarify the forms of ambiguity.

Key Terms
مخالف (mukhalif): An appointed person who acts contrary to the specific command of the one who appointed him.
إبهام (ibham): Ambiguity in the command regarding the person, the ritual, or both.
نفقة (nafaqah): Expenses required for the journey, including provisions and transportation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is appointed to perform Hajj exclusively (ifrad) but instead performs qiran, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The Hajj is valid and the appointee is not a violator.
B) The Hajj is valid but the appointee becomes a violator and must guarantee expenses.
C) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The appointee may keep any surplus expenses.

Key Takeaway
The appointee must strictly follow the specified type of Hajj; changing the type (e.g., qiran instead of ifrad) makes him a violator who must repay expenses.

Surplus Expenses and Istihsan in Hajj on Behalf of Others
Ruling on surplus expenses and an istihsan exception for hiring out a camel in Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on surplus expenses for a Hajj deputy, identify the exception via istihsan, and apply the ruling to cases with wills and waqf.

Core Idea
Surplus expenses remain the owner's property unless explicitly gifted; necessity (istihsan) permits deviation to avoid hardship.

This lesson explores a key fiduciary rule in Hajj: the deputy does not own surplus expenses. Yet, when a specific camel is given for Hajj and the deputy hires it out to perform Hajj on foot, the Hanafi school allows this by istihsan. We'll unpack the reasoning and its limits, including how this applies to wills and waqf endowments.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling on surplus expenses
Identify that the deputy must return any surplus expenses to the owner unless the owner explicitly gives permission to keep it. This applies whether the principal is alive or dead, and whether the amount is specified or not.
The text emphasizes that the deputy does not own the surplus; it remains a trust (amanah).
2
Examine the exception: hiring out the camel
Consider the case where a testator gives a camel for Hajj riding, but the deputy hires it out, spends the hire on himself, and performs Hajj walking. This violates the command, but the scholars rule it valid by istihsan.
This exception deviates from the general rule (qiyas) due to necessity.
3
Follow the istihsan reasoning
Trace the logic: since the deputy could have sold the camel (own the corpus) and performed Hajj with the price, allowing him to own the usufruct via hire is more fitting. This prevents harm to the deceased, as the Hajj is valid and the camel is returned to the heirs.
The key phrase: 'لأنه لو لم يظهر في الآخرة أنه يملك ذلك يكون الكراء له والحج له' (if it did not appear that he owns that, the hire would be for him and the Hajj for him, harming the deceased).
4
Understand the tarjih (preference) mechanism
The authors of fatawa and al-Muhit correct this as the chosen view (al-mukhtar) despite the apparent violation. This illustrates how later Hanafi scholars weigh necessity against strict textual command.
Authority: 'وقال أصحاب الفتاوى : هو المختار' (the authors of fatawa said: it is the chosen).
5
Apply to other scenarios: specified amount and waqf
The text extends the same principle: whether the testator specifies an amount or not, and even in the case of a waqf with a fixed stipend, the deputy may not keep surplus; it must be returned to the heirs or waqf.
The example from al-Walwaliji shows the calculation when no amount is specified: the lesser of two adequate sums is taken.

فأنفق الكراء على نفسه في الطريق وحج ماشياً جاز عن الميت استحساناً وإن خالف أمره. وصححه في المحيط . وقال أصحاب الفتاوى : هو المختار لأنه لما ملك أن يملك رقبتها بالبيع ويحج بالثمن استحساناً . هو المختار فلأن يملك أن يملك منفعتها بالإجارة ويحج ببدل المنفعة كان أولى لأنه لو لم يظهر في الآخرة أنه يملك ذلك يكون الكراء له لأنه غاصب والحج له فيتضرر الميت ثم يرد البعير إلى ورثة الميت لأنه ملك المورث ا هـ . وهذه المسألة خرجت عن الأصل للضرورة فإن الأصل أن المأمور بالحج راكباً إذا حج ماشياً فإنه يكون مخالفاً وإن لم يعين الموصي قدراً فإنَّ الورثة يحجون عنه من الثلث بقدر الكفاية. ولهذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه : رجل مات وأوصى أن يحج عنه ولم يقدر فيه مالاً، فالوصي إن أعطى إلى رجل ليحج عنه في محمل احتاج إلى ألف ومائتين، وإن حج راكباً لا في محمل يكفيه الألف وكل ذلك يخرج من الثلث يجب أقلهما لأنه فالحاصل أن المأمور لا يكون مالكاً لما أخذه المتيقن ا هـ . هو بل يتصرف فيه على ملك المحجوج عنه حياً كان أو ميتاً، معيناً كان القدر أو غير معين، ولا يحل له الفضل إلا بالشرط المتقدم. سواء كان الفضل كثيراً أو يسيراً كيسير من صرح به في الفتاوى الظهيرية، وينبغي أن تكون كذلك الحجة المشروطة من جهة الواقف كما شرط سليمان باشا بوقفه بمصر قدراً معيناً لمن يحج عنه كل سنة فإنه يتبع شرطه، ولا يحل للمأمور ما فضل منه بل يجب رده إلى الوقف.
It is permissible to decrease? for a dead person. If he is alive, he gives him sufficient as stated. If he gives him excess over sufficiency, it is not permissible for the appointee to take the excess; rather he must return it to his owner, unless he said: 'I appoint you to gift the surplus from yourself and take it for yourself.' If he is on death, he says: 'The remainder from me is for you as a will.' And if he had willed that Hajj be performed for him and then died, then either he specified an amount or not. If he specified an amount, that amount is followed, even if it is not sufficient, as long as it comes from the third (thuluth) as the details will come soon in the chapter on wills. For this, al-Muhit says: A man died and left two sons and willed that Hajj be performed for him for three hundred, and left nine hundred. One son denied and the other acknowledged. Each took half the wealth. Then the acknowledging one paid one hundred fifty to perform Hajj for the deceased. Then the other acknowledged. If he performs Hajj by order of the judge, the acknowledging one takes seventy-five dirhams from the denying one, because the Hajj for the deceased is valid with one hundred fifty, and one hundred fifty remains as inheritance for them, so each gets half. If he performs Hajj without the judge's order, then he performs Hajj again with three hundred, because the Hajj for the deceased is not valid since he was commanded for three hundred. And with the specified amount, the appointee may not keep the surplus; rather he returns it to his heirs. For this they said: If he willed that his camel be given to a man to perform Hajj for him, and it was given to a man who hired it out, spent the hire on himself on the road, and performed Hajj walking, it is valid for the deceased by istihsan, even though he violated his command. Al-Muhit corrected it. The authors of fatawa said: it is the chosen view, because since he can own its corpus by sale and perform Hajj with the price by istihsan, then it is more fitting that he can own its usufruct by hire and perform Hajj with the substitute for the usufruct. Because if it does not appear in the end that he owns that, the hire would be for him as a usurper and the Hajj for him, harming the deceased, then he returns the camel to the heirs of the deceased. This issue is exceptional due to necessity; the original rule is that the appointee for Hajj riding, if he performs Hajj walking, is a violator. And if the testator did not specify an amount, the heirs perform Hajj for him from the third for sufficient expenses. For this, al-Walwaliji in his fatawa: A man died and willed that Hajj be performed for him without specifying a sum. The executor if he gives to a man to perform Hajj in a litter, needs 1200; if he performs Hajj riding without a litter, 1000 suffices; all that comes from the third; the lesser of the two is obligatory because... The conclusion: the appointee does not own what he took; rather he spends it on the property of the one on whose behalf Hajj is performed, whether alive or dead, whether the amount is specified or not. The surplus is not permissible for him except with the aforementioned condition, whether the surplus is large or small, as stated in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah. It should be likewise for a Hajj stipulated by a waqf, as Sulayman Pasha stipulated in his waqf in Egypt a specific amount for someone to perform Hajj for him every year; his condition is followed, and the appointee may not keep what is surplus; rather it must be returned to the waqf.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with expenses (nafaqah) in Hajj on behalf of another. It opens with a discussion about surplus: if the appointee receives more than sufficient expenses, he must return the excess, unless the commander explicitly authorized him to keep it as a gift. If the commander is dead and has willed the surplus to him, it is a bequest (wasiyyah). The text then presents a detailed case from al-Muhit: a man dies leaving 900 dirhams, willing that 300 be spent on his Hajj. His two sons inherit. One son acknowledges the will and pays 150 to a deputy, but the other son initially denies. The text explains the calculations if the judge orders payment or not, clarifying that the appointee cannot keep surplus. The next issue: if a testator gives a camel to a person to perform Hajj, but the person hires out the camel, uses the hire for himself, and performs Hajj on foot. By istihsan, this is valid for the deceased, although it violates the command (the appointee was supposed to ride). The scholars say this is the chosen view due to necessity, because the appointee could have sold the camel and performed Hajj with the price, so hiring it out is even more fitting. The passage concludes with the general principle: the appointee does not own the expenses; he acts as a trustee on the property of the deceased. Surplus must be returned if not explicitly given as a gift. This principle applies even to a waqf (religious endowment) where a specific sum is stipulated for Hajj annually; the deputy must return any surplus to the waqf.

Key Terms
فضل النفقة (fadl al-nafaqah): Surplus expenses given to the appointee beyond what is necessary for the journey.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference departing from strict analogy due to necessity.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest; after death, expenses and surplus follow the testator's directives within the third of wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator specifies a certain amount for Hajj but the actual journey costs less, who is entitled to the surplus?
A) The appointee, as a reward for his effort.
B) The testator's heirs, as the surplus is part of the estate.
C) The waqf if the testator had a waqf.
D) The charity (sadaqah).

Key Takeaway
The deputy for Hajj holds surplus expenses in trust; only explicit permission entitles him to keep any excess.

Ruling on Excess Payment to Hajj Proxy for Deceased
Ruling on giving more or less than sufficient for Hajj on behalf of deceased.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of returning surplus to the principal and identify the condition under which the proxy may keep it.

Core Idea
Surplus given to a Hajj proxy must be returned; it only becomes a gift if explicitly permitted.

This lesson addresses a practical question in Hajj on behalf of others: what happens if the principal gives more money than the proxy needs? The Hanafi ruling is clear—any extra remains the property of the principal unless he explicitly authorises it as a gift. We will examine the rule, the exception, and the distinction between living and deceased principals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and transaction
We have a principal (hiring or appointing a proxy for Hajj) and a proxy (al-ma'mur). The principal gives money for the journey.
The proxy is a trustee of the funds.
2
State the general rule regarding surplus
If the amount given exceeds what is sufficient for the journey, the surplus is not permissible for the proxy; he must return it to the principal.
This is wajib (obligatory).
3
Identify the exception and its condition
If the principal explicitly says, 'I appoint you to gift the surplus from yourself and take possession for yourself,' then the proxy may keep it as a gift.
The permission must be explicit; custom is not enough.
4
Distinguish between living and deceased cases
For a living principal, the explicit statement constitutes a gift (hibah). For a deceased person, a similar statement is a bequest (wasiyyah), which also allows the proxy to keep the surplus.
The bequest is subject to the one-third limit if there are other heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز النقص ميتاً، فإن كان حياً فإنه يعطيه بقدر ما يكفيه كما ذكرنا فإن أعطاه زائداً على كفايته فلا يحل للمأمور ما زاد بل يجب عليه رده إلى صاحبه إلا إذا قال وكلتك تهب الفضل من نفسك وتقبضه لنفسك، فإن كان على موت قال والباقي مني لك وصية
It is permissible to give less for a deceased person. If the person is alive, then he gives him what suffices him as we mentioned. If he gives him extra beyond his sufficiency, then what is extra is not permissible for the agent, rather he must return it to its owner, unless he said: 'I appoint you as my agent to gift the surplus from yourself and take possession for yourself.' If it is upon death, he says: 'And the remainder from me to you is a bequest.'
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage contains a basic ruling from the chapter of Hajj on behalf of others. It states that when someone hires or appoints a proxy for Hajj, the proxy is entitled to what is sufficient for the journey. If the principal gives extra, the proxy does not own the surplus—he must return it. An exception exists if the principal explicitly permits the proxy to take the surplus as a gift. In the case of a deceased person, such a statement constitutes a bequest. This ruling applies to both the living and the dead, with the condition that for a living person, the statement must be explicit about gifting.

Key Terms
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another.
الفضل (al-fadl): The surplus amount beyond the proxy's actual expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a proxy for Hajj and gives him 1000 dirhams, but the journey only costs 800, what must the proxy do with the remaining 200?
A) Keep it as a gift from the principal.
B) Return it to the principal or his heirs.
C) Spend it on charity on behalf of the principal.
D) Use it for his own next Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Surplus given to a Hajj proxy must be returned; it only becomes permissible to keep if the principal explicitly authorises it as a gift or bequest.

Binding Nature of a Specified Bequest for Hajj
Case study on will for Hajj with specified amount and heir dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a bequest for Hajj with a specified amount must be fulfilled exactly from the third of the estate, and determine the consequence of reduction without judicial authorization.

Core Idea
A bequest for Hajj with a specified amount is binding; reducing it without a judge's order invalidates the Hajj.

This passage from Al-Muhit presents a practical case illustrating the binding nature of a specified bequest for Hajj. It shows how the rules of evidence and inheritance interact when one heir acknowledges the bequest and the other denies it. We will analyze the conditions for a valid substitute Hajj and the distribution of the estate when the bequest is partially fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's instruction and its legal effect
The testator specified an amount of 300 dirhams for Hajj. In Hanafi law, a bequest with a specified amount is binding and must be followed exactly.
This applies even if the bequest comes out of the third of the estate.
2
Determine the bequest's priority from the estate
The third of the estate is 300 out of 900, so the bequest fits entirely within the third. The remaining 600 is inheritance for the two sons.
The bequest must be satisfied before inheritance is distributed.
3
Analyze the heirs' positions
One son acknowledges the bequest, the other denies. Each initially takes half of the entire estate (450 each), ignoring the bequest.
The acknowledging son is bound to fulfill the bequest from his share.
4
Apply the rule of judicial authorization
If the acknowledging son performs Hajj with only 150 dirhams without a judge's order, the Hajj is invalid and must be repeated with the full 300. If he does so by judge's order, the Hajj is valid with 150, and the remaining 150 of the bequest becomes inheritance.
The judge's order effectively allows a reduction if the actual cost is less, but only with judicial oversight.
5
Calculate the financial recovery between heirs
After a valid Hajj with 150, the remaining 150 of the bequest is split equally between the sons. Since the acknowledging son already spent 150, the judge recovers 75 from the denying son to equalize their shares.
Each son ends with 375 dirhams total.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان قد أوصى بأن يحج عنه ثم مات، فإما أن يعين قدراً أو لا، فإن عين قدراً اتبع ما عينه حتى لا عنه إذا كان يخرج من الثلث كما سيأتي تفصيله قريباً في مسألة الوصية، ولهذا قال في المحيط: رجل مات وترك ابنين وأوصى بأن يحج عنه بثلاثمائة وترك تسعمائة فأنكر أحدهما وأقر الآخر. وأخذ كل واحد منهما نصف المال، ثم إنَّ المقر دفع مائة وخمسين يحج بها عن الميت، ثم أقر الآخر إن أحج يأمر القاضي يأخذ المقر من الجاحد خمسة وسبعين درهماً لأنه جاز الحج عن الميت بمائة وخمسين وبقي مائة وخمسون ميراثاً لهما فيكون لكل واحد نصفه، وإن أحج بغير أمر القاضي فإنه يحج مرة أخرى بثلاثمائة لأنه لم يجز الحج عن الميت لأنه أمره بثلاثمائة
And if he had bequeathed that Hajj be performed on his behalf and then died, then either he specified an amount or not. If he specified an amount, what he specified is followed, even if [it is not carried out?] if it comes out of the third of the estate, as its detail will come soon in the issue of bequest. For this reason, it is said in Al-Muhit: A man died leaving two sons and bequeathed that Hajj be performed on his behalf for three hundred [dirhams], and left nine hundred. One son denied [the bequest] and the other acknowledged. Each took half the wealth. Then the acknowledging son paid one hundred fifty to perform Hajj for the deceased. Then the other acknowledged [the bequest?] if he performs Hajj by order of the judge, the judge takes from the acknowledging son for the denying son seventy-five dirhams, because the Hajj for the deceased is valid with one hundred fifty, and one hundred fifty remains as inheritance for both, so each gets half. If he performs Hajj without the judge's order, then he performs Hajj again with three hundred, because the Hajj for the deceased was not valid because he [the testator] ordered three hundred.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed case about a will for Hajj with a specified amount. The testator specified 300 dirhams, but his estate was 900. After each son took 450, the acknowledging son paid only 150 for the Hajj. If the judge orders, he can recover 75 from the acknowledging son for the denying son because the Hajj is valid with 150, and the remaining 150 of the bequest is split between them. If the son acted without judge's order, the Hajj is not valid and must be repeated with the full 300. This illustrates that the specified amount is binding and must be spent fully; any reduction without proper authorization invalidates the Hajj on behalf of the deceased.

Key Terms
الوصية بالحج (al-wasiyyah bi'l-hajj): A bequest instructing that Hajj be performed on behalf of the deceased after death.
المقر والجاحد (al-muqirr wa'l-jahid): The acknowledging heir (muqirr) and the denying heir (jahid) regarding the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example from Al-Muhit, why does the judge order the acknowledging heir to pay 75 dirhams to the denying heir?
A) Because the denying heir is poor and deserves charity.
B) Because the bequest was for 300, but only 150 was spent, leaving 150 as inheritance, half of which belongs to the denying heir.
C) Because the acknowledging heir cheated the denying heir.
D) Because the judge always splits contested bequests equally.

Key Takeaway
The specified amount in a bequest for Hajj is binding; if the full amount is not spent without judicial authorization, the Hajj must be repeated with the full amount.

Proxy Hajj Contravention and Istihsan
Istihsan ruling on proxy Hajj contravention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi istihsan ruling when a Hajj proxy rents out the provided camel and walks, and derive the underlying qiyas a priori reasoning.

Core Idea
Istihsan validates a proxy's contravening act if it achieves the deceased's Hajj more effectively, overriding qiyas.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced Hanafi ruling from Al-Muhit and Fatāwā: if a testator bequeaths a camel for proxy Hajj, but the agent rents it out, uses the rental income for expenses, and performs Hajj walking, the Hajj is valid by istihsan (juristic preference). At first glance, this seems to violate instructions, but deeper reasoning reveals a powerful legal principle: necessity and a qiyas a priori from selling to leasing. By the end, you will see how Hanafi jurists balance textual instructions with practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the apparent problem
Identify the case: a testator specifies a camel for a proxy to ride for Hajj. The proxy rents out the camel, uses the fee for himself, and walks. What is the apparent ruling (qiyas)?
Normally, the proxy must follow instructions; contravention makes him a usurper and the Hajj invalid.
2
Identify the istihsan ruling and its source
The passage says the Hajj is valid (jā'iz) from the deceased by istihsan. Note that this is authenticated in Al-Muhit and chosen by the authors of Fatāwā.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.
3
Analyze the reasoning: qiyas a priori
The proof is a qiyas a priori (first appropriateness): since the proxy could sell the camel and perform Hajj with the price (by istihsan), then he can also lease it and use the rental income. Selling disposes of the corpus, leasing disposes of the usufruct – the latter is less drastic.
The analogy is: if selling (corpus disposal) is allowed by istihsan, then leasing (usufruct disposal) is even more suitable.
4
Understand the necessity (darura)
The passage explicitly states the issue deviates from the original due to necessity. The necessity is to avoid harming the deceased by having the proxy be a usurper and the Hajj be invalid, and to achieve the deceased's benefit.
The original rule would be harsh; istihsan brings ease (al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir).
5
Note the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
The Hajj counts for the deceased, and the proxy returns the camel (or its value) to the heirs. The surplus rental fee, if any, is also returned.
The proxy does not keep extra profits; the benefit goes to the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومع التعيين المذكور لا يحل للمأمور المذكور ما فضل بل يرده على ورثته، ولهذا قالوا: لو أوصى بأن يعطى بعيره هذا رجلاً ليحج عنه فدفع إلى رجل فأكراه الرجل فأنفق الكراء على نفسه في الطريق وحج ماشياً جاز عن الميت استحساناً وإن خالف أمره. وصححه في المحيط. وقال أصحاب الفتاوى: هو المختار لأنه لما ملك أن يملك رقبتها بالبيع ويحج بالثمن استحساناً. هو المختار فلأن يملك أن يملك منفعتها بالإجارة ويحج ببدل المنفعة كان أولى لأنه لو لم يظهر في الآخرة أنه يملك ذلك يكون الكراء له لأنه غاصب والحج له فيتضرر الميت ثم يرد البعير إلى ورثة الميت لأنه ملك المورث. وهذه المسألة خرجت عن الأصل للضرورة فإن الأصل أن المأمور بالحج راكباً إذا حج ماشياً فإنه يكون مخالفاً
And with the aforementioned specification, it is not permissible for the mentioned agent [to keep] the surplus, rather he must return it to his heirs. For this reason they said: If he bequeathed that this camel of his be given to a man to perform Hajj on his behalf, and he gave it to a man, and the man rented out the camel, spent the rental fee on himself during the journey, and performed Hajj walking, it is valid on behalf of the deceased by istihsan, even though he opposed his instruction. And it was authenticated in Al-Muhit. And the authors of Fatawa said: It is the chosen position, because since he has the right to own its corpus by selling and perform Hajj with the price by istihsan, it is the chosen position. Then it is even more appropriate that he has the right to own its usufruct by leasing and perform Hajj with the substitute of the usufruct. Because if it does not become apparent in the end that he owns that, then the rental is for him because he is a usurper, and the Hajj is for him, so the deceased is harmed, then he returns the camel to the heirs of the deceased because it is the property of the testator. This issue deviates from the original due to necessity, for the original is that the agent for Hajj who is [told] to ride, if he performs Hajj walking, then he is [considered] contravening.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents an istihsan ruling from Al-Muhit and Fatāwā. The scenario: a testator bequeaths a specific camel to be given to a proxy for Hajj. The proxy instead rents out the camel, uses the rental income for his own expenses, and performs Hajj on foot. Normally, this would be a violation of the testator's instruction, making the proxy a usurper and the Hajj invalid. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), the Hajj is valid because the proxy could have sold the camel and used the proceeds for Hajj (which is permitted by istihsan). Since he has the right to dispose of the camel's corpus by sale, it is even more appropriate that he may dispose of its usufruct by leasing. The necessity is to benefit the deceased and avoid harm. The original rule (qiyas) would invalidate such an act, but istihsan overrides due to need.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that allows deviation from qiyas (analogy) due to necessity or custom, leading to a more equitable ruling.
المشقة تجلب التيسير (al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir): The legal maxim that hardship brings ease, underlying this istihsan ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
By which legal principle did the Hanafi jurists allow the proxy to rent out the camel and perform Hajj walking?
A) Qiyas jaliy
B) Istihsan
C) Ijma
D) Maslaha mursala

Key Takeaway
Istihsan can validate a Hajj proxy's contravention if it benefits the deceased and avoids hardship, overriding the original qiyas.

Proxy Hajj: Surplus Belongs to the Principal
Ruling on proxy Hajj with unspecified amount; surplus must be returned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a testator bequeaths Hajj without specifying an amount and explain why the proxy does not own any surplus.

Core Idea
The proxy for Hajj never owns the surplus unless explicitly permitted.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a testator leaves a will for Hajj but does not specify how much to spend. The executor must spend only what is necessary from the one-third of the estate. The proxy (agent) acts on behalf of the deceased and does not own the money; therefore any leftover must be returned. The same principle applies to endowments (waqf) designated for annual Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case
The testator bequeaths Hajj without specifying an amount. The heirs or executor must perform Hajj using the deceased's estate (from the one-third of the wealth).
2
Determine the Spending Rule
The executor should spend only the minimum necessary for a valid Hajj (e.g., 1000 dirhams if riding without a litter, or 1200 with a litter). The lesser of the two is taken.
This ensures the heirs' rights are protected.
3
Understand the Agency Principle
The proxy is not the owner of the money; he acts on the ownership of the deceased (or the living principal). Any surplus after the Hajj remains on the principal's ownership.
This is a trust situation, not a gift.
4
Apply the Ruling to Endowments
If a waqf (endowment) stipulates a specific amount for Hajj annually, the same rule applies: the appointed person must return any surplus to the waqf. The condition of the waqf is binding.
This extends the principle to waqf, as illustrated by Suleiman Pasha's endowment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يعين الموصي قدراً فإنَّ الورثة يحجون عنه من الثلث بقدر الكفاية. ولهذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه: رجل مات وأوصى أن يحج عنه ولم يقدر فيه مالاً، فالوصي إن أعطى إلى رجل ليحج عنه في محمل احتاج إلى ألف ومائتين، وإن حج راكباً لا في محمل يكفيه الألف وكل ذلك يخرج من الثلث يجب أقلهما لأنه فالحاصل أن المأمور لا يكون مالكاً لما أخذه المتيقن. هو بل يتصرف فيه على ملك المحجوج عنه حياً كان أو ميتاً، معيناً كان القدر أو غير معين، ولا يحل له الفضل إلا بالشرط المتقدم. سواء كان الفضل كثيراً أو يسيراً كيسير من صرح به في الفتاوى الظهيرية، وينبغي أن تكون كذلك الحجة المشروطة من جهة الواقف كما شرط سليمان باشا بوقفه بمصر قدراً معيناً لمن يحج عنه كل سنة فإنه يتبع شرطه، ولا يحل للمأمور ما فضل منه بل يجب رده إلى الوقف.
And if the testator did not specify an amount, then the heirs perform Hajj on his behalf from the third of the estate as much as suffices. For this reason, Al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa: A man died and bequeathed that Hajj be performed on his behalf, and did not specify any money. So the executor, if he gives to a man to perform Hajj on his behalf in a litter, he needs 1200; if he performs Hajj riding without a litter, 1000 suffices. All that comes out of the third. The lesser of the two must be taken, because the agent is not the owner of what he takes. Rather, he acts upon it on the ownership of the one for whom Hajj is performed, whether alive or dead, whether the amount was specified or unspecified. And the surplus is not permissible for him except with the previously mentioned condition. Whether the surplus is much or little, even a small amount as clarified in Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah. And likewise should be the conditioned Hajj from the side of the endowment (waqf), as Suleiman Pasha stipulated in his endowment in Egypt a specified amount for whoever performs Hajj on his behalf every year; his condition is followed, and what is surplus is not permissible for the agent but must be returned to the endowment.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion on proxy Hajj with unspecified amounts. The heirs must spend only what is necessary from the deceased's estate. The proxy does not own the money; it remains on the ownership of the deceased (or the living principal). Hence, any surplus must be returned. This applies equally to endowments (waqf) where a specific amount is stipulated for annual Hajj; the proxy cannot keep any surplus. The condition for ownership is the same as before: explicit permission by the principal to take the surplus as a gift.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor of the will, responsible for carrying out the testator's instructions.
الوقف (al-waqf): An endowment, in this context used to fund annual Hajj for the founder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths Hajj without specifying an amount, and the executor pays a proxy 1200 dirhams when 1000 would suffice, what must the proxy do with the extra 200?
A) Keep it as his fee.
B) Return it to the estate.
C) Spend it on charity for the testator.
D) Use it for his own expenses.

Key Takeaway
The proxy for Hajj does not own the money; any surplus must be returned to the testator's estate or waqf.

Unspecified Amount for Hajj: Proxy Ownership
Ruling on unspecified Hajj bequest leading to proxy ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an unspecified amount is given to a proxy for Hajj as a will, and explain why the proxy becomes the owner of the money.

Core Idea
The unspecified Hajj amount becomes the proxy's property, not a trust; he may choose to perform Hajj or not.

This lesson examines a specific Hanafi ruling regarding a proxy (na'ib) given an unspecified amount to perform Hajj on behalf of another. Unlike earlier cases where the money remains a trust, here the proxy becomes the owner. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the legal consequences in bequests and wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a person giving a proxy an unspecified amount with the instruction to perform Hajj, possibly under a will (from the deceased).
The amount is not fixed; the instruction is general.
2
Determine the legal classification
The money becomes the proxy's personal property (milk), not a trust (amanah). The passage states 'ويكون ملكاً له' (it becomes his property).
This is a key Hanafi distinction from other scenarios.
3
Explore the consequences
The proxy may perform Hajj with the money or not; if he performs, it counts for the principal; if not, the money is his and he is not obliged to perform.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) for the proxy.
4
Note the authority
The ruling is cited from Al-Mabsut and other classic Hanafi texts, making it a part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كم يعطي فإنه يعطي قدر ما يحج به ويكون ملكاً له وإن شاء حج به وإن شاء لم يحج وهو وصية كما في المبسوط وغيره.
How much should he give? For he gives the amount with which Hajj can be performed, and it becomes his property. If he wishes, he may perform Hajj with it, and if he wishes, he may not perform Hajj, and it is a bequest, as in Al-Mabsut and others.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This short passage presents a distinct ruling: if the principal gives a proxy a sum of money to perform Hajj without specifying an exact amount, that sum becomes the proxy's own property (like a gift). This is different from the earlier cases where the money remains on the ownership of the principal. Here, because the amount is unspecified and given as a general instruction, the proxy owns it and may choose whether to perform Hajj or not. However, this is considered a bequest (if from the deceased) or a gift (if from a living person). The ruling is from Al-Mabsut, a foundational Hanafi text.

Key Terms
ملكه (milkuhu): The money becomes the proxy's personal property, not a trust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when an unspecified amount is given to a proxy for Hajj as a will?
A) The proxy must perform Hajj or return the money.
B) The proxy becomes the owner of the money and may choose whether to perform Hajj.
C) The money must be given to charity if not used for Hajj.
D) The proxy is only a trustee and must return any surplus.

Key Takeaway
An unspecified amount given for Hajj as a will makes the proxy the owner, not a trustee — a key Hanafi distinction.

Permissible Expenses for the Hajj Proxy
Detailed list of what the proxy may spend on while traveling for Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for the Hajj proxy's expenses and apply the distinction between necessary and discretionary stays.

Core Idea
The proxy's reasonable travel expenses are from the principal; only necessary waiting stays qualify as travel expenses.

In Hanafi fiqh, when someone is appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another (al-ma'mur bil-hajj), the question of who bears the expenses arises. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the default rules: the proxy spends reasonably on travel necessities. But if he stays in Mecca after Hajj for non-essential reasons, the expenses shift to him. Understanding this distinction prevents wrongful depletion of the principal's wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule for proxy expenses
The proxy may spend on himself in a reasonable manner (nafaqah bi'l-ma'ruf) while going, returning, and staying. This includes food, drink, clothing, mount, and essential travel equipment.
Spending must be without extravagance or stinginess.
2
Distinguish between necessary and discretionary stays
If the proxy settles (tawattun) after Hajj, the cause matters: waiting for a caravan (necessity) keeps expenses on the principal; otherwise, on the proxy.
The ruling applies regardless of the duration if the reason is valid.
3
Apply the customary period of 15 days
Most scholars rule that if the proxy stays 15 days without an excuse (like waiting for caravan), expenses are on him. Some said 3 days, but the relied-upon position is 15 days when there is an excuse.
The 15-day period is interpreted as the maximum customary stay with a valid reason.
4
Analyze special cases: haste and alternate routes
If the proxy hastens to Mecca before Dhul-Hijjah, expenses are from his own until the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah. If he takes a longer route that is commonly used, expenses remain on the principal; otherwise, on him.
The ruling is based on custom and necessity.
5
Note the analogy to nashizah wife and mudarib
The passage analogizes the proxy who stays for personal need to a rebellious wife who returns home, and to a mudarib who stays in another town for his own need – both shift expenses to themselves.
This illustrates the principle: personal benefit shifts financial responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا عرف ذلك فللمأمور بالحج أن ينفق على نفسه بالمعروف ذاهباً وآيباً ومقيماً من غير تبذير ولا تقتير في طعامه وشرابه وثيابه وركوبه وما لا بد له منه من محمل وقربة وأدوات السفر، فلو توطن بمكة بعد الفراغ فإن كان لانتظار القافلة فنفقته في مال الميت وإلا فمن مال نفسه. وما ذكره أكثر المشايخ من أنه إذا توطن خمسة عشر يوماً فنفقته عليه، فمحمول على ما إذا كان لغير عذر وهو عدم خروج القافلة، وكذا ما ذكره بعضهم من اعتبار الثلاث. وإذا صارت النفقة عليه بعد خروجها ثم بدا له أن يرجع رجعت نفقته في مال الميته لأنه كان استحق نفقة الرجوع في مال الميت وهو كالناشزة، إذا عادت إلى المنزل والمضارب إذا أقام في بلد أو بلدة أخرى خمسة عشر يوماً لحاجة نفسه. وفي البدائع: هذا إذا لم يتخذ مكة داراً، فإما إذا اتخذها داراً ثم عاد لا تعود النفقة بلا خلاف وإن أقام بها من غير نية الإقامة قالوا: إن كانت الإقامة معتادة لم تسقط، وإن زاد على المعتاد سقطت ولو تعجل إلى مكة فهي في مال نفسه إلى أن يدخل عشر ذي الحجة فتصير في مال الآمر. ولو سلك طريقاً أبعد من المعتاد إن كان مما سلكه الناس ففي مال الآمر وإلا ففي ماله
When that is known, the agent for Hajj may spend on himself in a reasonable manner going, returning, and staying, without extravagance or stinginess, on his food, drink, clothing, mount, and what is indispensable for him of litter, water-skin, and travel equipment. If he settles in Mecca after completion, then if it is to wait for the caravan, his expenses are from the deceased's wealth; otherwise, from his own wealth. What most scholars mentioned, that if he settles for fifteen days, his expenses are on him, is interpreted as when it is without an excuse, i.e., the caravan not leaving. Similarly, what some mentioned of considering three [days]. And when the expenses become on him after the caravan leaves, then he decides to return, his expenses revert to being from the deceased's wealth, because he had become entitled to the return expenses from the deceased's wealth, and he is like the wife who is nashizah (rebellious) who returns home, and like the mudarib (silent partner) who stays in another town for fifteen days for his own need. In Al-Bada'i': This is if he did not take Mecca as [his] abode. If he took it as an abode and then returns, the expenses are not returned without disagreement. And if he stays without intention of residence, they said: if the stay is customary, it does not fall; if it exceeds the customary, it falls. And if he hastens to Mecca, the expenses are from his own wealth until the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah enters, then it becomes from the principal's wealth. And if he takes a route farther than usual, if it is among routes that people take, then from the principal's wealth; otherwise, from his own wealth.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rules for the Hajj proxy's expenses. The general principle is to spend reasonably without excess or stinginess. If the proxy stays in Mecca after completing Hajj, his expenses during the wait for a caravan are from the principal's wealth; if he stays for his own purpose, they are his own. The fifteen-day rule is interpreted as a customary period; if the delay is due to necessity (waiting for caravan), expenses remain on the principal. If the proxy decides to return after the caravan has left, his return expenses are also from the principal. If he takes a longer route that is commonly used, expenses are still on the principal; otherwise, on himself. The ruling from Al-Bada'i' explicitly distinguishes between taking Mecca as an abode (permanent residence) vs. temporary stay.

Key Terms
النفقة بالمعروف (al-nafaqah bi'l-ma'ruf): Spending in a customary and reasonable manner without waste or deprivation.
التوطن (al-tawattun): Taking Mecca as a home or settling there for a period beyond normal stay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Hajj proxy stays in Mecca for 15 days after the Hajj simply because he likes the city, who bears his expenses?
A) The principal (the one who hired him).
B) The proxy himself.
C) Half from each.
D) The state treasury.

Key Takeaway
The Hajj proxy's expenses are borne by the principal only for necessary travel and waiting; personal stays and disputed delays shift the burden to the proxy.

Prohibited Expenses and Trading by Hajj Proxy
List of impermissible expenses and ruling on trading with the Hajj fund.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which expenses are prohibited for a Hajj proxy and state the ruling on trading with the Hajj fund.

Core Idea
A Hajj proxy must spend only on necessities; luxury and personal expenses are prohibited, and trading requires charity of profit.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines the boundaries of what a Hajj proxy may spend. Some expenses are permissible as necessities, while others are luxuries and strictly prohibited. Additionally, trading with the Hajj fund or mixing it with personal money has specific consequences. Understanding these limits ensures the validity of the Hajj and the proxy’s trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Identify permissible expenses
Note the expenses the proxy is allowed: food (including meat), clothing, reward for Ihram, wages for a servant if needed, and a mount (donkey or camel).
Camel is recommended over donkey due to lower expenses.
2
Identify prohibited luxury expenses
List expenses considered luxuries or personal benefit: lamp oil, oils, medicine, cupping, bathhouse fees, and barber. These are not allowed unless there is a need (later scholars permit bathhouse and guard fees).
Some Hanafi authorities allow bathhouse and guard fees if necessary.
3
List other prohibited uses
The proxy may not use the fund to invite others, give charity, make loans, exchange currency, or buy water for wudu.
These are personal or charitable uses beyond the scope of Hajj.
4
Understand ruling on trading
If the proxy trades with the fund and makes a profit, then performs Hajj with an equivalent amount, the Hajj is valid for the deceased, but the profit must be given in charity.
This is similar to mixing funds, which makes the proxy a guarantor.
5
Note exception for mixing funds with companions
The proxy may mix his funds with fellow travelers for joint expenses due to custom, as recorded in Al-Muhit.
Custom (urf) permits this pooling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله أن ينفق على نفسه نفقة مثله من طعام ومنه اللحم والكسوة ومنه ثوابا إحرامه وأجرة من يخدمه إن كان ممن يخدم، وليس له أن ينفق ما فيه ترفيه كدهن السراج والادهان والتدواي والاحتجام وأجرة الحمام والحلاق إلا أن. عليه. واختار في المحيط والخانية أن يعطي أجرة الحمام والحارس، وصرح الولوالجي بأنه المختار وقالوا له أن يشتري حماراً يركبه. وذكر الولوالجي بأنه مكروه والجمل أفضل لأن النفقة فيه أكثر. وليس له أن يدعو أحداً إلى طعامه ولا يتصدق به ولا يقرض أحداً ولا يصرف الدراهم بالدنانير ولا يشتري بها ماء لوضوئه، ولو اتجر في المال ثم حج بمثله فالأصح أنها عن الميت. ويتصدق بالربح كما لو خلطها بدراهمه حتى صار ضامناً ثم حج بمثلها. وله أن يخلط الدراهم للنفقة مع الرفقة للعرف كذا في المحيط.
And he may spend on himself like his peers in food, including meat, clothing, and including the reward for his Ihram, and the wages of a servant if he is someone who is served. And he may not spend on luxuries like lamp oil, oils, medicine, cupping, bathhouse fees, and barber, except if [he has a need?]. And Al-Muhit and Al-Khaniyyah chose that he may give the bathhouse and guard fee, and Al-Walwaliji stated that it is the chosen. And they said: He may buy a donkey to ride. And Al-Walwaliji mentioned that it is makruh, and a camel is better because expenses on it are more. And he may not invite anyone to his food, nor give charity from it, nor lend anyone, nor exchange dirhams for dinars, nor buy water for his wudu with it. And if he trades with the money and then performs Hajj with the like of it, the most correct view is that it is on behalf of the deceased, and he gives the profit as charity, just as if he mixed it with his own dirhams and thus became a guarantor, then performed Hajj with the like of it. And he may mix the dirhams for expenses with the companions due to custom, as in Al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage clarifies the limits of the proxy's spending. He may spend on food, clothing, hire a servant if customary, and buy a mount. However, he cannot spend on luxuries like lamp oil, personal oils, medical treatments, cupping, bathhouse, or barber—unless there is a need (as some scholars allow). He cannot use the money to invite others, give charity, make loans, exchange currency, or buy water for wudu (since that is a personal religious expense). If the proxy trades with the Hajj fund and makes a profit, and then performs Hajj with an equivalent amount, the Hajj is valid for the deceased, and the profit must be given as charity. This is analogous to mixing the fund with his own money, which makes him a guarantor—he must give the profit in charity. However, he may mix the funds with fellow travelers for joint expenses due to custom.

Key Terms
التجارة بالمال (al-tijarah bi'l-mal): Using the Hajj fund for trade with the intention of profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Hajj proxy uses some of the Hajj money to buy goods to sell along the way, what must he do with any profit?
A) Keep it as a reward for his effort.
B) Give it as charity.
C) Return it to the principal along with the Hajj expenses.
D) Use it for extra Hajj rituals.

Key Takeaway
The proxy must limit spending to necessities and avoid any trading or personal luxury; profit from unauthorized trade must be given in charity.

Blood Offerings in Hajj by Proxy: Principal vs. Agent Liability
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for blood offerings in Hajj by proxy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the liability of the principal and proxy for blood offerings in Hajj and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding payment from the deceased principal's estate.

Core Idea
Liability follows causation: the principal owes dam al-ihsar; the proxy owes dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah.

In Hajj performed by proxy, who bears the cost of obligatory blood offerings? The answer depends on the type of offering and whose action caused it. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the general rule and then presents a nuanced dispute about the deceased principal's estate. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assigning financial responsibility in proxy Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties and Their General Liabilities
Recognize that the principal (the one for whom Hajj is performed) is liable for dam al-ihsar (obstruction), while the proxy is liable for dam al-qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) and dam al-jinayah (violations). Note the rationale: the principal is under the obligation and must fulfill it; the proxy is responsible for his own actions.
The passage explicitly states: 'دم الإحصار على الأمر ودم القرآن ودم الجناية على المأمور'.
2
Understand the Scope of 'Principal' (Al-Amir)
The term 'principal' includes the deceased person for whom Hajj is performed. This leads to the question of how to pay for the blood offering from the deceased's estate.
The text says: 'وأراد من الآمر المحجوج عنه فشمل الميت'.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Two views are presented: (1) dam al-ihsar is taken from the third of the estate, like a bequest (ṣilah), akin to zakat; (2) it is taken from the entire estate because it becomes a debt owed to the proxy. Understand the rationale for each view.
The dispute is cited from Al-Hidayah: 'قيل هو من ثلث ماله... وقيل من جميع وجب حقاً للمأمور فصار ديناً'.
4
Evaluate the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If from the third, the offering is limited by the one-third rule of bequests, potentially leaving the heirs unaffected if the estate is large. If from the whole, it is a debt that must be paid before distribution, reducing the heirs' shares.
No tarjih is given in this text; both views are considered valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ودم) الإحصار على الأمر ودم القرآن ودم الجناية على المأمور) لأن الأمر هو الذي في هذه العهدة فعليه خلاصه وأراد من الآمر المحجوج عنه فشمل الميت فإن دم الإحصار من ماله ثم قيل هو من ثلث ماله لأنه صلة كالزكاة وغيرها، وقيل من جميع وجب حقاً للمأمور فصار ديناً. كذا في الهداية.
His saying: (And blood) [of] obstruction is upon the principal, and blood of combining (qiran) and blood of violation (jinayah) upon the agent, because the principal is the one who is under this obligation, so upon him is its fulfillment. And by 'principal' is meant the one for whom Hajj is performed, so it includes the deceased. So the blood of obstruction is from his wealth. Then it is said: It is from the third of his wealth because it is a charitable gift like zakat and others. And it is said: From all of it because it becomes a right of the agent, so it becomes a debt. This is in Al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on a line from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding liability for blood offerings (dams) in Hajj. The principal (the one on whose behalf Hajj is performed) is liable for the blood of obstruction (ihsar) because he is the one obligated. The proxy is liable for blood of combining (qiran) and violations (jinayah) because they arise from his actions. For the deceased, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say the blood of obstruction comes from the third of the estate (like a bequest), others say from the entire estate because it becomes a debt owed to the proxy. The commentary refers to Al-Hidayah for this ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
دم الإحصار (dam al-ihsar): A blood offering (sacrifice) required when one is prevented from completing Hajj due to an obstacle.
دم الجناية (dam al-jinayah): A blood offering for violations committed during Ihram, such as hunting, shaving, or sexual activity.
دم القرآن (dam al-qiran): A blood offering required when performing Hajj and Umrah together (qiran).
الآمر (al-amir): The principal: the person who hires someone to perform Hajj on his behalf, or the deceased on whose behalf Hajj is performed.
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The proxy: the person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A proxy for Hajj commits a violation (jinayah) during Ihram. Who is liable for the required blood offering?
A) The principal (the one for whom Hajj is being performed).
B) The proxy himself.
C) Both share equally.
D) No one, since it was accidental.

Key Takeaway
In Hajj by proxy, the principal bears dam al-ihsar; the proxy bears dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah; for a deceased principal, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether dam al-ihsar comes from the third or the whole estate.
