Ruling on Obstructed Hajj Proxy: Make-Up Hajj Next Year
Ruling on obstructed proxy's make-up Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an obstructed Hajj proxy (muhsir) who performs tahlul, and explain why he must perform Hajj the next year at his own expense.

Core Idea
An obstructed Hajj proxy must repeat Hajj at his own cost, like one who misses the standing.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario: a person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another (the principal) is prevented from completing the rites due to an obstacle (muhsir). He exits Ihram by sacrificing an animal. What are his obligations? The text rules that he must perform Hajj the following year from his own wealth, and he is not liable for the expenses incurred. This ruling is analogous to the case of one who misses the Hajj altogether (fa'it al-hajj). Additionally, if he was hired for a specified amount in a will, the same duty applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage deals with a muhsir agent who performs tahlul by sacrificing an animal.
The agent was appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another.
2
State the primary ruling
He must perform Hajj the next year from his own wealth.
This is an obligation (wajib).
3
Note the financial liability
He is not a guarantor for the expenses already spent.
Contrast with cases of contravention.
4
Understand the analogy
The ruling is like that of one who misses the Hajj (fa'it al-hajj).
The common element is the absence of contravention.
5
Apply to the executor of a will
The same ruling applies if the proxy was hired via a will with a fixed amount.
The passage ends with 'وعليه الموصى قدراً'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا تحلل المأمور المحصر بذبح الهدي فعليه الحج من قابل بمال نفسه ولا يكون ضامناً للنفقة كفائت الحج لعدم المخالفة، وعليه الموصى قدراً
And when the obstructed agent performs tahlul by slaughtering the sacrificial animal, then upon him is [to perform] Hajj the following year from his own wealth, and he is not a guarantor for the expenses, like the one who misses Hajj, due to the absence of contravention. And upon him [is] he who was bequeathed an amount.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on proxy Hajj by addressing a special case: the proxy who is prevented from completing Hajj (muhsir) and thus performs tahlul (exits Ihram) by sacrificing an animal. In this case, he must perform Hajj the next year at his own expense, and he is not liable to reimburse the principal for expenses already incurred, because he did not contravene—the obstruction was beyond his control. This ruling applies to a proxy who was given a specified amount in a will (al-muṣā bi qadran). The passage ties back to earlier discussions on the will for Hajj.

Key Terms
المحصر (al-muhsir): One who is prevented from completing Hajj due to an obstacle such as illness, enemy, or other forces.
التحلل (al-tahlul): Exiting the state of Ihram after performing the necessary sacrifice or completing the rituals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An obstructed Hajj proxy (muhsir) sacrifices an animal and returns home. What is his obligation?
A) He owes nothing; the sacrifice completes his duty.
B) He must perform Hajj the next year at his own expense.
C) He must refund the principal for all expenses.
D) He must send a proxy in his place the next year.

Key Takeaway
An obstructed Hajj proxy must perform Hajj the following year at his own expense and is not liable for prior expenses, analogous to one who misses the Hajj without fault.

Permissible Expenses of the Appointed Hajji
Ruling on permissible expenses and residence-related costs for the appointed Hajji.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling on the appointee's expenses from the principal's wealth and apply the rule regarding residence in Mecca after Hajj, distinguishing between waiting for the caravan and personal stay.

Core Idea
The appointee may spend reasonably on necessities; residence expenses shift to him if not due to waiting for the caravan.

This lesson explores the foundational principles governing what an appointed Hajj performer may spend from the deceased's estate. The text establishes the baseline of reasonable spending without extravagance, then delves into the critical issue of residence after Hajj, where the duty of the principal's wealth depends on the appointee's intent and reason for staying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Determine the baseline for spending: the appointee (al-ma'mur) may spend on himself in a reasonable manner (bi al-ma'ruf) without extravagance or stinginess.
This is the overarching principle governing all expenses.
2
List categories of permissible expense
Identify the specific items allowed: food, drink, clothing, mount (riding animal), litter, water-skin, and travel equipment.
These are necessities for the journey.
3
Analyze residence (tawattun) after Hajj
Two cases: if the appointee resides in Mecca to wait for the caravan, expenses remain on the deceased; if for any other reason, expenses are on the appointee himself.
The reason for staying determines the liability.
4
Apply the 15-day rule
Most scholars said that if he resides 15 days, expenses are on him. But this is qualified: it applies only when there is no excuse (i.e., the caravan is not leaving). Some scholars considered 3 days.
The 15-day rule is not absolute; it depends on the caravan situation.
5
Note the analogy for reversion of expenses
If expenses become on him after the caravan leaves, then he decides to return, his return expenses revert to the deceased's estate. The text compares this to a nashizah (disobedient wife) returning home and a mudarib (silent partner) staying for personal need.
The analogy illustrates that reversion is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا عرف ذلك فللمأمور بالحج أن ينفق على نفسه بالمعروف ذاهباً وآيباً ومقيماً من غير تبذير ولا تقتير في طعامه وشرابه وثيابه وركوبه وما لا بد له منه من محمل وقربة وأدوات السفر، فلو توطن بمكة بعد الفراغ فإن كان لانتظار القافلة فنفقته في مال الميت وإلا فمن مال نفسه. وما ذكره أكثر المشايخ من أنه إذا توطن خمسة عشر يوماً فنفقته عليه، فمحمول على ما إذا كان لغير عذر وهو عدم خروج القافلة، وكذا ما ذكره بعضهم من اعتبار الثلاث. وإذا صارت النفقة عليه بعد خروجها ثم بدا له أن يرجع رجعت نفقته في مال الميته لأنه كان استحق نفقة الرجوع في مال الميت وهو كالناشزة، إذا عادت إلى المنزل والمضارب إذا أقام في بلد أو بلدة أخرى خمسة عشر يوماً لحاجة نفسه. وفي البدائع : هذا إذا لم يتخذ مكة داراً، فإما إذا اتخذها داراً ثم عاد لا تعود النفقة بلا خلاف وإن أقام بها من غير نية الإقامة قالوا: إن كانت الإقامة معتادة لم تسقط، وإن زاد على المعتاد سقطت ولو تعجل إلى مكة فهي في مال نفسه إلى أن يدخل عشر ذي الحجة فتصير في مال الآمر . ولو سلك طريقاً أبعد من المعتاد إن كان مما سلكه الناس ففي مال الآمر وإلا ففي ماله وله أن ينفق على نفسه نفقة مثله من طعام ومنه اللحم والكسوة ومنه ثوابا إحرامه وأجرة من يخدمه إن كان ممن يخدم، وليس له أن ينفق ما فيه ترفيه كدهن السراج والادهان والتدواي والاحتجام وأجرة الحمام والحلاق إلا أن. عليه. واختار في المحيط والخانية أن يعطي أجرة الحمام والحارس، وصرح الولوالجي بأنه المختار وقالوا له أن يشتري حماراً يركبه . وذكر الولوالجي بأنه مكروه والجمل أفضل لأن النفقة فيه أكثر . وليس له أن يدعو أحداً إلى طعامه ولا يتصدق به ولا يقرض أحداً ولا يصرف الدراهم بالدنانير ولا يشتري بها ماء لوضوئه، ولو اتجر في المال ثم حج بمثله فالأصح أنها عن الميت. ويتصدق بالربح كما لو خلطها بدراهمه حتى صار ضامناً ثم حج بمثلها. وله أن يخلط الدراهم للنفقة . مع الرفقة للعرف كذا في المحيط .
When that is known, the one commanded to perform Hajj may spend on himself in a reasonable manner while going, returning, and staying, without extravagance or stinginess, in his food, drink, clothing, mount, and what he inevitably needs of a litter, water-skin, and travel equipment. If he takes up residence in Mecca after finishing, if it is to wait for the caravan, his expenses are from the deceased's estate; otherwise from his own wealth. What most scholars mentioned that if he resides fifteen days, his expenses are upon him, is interpreted as when it is without an excuse, i.e., the caravan not leaving. Similarly, what some mentioned of considering three days. When expenses become upon him after the caravan leaves, then he decides to return, his expenses revert to the deceased's estate because he had deserved the return expenses from the deceased's estate, and he is like a nashizah when she returns home, and the mudarib when he stays in a town or another town for fifteen days for his own need. In al-Bada'i': This is if he does not take Mecca as a home. If he takes it as a home and then returns, the expenses do not revert without dispute. If he stays without intention of residence, they said: if the stay is customary, it does not drop; if it exceeds the customary, it drops. If he hurries to Mecca, it is from his own wealth until he enters the tenth of Dhul-Hijjah, then it becomes from the principal's wealth. If he takes a road farther than the customary, if it is among what people traverse, it is from the principal's wealth; otherwise from his own. He may spend on himself like his peers in food, including meat, clothing, and the garments of his ihram, and the wage of one who serves him if he is of those who are served. He may not spend on that which involves luxury, like lamp oil, oiling, medicine, cupping, bathhouse fee, and barber fee except... It is chosen in al-Muhit and al-Khaniyah that he is given the bathhouse and guard fee, and al-Walwaliji declared it the chosen view. They said he may buy a donkey to ride. Al-Walwaliji mentioned it is disliked, and a camel is better because expenditure on it is more. He may not invite anyone to his food, nor give charity from it, nor lend to anyone, nor exchange dirhams for dinars, nor buy water for his ablution with it. If he trades with the money and then performs Hajj with its like, the correct view is that it is on behalf of the deceased. He gives the profit in charity, just as if he mixed it with his own dirhams so he became a guarantor, then he performed Hajj with its like. He may mix dirhams for expenses with the company customarily. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of expenses for the person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another (whether a deceased or someone unable). The author, Ibn Nujaym, details what the appointee (al-ma'mur) may spend from the principal's (al-ammir) wealth. The key principle is that the appointee is a trustee (amin) and must spend reasonably (bi al-ma'ruf) without extravagance or miserliness. The passage covers several scenarios: initial travel expenses, residence in Mecca after Hajj, changing the route, and what constitutes permissible expenses (necessities like food, clothing, transport, servant's hire) versus luxuries (oil, medicines, bathhouse, etc.) which are not allowed unless specified by the principal. There is also discussion on mixing money and engaging in trade; the profit must be given in charity and the Hajj is valid. The commentary follows the Hanafi madhhab, citing authorities like al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, al-Khaniyah, and al-Walwaliji. The mufta bihi position favors giving the appointee the bathhouse and guard fee, and it is permissible to buy a donkey but disliked; a camel is better.

Key Terms
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person appointed or commanded to perform Hajj on behalf of another (the principal or deceased).
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Expenses necessary for the journey, including food, drink, clothing, transport, and essential items.
التوطن (al-tawattun): Taking up residence in a place (here Mecca) after completing Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the appointed Hajji resides in Mecca after Hajj for 15 days waiting for the caravan, whose wealth bears the expenses?
A) The appointee's own wealth, because 15 days is too long.
B) The deceased's estate, because he is waiting for the caravan.
C) Half from the deceased, half from the appointee.
D) It depends on whether the caravan leaves within 15 days.

Key Takeaway
The appointee's residence expenses after Hajj are on the deceased only if he stays for a reason related to the journey (e.g., waiting for the caravan); otherwise, they are on himself.

Luxury Expenses and Trade by the Appointed Hajji
Rulings on prohibited luxuries and ancillary financial transactions by the appointee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible necessities and prohibited luxuries for the appointee, and apply the ruling on buying a donkey versus a camel, as well as the effect of trading with the Hajj funds.

Core Idea
The appointee cannot spend on luxuries but may buy a donkey (disliked) or camel; profit from trade must be given in charity.

This lesson continues from the previous one, delving into the finer details of what constitutes permissible spending. The text distinguishes between true necessities and mere comforts, providing rulings on items like oil, cupping, and the barber. It also addresses practical concerns such as purchasing a mount, trading with the allocated funds, and mixing money.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of prohibited luxury items
The text lists: lamp oil, oiling (any oil for body/hair), medicine, cupping, bathhouse fee, and barber fee. These are considered tanzihi (luxury) and not allowed.
The default is prohibition; exceptions are made for bathhouse and guard fee according to some authorities.
2
Note the exception for bathhouse and guard fee
Al-Muhit and al-Khaniyah chose that the appointee is given the bathhouse and guard fee. Al-Walwaliji declared this the chosen view (mukhtar).
This is a mufta bihi position, overriding the general prohibition.
3
Analyze the ruling on buying a mount
The appointee may buy a donkey to ride, but al-Walwaliji said it is makruh (disliked). A camel is better because expenses on it are more (i.e., more beneficial).
The ruling is permissive but with a preference for camel.
4
Understand prohibitions on using funds for others
The appointee may not invite others to his food, give charity from it, lend money, exchange dirhams for dinars, or buy water for wudu with the hajj funds.
These actions are either using the funds for non-essential purposes or mixing with personal benefit.
5
Learn the ruling on trading and mixing money
If the appointee trades with the hajj money (e.g., engages in commerce), the profit must be given in charity, and the hajj is valid if performed with its like. If he mixes the money with his own, he becomes a guarantor (damman) but still can perform hajj with the like amount.
The profit does not belong to the appointee; it must be disposed in charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

When that is known, the one commanded to perform Hajj may spend on himself in a reasonable manner while going, returning, and staying, without extravagance or stinginess, in his food, drink, clothing, mount, and what he inevitably needs of a litter, water-skin, and travel equipment. If he stays without intention of residence, they said: if the stay is customary, it does not drop; if it exceeds the customary, it drops. If he takes a road farther than the customary, if it is among what people traverse, it is from the principal's wealth; otherwise from his own. Al-Walwaliji mentioned it is disliked, and a camel is better because expenditure on it is more. He may not invite anyone to his food, nor give charity from it, nor lend to anyone, nor exchange dirhams for dinars, nor buy water for his ablution with it. If he trades with the money and then performs Hajj with its like, the correct view is that it is on behalf of the deceased. He gives the profit in charity, just as if he mixed it with his own dirhams so he became a guarantor, then he performed Hajj with its like. He may mix dirhams for expenses with the company customarily. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of expenses for the person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another (whether a deceased or someone unable). The author, Ibn Nujaym, details what the appointee (al-ma'mur) may spend from the principal's (al-ammir) wealth. The key principle is that the appointee is a trustee (amin) and must spend reasonably (bi al-ma'ruf) without extravagance or miserliness. The passage covers several scenarios: initial travel expenses, residence in Mecca after Hajj, changing the route, and what constitutes permissible expenses (necessities like food, clothing, transport, servant's hire) versus luxuries (oil, medicines, bathhouse, etc.) which are not allowed unless specified by the principal. There is also discussion on mixing money and engaging in trade; the profit must be given in charity and the Hajj is valid. The commentary follows the Hanafi madhhab, citing authorities like al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, al-Khaniyah, and al-Walwaliji. The mufta bihi position favors giving the appointee the bathhouse and guard fee, and it is permissible to buy a donkey but disliked; a camel is better.

Key Terms
الترفيه (al-tarfih): Luxury or comfort items beyond basic necessity, such as lamp oil, body oil, medicine, cupping, bathhouse, and barber services.
التجارة (al-tijarah): Trade or commerce using the Hajj funds.
الضمان (al-daman): Guarantee or liability; here, if the appointee mixes his money with the Hajj funds, he becomes a guarantor (damin) of the equivalent amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the appointed Hajji buys a donkey to ride during the journey, what is the ruling?
A) It is allowed but disliked, and a camel is better.
B) It is absolutely forbidden.
C) It is only allowed if the principal explicitly permits.
D) It is recommended and must be done.

Key Takeaway
The appointee must avoid luxury expenditures, but practical needs like a bathhouse fee are allowed by the preferred view; trading requires charity of profit.

Dam and Missed Hajj for the Appointed Pilgrim
Clarifies who bears dam and liability in proxy Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who bears the dam for ihsar, qiran, and jinnayah, and apply the Hanafi ruling on liability when the appointee misses Hajj due to negligence or unavoidable cause.

Core Idea
Dam for ihsar is on the principal; dam for qiran and jinnayah is on the appointee; missed Hajj due to negligence makes the appointee liable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq untangles the allocation of blood sacrifices (dam) when someone performs Hajj on behalf of another. It also resolves a critical question: what happens if the appointed pilgrim misses the Hajj? Understanding these rulings protects the validity of the proxy Hajj and prevents financial disputes between the principal and the appointee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of dam and their bearers
The passage states: dam al-ihsar is upon the principal (the one on whose behalf Hajj is performed), while dam al-qiran and dam al-jinnayah are upon the appointee. Note that 'principal' includes the deceased.
Dam al-ihsar may come from the principal's one-third (if bequest) or entire estate (if debt).
2
Understand the reasoning for dam al-qiran
The appointee bears dam al-qiran because it is gratitude for the blessing of combining the two rituals, a real action emanating from the appointee, even though the Hajj legally falls for the principal.
This distinguishes it from dam al-ihsar, which is a means to free the principal from the obligation.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for violating instructions
If the appointee does qiran when commanded to do ifrad, Abu Hanifa holds him liable for expenses because he violated a specific command. The Sahibayn say it is a violation towards good and thus no liability.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: the appointee must follow instructions or bear costs.
4
Apply the rule for missed Hajj (fawat) based on cause
If the appointee misses Hajj due to negligence, he is liable for expenses and must repeat Hajj next year on behalf of the principal from his own wealth. If due to an unavoidable cause (illness, etc.), he is not liable and repeats Hajj on his own behalf.
This distinction between trustee (amin) and guarantor (damin) is crucial.

Two cases remain where he is violating by doing qiran: one is when they did not permit him to do qiran and he did qiran on their behalf, then he is liable for their expenses. The second is when he commanded him to do ifrad (Hajj only) and he did qiran, then he is liable for expenses; not because ifrad is better than qiran, but because he commanded him to perform a separate journey and he violated. If he misses Hajj (fawat), he is not liable because he is a trustee, and he must make up the missed Hajj and perform Hajj for the principal. Then he narrated from al-Karkhi what we have presented: that guarantee is not required of him, and upon himself is Hajj next year, up to the end of what is mentioned in al-Nahr. What is established from these narrations is that either he missed it due to his negligence or not. In the first, he is liable for expenses and performs Hajj next year on behalf of the deceased from his own wealth, as in al-Hawi. In the second, he is not liable for expenses and performs Hajj next year on his own behalf according to al-Muntaqa and al-Siraj. As for what is in al-Tahdhib, it is from...
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with two main issues: first, who bears the dam (blood sacrifice) when the appointed Hajji is prevented (ihsar), performs qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah), or commits a jinnayah (infraction); second, what happens if the appointee misses the Hajj (fawat). The author explains that dam for ihsar is on the principal (the one on whose behalf the Hajj is performed) because the principal is responsible for freeing the appointee from the obligation. There is a difference of opinion whether this dam comes from the principal's entire estate or only from one-third (if it is a bequest). The dam for qiran and jinnayah is on the appointee because these arise from his own actions. For qiran, the text provides reasoning: it is gratitude for the blessing of combining the two rituals, which the appointee experiences. If the appointee is prevented (muhsar) and sacrifices, he must still perform Hajj the next year from his own wealth, and he is not liable for expenses. The passage then discusses the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether the appointee acting against instructions (e.g., doing qiran when told to do ifrad) makes him liable. Abu Hanifa holds him liable because he violated the command; the Sahibayn say it is a violation towards good (i.e., he did something better) and thus not liable. The book favors Abu Hanifa's view. Regarding missed Hajj (fawat), the text collects numerous authorities: from Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and al-Karkhi. The settled position (al-mu'tamad) is that if the appointee misses Hajj due to negligence, he is liable for expenses and must perform Hajj next year on behalf of the deceased from his own wealth. If due to an unavoidable cause (like illness), he is not liable for expenses and the next year's Hajj is on his own behalf, not the deceased's. This is a crucial ruling differentiating between trustee (amin) and guarantor (damin) status.

Key Terms
دم الإحصار (dam al-ihsar): The blood sacrifice required when a pilgrim is prevented from completing Hajj (ihsar) and must slaughter a hady.
دم القران (dam al-qiran): The blood sacrifice required for performing Hajj and Umrah together (qiran) as gratitude.
الفوات (al-fawat): Missing the standing at Arafat (wuquf) thus missing Hajj for that year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the appointee misses Hajj due to an unavoidable cause (e.g., illness), what is the ruling regarding the next year's Hajj?
A) He must perform Hajj on behalf of the principal from his own wealth.
B) He must perform Hajj on his own behalf and is not liable for expenses.
C) The missed Hajj is waived; no repetition is needed.
D) He must perform Hajj on behalf of the principal but the expenses are covered by the principal's estate.

Key Takeaway
The appointee is liable for expenses and must repeat Hajj for the principal only when he violates instructions or is negligent; otherwise, he is a trustee and repeats on his own behalf.

Bearing the Dam of Ihsar, Qiran, and Jinaya in Hajj on Behalf
States the rule for who bears the dam of ihsar, qiran, and jinaya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the dam for ihsar, qiran, and jinaya when performing Hajj on behalf of another, and explain the rational proof (talil) for the agent bearing the dam of qiran.

Core Idea
The agent bears dam for his own acts; the principal bears dam for external prevention.

When Hajj is performed on behalf of another (Hajj al-ghayr), various dam obligations may arise. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq distinguishes three types: dam al-ihsar (prevention), dam al-qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah), and dam al-jinaya (violations). It then provides a rational proof for why the agent bears dam al-qiran, based on the principle of gratitude for actual performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three dam obligations
List the three types of dam mentioned: al-ihsar, al-qiran, and al-jinaya. Note each arises from a different cause.
These are standard categories in Hajj jurisprudence.
2
State the primary rule for each dam
The text states: dam al-ihsar is on the principal (al-āmir), while dam al-qiran and al-jinaya are on the agent (al-ma'mūr). Commit this distinction.
The principal is the one who commissions the Hajj; the agent performs it.
3
Analyze the talil for dam al-qiran
The proof: dam al-qiran is wajib as gratitude (shukr) for the blessing of combining the two rites. Since the agent actually performed the acts, the gratitude belongs to him, so the dam is his responsibility.
Even though the Hajj legally counts for the principal (wuqū' shar'ī), the real action (haqīqat al-fi'l) is from the agent.
4
Note the unresolved issues
The text mentions but does not yet resolve: if the agent dies or misses the Hajj, does the makeup Hajj count for the principal or agent? This is left for later discussion.
Recognize that not every question is answered in this passage.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical scenario
Consider: A man hires Zayd to perform Hajj and Umrah together (qiran). Zayd commits a violation (jinaya) in ihram. Who bears each dam? Use the rule to determine.
This tests understanding of the attribution of each dam type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودم الإحصار على الآمر ودم القران والجناية على المأمور فإن مات في طريقه الحج من قابل بمال نفسه كذا قالوا: ولم يصرحوا بأنه في الإحصار والفوات إذا قضى الحج هل يكون عن الآمر أو يقع للمأمور : وإذا كان للآمر فهل يجبر على الحج من قابل بمال نفسه. وإنما وجب دم القرآن على المأمور باعتبار أنه وجب شكراً لما وفقه الله تعالى من الجمع بين النسكين والمأمور هو المختص بهذه النعمة لأن حقيقة الفعل منه وإن كان الحج يقع عن الآمر لأنه وقوع شرعي، ووجوب دم الشكر مسبب عن الفعل الحقيقي الصادر . من المأمور .
And the blood sacrifice of prevention (ihsar) is upon the commander (principal) and the blood sacrifice of combining (qiran) and of violations (jinaya) is upon the commanded (agent). If he dies on his way, he performs Hajj the following year with his own wealth. Thus they said: And they did not clarify whether in the case of prevention (ihsar) and missing (fawat), if he performs the makeup Hajj, whether it is on behalf of the principal or falls for the agent. And if it is for the principal, is he then forced to perform Hajj the following year with his own wealth? The blood sacrifice of combining (qiran) is required from the agent because it is required as gratitude for what Allah facilitated for him of combining the two rites, and the agent is specifically entitled to this blessing because the reality of the action is from him, even though the Hajj falls for the principal because it is a legal occurrence, and the obligation of the blood sacrifice of gratitude is caused by the real action emanating from the agent.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq states a ruling on who bears the dam (blood sacrifice) obligations when performing Hajj on behalf of another. It distinguishes three types of dam: dam al-ihsar (due to prevention from completing Hajj), dam al-qiran (due to combining Hajj and 'Umrah), and dam al-jinaya (due to violations like hunting or wearing sewn clothes). The ruling: dam al-ihsar is on the principal (the one who commissioned the Hajj), while dam al-qiran and dam al-jinaya are on the agent performing the Hajj. The text then begins to discuss what happens if the agent dies or misses the Hajj, a theme to be continued. The reasoning provided for dam al-qiran being on the agent is that it is a gratitude offering (shukr) for the blessing of having performed both rites, and that blessing belongs to the agent because the actual physical actions are from him. Even though the Hajj legally counts for the principal, the gratitude obligation arises from the real act of the agent. This is a key Hanafi principle: the 'illah (effective cause) for the dam is the actual performance, not the legal attribution.

Key Terms
دم الإحصار (dam al-ihsar): Blood sacrifice required when a person performing Hajj is prevented from completing it, e.g., by enemy or illness.
دم القران (dam al-qiran): Blood sacrifice required for combining Hajj and 'Umrah in the same journey without performing a separate 'Umrah.
الجناية (al-jinaya): Violations committed while in ihram, such as killing game, wearing sewn clothes, applying perfume, etc., requiring dam or penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is required to offer the dam (blood sacrifice) for combining Hajj and 'Umrah (qiran) when the Hajj is performed on behalf of another person?
A) The principal (the one who commissioned the Hajj)
B) Both the principal and the agent
C) The agent (the one performing the Hajj)
D) No dam is required for qiran

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, dam obligations in Hajj on behalf are assigned based on who performed the act (agent) or who is affected by prevention (principal).

Agent's Liability When Hajj Is Invalidated Before Wuquf
Rulings on agent's invalidation before Wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the agent's obligations (blood, expense guarantee, repeat Hajj) when Hajj is invalidated before Wuquf and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the repetition counts for the principal.

Core Idea
The agent bears the consequences of invalidating Hajj; the principal's obligation is not automatically fulfilled.

When an agent (na'ib) invalidates the Hajj of his principal (amir) by committing intercourse before Wuquf, the Hanafi school holds that the agent must repeat the Hajj with his own money and bear all expenses. However, there is an unresolved dispute (taraddud) within the school whether this repetition counts as the principal's obligatory Hajj or not. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act that invalidates Hajj
The passage specifies that intercourse before Wuquf invalidates Hajj (fasad). Understand what fasad means in Hajj context: it requires repetition but not nullification of the entire act.
After Wuquf, intercourse does not invalidate but still requires blood.
2
Determine financial liability
If intercourse occurs before Wuquf, the agent guarantees all expenses (nafaqa) because he became a violator. After Wuquf, no guarantee, but blood (dam) is still due.
Expenses include travel, lodging, etc.
3
Extract the obligation to repeat Hajj
The agent must perform Hajj the following year with his own money. This is wajib upon him.
Failure to repeat may incur sin.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute (taraddud)
The passage mentions hesitation (taraddud) about whether the repeated Hajj counts for the principal. One view says it does; the other says it does not. The context leans toward the principal remaining obligated.
The author does not explicitly choose, but later practice favors the principal's duty.
5
Connect to the principal's obligation
Since the invalidation was the agent's fault, the principal must still provide another Hajj (from his own wealth or another agent). The passage states 'يجب على الآمر الإحجاج'.
This is a key practical takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بالقرآن دم الجمع بين النسكين قراناً كان أو تمتعاً كما صرح به غاية البيان لكن بالإذن المتقدم. وأطلق في دم الجناية فشمل دم الجماع ودم جزاء الصيد ودم الحلق ودم لبس المخيط والطيب ودم المجاوزة بغير إحرام وإنما وجب على المأمور وحده باعتبار أنه تعلق بجنايته لكن في الجناية بالجماع تفصيل إن كان قبل الوقوف ضمن جميع النفقة لأنه صار مخالفاً بالإفساد، وإن بعده فلا ضمان والدم على المأمور على كل حال. وإذا فسد حجه لزمه الحج من قابل بمال نفسه وفيه ما تقدم من التردد في وقوعه عن الأمر ولو أتم الحج إلا طواف الزيارة فرجع ولم يطفه فهو حرام على النساء ويعود بنفقة نفسه ويقضي ما بقي عليه لأنه جان في هذه الصورة، أما لو مات بعد الوقوف قبل الطواف جاز عن الآمر لأنه أدى الركن الأعظم. كذا قالوا، وقد قدمنا في أول كتاب الحج فيه بحثاً وأعظمية أمرها إنما هو ا للأمن من الإفساد بعده لا لأنه يكفي فيجب على الأمر الإحجاج. وفي فتح القدير : وأما دم رفض النسك ولا يتحقق ذلك إذا تحقق إلا في مال الحاج ولا يبعد لو فرض أنه أمره بحجتين معاً ففعل حتى ارتفضت إحداهما كونه على الآمر ولم أره والله سبحانه أعلم ا اهـ.
And he intended by 'al-Quran' the blood of combining the two rituals, whether Qiran or Tamattu', as clarified by Ghayat al-Bayan, but with prior permission. And he spoke generally in the blood of transgression, so it includes the blood of intercourse, the blood of game compensation, the blood of shaving, the blood of wearing stitched garments and perfume, and the blood of passing Miqat without Ihram. And it is only obligatory upon the agent alone because it is related to his transgression, but in the transgression of intercourse there is detail: if it was before Wuquf, he guarantees all expenses because he became a violator by invalidation; and if after, no guarantee, and the blood is upon the agent in all cases. And if his Hajj becomes invalid, he must perform Hajj next year with his own money, and in it is the previous hesitation about it being valid for the principal. And if he completed Hajj except Tawaf al-Ziyarah and returned without performing it, he is forbidden to women and returns with his own expenses and makes up what remains upon him because he is a transgressor in this case. But if he died after Wuquf before Tawaf, it is valid for the principal because he performed the greatest pillar. Thus they said, and we have presented in the beginning of the book of Hajj a discussion about it, and the gravity of its matter is for security from invalidation afterward, not because it suffices, so it is obligatory upon the principal to provide Hajj. And in Fath al-Qadir: As for the blood of abandoning the ritual, it does not occur unless it occurs in the wealth of the pilgrim, and it is not far if we suppose he ordered him to perform two Hajjs together and he did so until one of them was abandoned, it would be upon the principal, but I have not seen it, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the consequences when an agent (ma'mur) invalidates the Hajj he is performing on behalf of another (amir). It begins by explaining that the 'blood' mentioned in the context of combining two rituals (Qiran or Tamattu') is obligatory only with prior permission from the principal. Then it discusses various types of 'blood of transgression' (dam al-jinaya) including intercourse, hunting, shaving, wearing stitched garments, and passing the miqat without ihram. These are all the agent's responsibility because they stem from his own actions. In the case of intercourse, if it occurs before Wuquf, the agent must guarantee all expenses because he has invalidated the Hajj; if after, he does not guarantee expenses but still must offer the blood sacrifice. The key ruling: if the agent's Hajj becomes invalid (fasad), he must repeat it the following year with his own money, and there is disagreement (taraddud) whether this repetition counts for the principal or not. The passage then addresses a scenario where the agent performs everything except Tawaf al-Ziyarah and returns home; he remains in ihram (forbidden to women), must return at his own expense, and complete what remains. If he dies after Wuquf but before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, his Hajj is valid for the principal because he performed the essential pillar (Wuquf). The author notes that earlier in the book he discussed whether the principal is obligated to provide another Hajj; the relied-upon view is that the principal must do so because the invalidation was accidental. A quote from Fath al-Qadir introduces a novel scenario: if the agent was ordered to perform two Hajjs simultaneously and abandoned one, the blood for abandonment might be on the principal, but this is not seen in the texts.

Key Terms
دم الجناية (dam al-jinaya): Blood sacrifice owed due to a transgression committed during Hajj (e.g., wearing stitched garments, intercourse, hunting).
فساد الحج (fasad al-hajj): Invalidation of Hajj due to a major violation like sexual intercourse before Wuquf.
التردد (al-taraddud): Hesitation or unresolved dispute among scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding the agent's guarantee of expenses if he commits intercourse before Wuquf?
A) He must guarantee all expenses because he invalidated the Hajj.
B) He does not guarantee expenses, only the blood is upon him.
C) He guarantees half the expenses.
D) The principal guarantees expenses.

Key Takeaway
When an agent invalidates Hajj before Wuquf, he must repeat it with his own money, and the principal is not absolved of his obligation.

7 min
Agent Who Misses Tawaf al-Ziyarah or Dies After Wuquf
Partial performance and death of agent after Wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the rulings when an agent completes Hajj except Tawaf al-Ziyarah versus when he dies after Wuquf, and apply the concept of 'greatest pillar'.

Core Idea
Wuquf is the greatest pillar; if the agent dies after Wuquf, the Hajj is valid for the principal even if Tawaf remains undone.

The passage addresses two special cases: the agent who returns home without performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and the agent who dies after Wuquf before Tawaf. In the first case, the agent remains in ihram, must return, and is considered a transgressor. In the second, the Hajj is valid for the principal because Wuquf, the greatest pillar, was performed. This lesson also touches on a rare scenario from Fath al-Qadir about double Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: agent completes Hajj except Tawaf al-Ziyarah
The passage describes an agent who performed all of Hajj but skipped Tawaf al-Ziyarah and returned home. This is a violation.
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a pillar (rukn).
2
Determine the consequences for the agent
He is forbidden to women (haram 'ala al-nisa'), must return at his own expense, and must make up the remaining acts (Tawaf and possibly Sa'y).
He is considered a transgressor (jan).
3
Contrast with death after Wuquf
If the agent dies after Wuquf but before Tawaf, the Hajj is valid for the principal because Wuquf is the greatest pillar (al-ruknu al-a'zam).
Validity for the principal does not mean the principal's obligation is fully discharged.
4
Extract the principal's obligation after agent's death
Despite validity, the passage indicates a discussion (بحث) that the principal must still provide a Hajj (يجب على الآمر الإحجاج). So validity and sufficiency are separate.
This reflects caution (ihtiyat).
5
Note the rare case from Fath al-Qadir
If the agent was ordered to perform two Hajjs simultaneously and abandoned one, the blood might be on the principal, but this is an unverified opinion.
This is not a standard ruling.

Source Text

الركن الأعظم (al-ruknu al-a'zam): The greatest pillar of Hajj, referring to Wuquf at Arafah.

Wuquf is the greatest pillar, but even if the agent dies after it, the principal should still provide another Hajj as a precaution.

Credibility of the Agent in Hajj Performance Disputes
Determining credibility when agent and heirs disagree

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on disputes between an agent and heirs regarding Hajj performance, identify the exception for debtor agents, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A trustee is believed with his oath unless clear evidence contradicts him.

When an agent appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of a deceased person disputes with the heirs about whether the Hajj was performed or funds were spent, who is believed? The Hanafi school establishes a default rule of trusting the agent's statement with his oath, because he is a trustee. This lesson unpacks the rule, its exception, and the scholarly difference within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claims
Distinguish between the agent (ma'mur) and the heirs/executor. Understand the two possible claims: (1) the agent claims he spent money and was prevented, (2) the agent claims he performed Hajj.
2
Apply the default rule: trustee believed with oath
The general principle: the agent, as a trustee (amin), is believed with his oath when he claims discharge of his duty. The heirs' negative testimony (shahada 'ala al-nafy) is not accepted unless they prove an admission.
3
Recognize the exception for debtor agents
If the agent was also a debtor to the deceased and was ordered to use the debt for Hajj, he is not automatically believed when claiming repayment; he must provide proof.
This protects the rights of other creditors.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi sources (Khizanat al-Akmal) state that the agent's statement is only accepted with oath if there is no debt claim from the deceased's creditors. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the first view (no exception) as the relied-upon position.
The first view is supported by usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلف المأمور والورثة أو الوصي فقال وقد أنفق من مال الميت منعت من الحج وكذبه الآخر لا يصدق ويضمن إلا أن يكون أمراً ظاهراً يشهد على صدقه لأن سبب الضمان قد ظهر فلا يصدق في دفعه إلا بظاهر يدل على صدقه. ولو اختلفا فقال حججت وكذبه الآمر كان القول يدعي الخروج عن عهدة ما أمانة في يده ولا تقبل بينة الوارث أو للمأمور ببينة لأنه مع يمينه أنه كان لأنه هو يوم النحر بالبلد لأنها شهادة على النفي إلا أن يقيما على إقراره أنه لم يحج، أما لو كان الحاج مديوناً للميت أمره أن يحج بماله عليه، وباقي المسألة بحالها فإنه لا يصدق إلا يدعي قضاء الدين. هكذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي خزانة الأكمل: القول له مع يمينه إلا أن يكون للورثة مطالب بدين الميت فإنه لا يصدق في حق غريم الميت إلا بالحجة والقواعد تشهد للأول فكان عليه المعول.
And if the agent and the heirs or the executor disagree, and he says, 'I spent from the wealth of the deceased, so I was prevented from Hajj,' and the other denies him, he is not believed and must guarantee unless there is a clear matter that testifies to his truthfulness, because the cause of guarantee has become apparent, so he is not believed in its repudiation except by clear evidence indicating his truthfulness. And if they differ, he says, 'I performed Hajj,' and the principal denies him, the statement is of the claimant of discharge from the responsibility of what is a trust in his hand, and the evidence of the heir is not accepted, or for the agent with evidence because he [the agent] with his oath... because it is a testimony to negation unless they establish his acknowledgment that he did not perform Hajj. But if the pilgrim was a debtor to the deceased, and he ordered him to perform Hajj with the money owed to him, and the rest of the case remains as before, then he is not believed unless he claims repayment of the debt. Thus in many books. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: The statement is his with his oath unless the heirs have a claim of debt of the deceased, then he is not believed regarding the deceased's creditor except with proof, and the principles support the first, so it is the relied-upon.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage addresses disputes between the agent (ma'mur) and the heirs or executor (wasi) of the deceased. Two scenarios are presented: (1) The agent claims he was prevented from performing Hajj and spent money; his claim is only accepted if there is clear evidence, otherwise he must guarantee the funds. (2) The agent claims he performed the Hajj, while the principal (or heirs) deny it. The general rule is that the agent's statement is accepted with his oath, because he is a trustee (amin). The heirs' testimony to the contrary is not accepted as it is negative evidence (shahada 'ala al-nafy). However, if the heirs establish that the agent admitted he did not perform Hajj, then they prevail. There is an exception: if the agent was also a debtor to the deceased and was ordered to use that debt to perform Hajj, he is not automatically believed if he claims repayment; he must provide proof. The passage then mentions a difference of opinion: according to Khizanat al-Akmal, the agent's statement is accepted with oath unless there is a debt claim from the deceased's creditors, in which case the agent must produce proof for the creditors' sake. The author concludes that the first view (general trust) is supported by principles and is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
القول له مع يمينه (al-qawl lahu ma'a yaminih): The legal principle that the trustee's statement is accepted with his oath regarding the performance of trust duties.
شهادة على النفي (shahada 'ala al-nafy): Testimony that attempts to prove a negative (e.g., that someone did not perform an action); such testimony is generally not accepted in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when an agent claims he performed Hajj and the heirs deny it, what is the general evidentiary rule?
A) The heirs' testimony is accepted because they are the owners.
B) The agent is believed with his oath unless the heirs have clear evidence.
C) The agent must produce two male witnesses.
D) The court decides based on the majority.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over Hajj performance, the Hanafi school trusts the agent's oath unless clear evidence contradicts him, with a special rule for debtor agents.

Determining the Starting Point for Hajj on Behalf of a Deceased Who Died En Route
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj proxy starting point

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ikhtilaf on the starting point for performing Hajj on behalf of a deceased who died en route, distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn's, and apply the calculation method for successive agent deaths.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires Hajj from the deceased's hometown; Sahibayn from where he died — a difference rooted in the nature of the obligation.

This lesson unpacks a subtle ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq regarding a scenario where a person dies during Hajj travel and bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him. The passage reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples on the geographic starting point of the proxy Hajj. It also explores how the bequest's funding is calculated when agents die in succession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase
The base text states 'from his home with a third of what remains.' This can refer either to the agent dying or the testator dying. Identify both interpretations as explained by the commentator.
The pronoun ambiguity is resolved by context; the author favors the second interpretation (testator dies).
2
Distinguish the principal's status
Determine whether the person who appointed the Hajj is alive or dead at the time of the agent's death. If alive, he can appoint another from his home; if dead, the bequest's location becomes disputed.
3
State the core ikhtilaf
When the testator died after setting out for Hajj, Abu Hanifa says Hajj must be performed from his hometown. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say from where he died.
This ikhtilaf extends to the agent scenario.
4
Apply to multiple agents
Under Abu Hanifa, if successive agents die, each new agent must start from the hometown, using a third of the remaining estate each time until no funds suffice.
5
Analyze the calculation sub-ikhtilaf
Muhammad looks at what remains of the specific payment; Abu Yusuf recalculates based on the third of the entire estate. Trace the example given in the text.
The passage cuts off during Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن مات في طريقه يحج عنه من منزله بثلث ما بقي هذه العبارة تحتمل شيئين : الأول أن يكون فاعل مات المأمور بالحج فمعنى المسألة أن الوصي إذا أحج رجلاً عن الميت فمات الرجل في الطريق فإنه يحج عن الميت الموصي من منزله بثلث ما بقي من المال كله، وعلى هذا الوجه اقتصر الشارحون مع ما فيه من التعقيد في الضمائر فإن ضمير «مات» يرجع إلى المأمور، وضمير عنه ومنزله يرجع إلى الموصي الثاني أن يكون فاعل «مات» هو الموصي فيتحد مرجع الضمائر وهو صحيح فإنه إذا مات بعدما خرج حاجاً وأوصى بالحج فإنه يحج عنه من منزله بثلث تركته ويصدق عليه أنه بثلث ما بقي أي بعد الإنفاق في الطريق. فالحاصل أن الأمر إما أن يكون حياً وقت الإحجاج أو ميتاً، فإن كان حياً ومات المأمور في الطريق فإنه يحج إنساناً آخر من منزله على كل حال لأنه حي يرجع إليه، ولهذا لو أمر إنساناً بأن يحج عنه ودفع له مالاً فلم تبلغ النفقة من بلده لم يحج عنه من حيث تبلغ كالميت لأنه يمكن الرجوع إليه فيحصل الاستدراك بخلاف الميت كذا في الولوالجية. وإن كان ميتاً وأوصى بأن يحج عنه فلا يخلو إما أن يكون قدم خرج حاجا بنفسه ومات في الطريق أو لا، وفي كل منهما لا يخلو إما أن أطلق الوصية أو عين المال والمكان، فإن أوصى عنه يحج وأطلق يحج عنه من ثلث ماله لأنه بمنزلة التبرعات، فإن بلغ ثلثه أن يحج من بلده وجب الإحجاج من بلده لأن الواجب عليه الحج من بلده الذي يسكنه، وكذا إن خرج لغير الحج ومات في الطريق وأوصى . وأما إذا خرج للحج ومات في الطريق وأوصى فإنه يحج عنه من بلده عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يحج من حيث مات. وعلى هذا الخلاف المأمور في الحج إذا مات في الطريق فإنه يحج عن الموصي من منزله بثلث ما بقي من التركة، وكذا لو مات الثاني أو الثالث إلى أن لا يبقى شيء يمكن أن يحج بثلثه عند أبي حنيفة. وإن كان بأن عنه جوابه عن المقدسي قوله ويصدق عليه أنه بثلث ما بقي الخ قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن المتبادر من ثلث ما بقي يعني من التركة على أن المصنف رمز على صحة الخلاف بقوله من منزلة وبثلث ما بقي» وعلى ما ادعى لا خلاف أنه يحج عنه بثلث تركته .اهـ. والمراد بالخلاف ما سنذكره عن الفتح قوله (وعلى هذا الخلاف المأمور بالحج الخ) أي يحج عنه من منزله عنده وعندهما من حيث مات، ثم عنه عنده يحج من ثلث ما بقي. وقال محمد ينظر إن بقي من المدفوع شيء حج به وإلا بطلت الوصية. وقال أبو يوسف : إن كان المدفوع تمام الثلث كقول محمد، وإن كان بعضه يكمل فإن بلغ باقيه ما يحج به وإلا بطلت مثلاً كان المخلف أربعة آلاف دفع الوصية ألفاً فهلكت يدفع إليه ما يكفيه من ثلث الباقي أو كله وهو ألف فإن هلكت الثانية دفع إليه من ثلث الباقي بعدها هكذا مرة بعد مرة إلى أن لا يبقى ما ثلثه يبلغ الحج فيبطل وعند أبي يوسف : يأخذ ثلثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث مع تلك الألف ثلث الأربعة آلاف فإن كفت وإلا بطلت الوصية وعند محمد : إن فضل من
His statement: (If he dies on his way, Hajj is performed for him from his home with a third of what remains). This expression admits two possibilities: First, that the subject of 'dies' is the agent (ma'mur), so the meaning is that if the executor appointed a man to perform Hajj for the deceased, and the man dies on the way, then Hajj is performed for the deceased testator from his home with a third of all the remaining wealth. The commentators restricted themselves to this interpretation despite the complexity of the pronouns: the pronoun in 'he dies' refers to the agent, and the pronouns in 'for him' and 'from his home' refer to the testator. Second, that the subject of 'dies' is the testator, so the pronoun references unify; this is correct because if he dies after having set out as a pilgrim and bequeaths Hajj, then Hajj is performed for him from his home with a third of his estate, and it is true for him that it is with a third of what remains, i.e., after expenses on the road. The conclusion is that the principal (amir) is either alive at the time of appointing the Hajj or dead. If he is alive and the agent dies on the way, he appoints another person from his home in any case because he is alive and can be referred to. For this reason, if he ordered a man to perform Hajj for him and gave him money, but the expenses from his town were insufficient, Hajj is not performed from where the money suffices as in the case of a deceased, because reference back to him is possible and rectification can occur, unlike the deceased. Thus in al-Wilwaljiyya. If he is dead and bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him, then either he had set out himself as a pilgrim and died on the road or not. In each case, either he made the bequest absolute or specified the money and location. If he bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him absolutely, it is performed from a third of his wealth because it is like voluntary acts. If his third suffices for Hajj from his town, then performing Hajj from his town is obligatory because the obligation upon him was Hajj from his town where he resides. Similarly, if he set out for non-Hajj purposes and died on the road and bequeathed. But if he set out for Hajj and died on the road and bequeathed, then according to Abu Hanifa, Hajj is performed for him from his town. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Hajj is performed from where he died. On this difference, the agent in Hajj, if he dies on the way, then Hajj is performed for the testator from his home with a third of what remains of the estate. Similarly, if the second or third agent dies, until no property remains whose third can enable Hajj, according to Abu Hanifa. And if... the answer from al-Maqdisi regarding his statement 'it is true that it is with a third of what remains...' In al-Nahr: It is not hidden that the apparent meaning of 'a third of what remains' is from the estate, and that the author indicated the soundness of the ikhtilaf by his statement 'from his home' and 'with a third of what remains'. According to what he claimed, there is no ikhtilaf that Hajj is performed for him with a third of his estate. The ikhtilaf referred to is what we will mention from al-Fath. His statement: (On this ikhtilaf the agent in Hajj...) i.e., it is performed for him from his home according to him (Abu Hanifa) and according to them from where he died. Then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is performed from a third of what remains. Muhammad said: Consider if something remains from the payment given, then Hajj is performed with it, otherwise the bequest is void. Abu Yusuf said: If the payment given was the entire third, then it is like Muhammad's statement; if it was part of it, then it is completed; if what remains suffices for Hajj, then it is performed, otherwise void. For example, if the estate was 4000 and he paid 1000 as a bequest and it was lost, he pays to him what suffices from a third of the remaining, or all of it, and that is 1000. If the second payment is lost, he pays from the third of the remaining after it, and so on repeatedly until there is no longer a third sufficient for Hajj, then it becomes void. According to Abu Yusuf, he takes 333.33 along with that 1000 as a third of the 4000; if it suffices, otherwise the bequest is void. According to Muhammad, if there remains...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a complex ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the death of the agent (ma'mur) during the journey. The phrase 'from his home with a third of what remains' is ambiguous: it could refer to the agent dying (first interpretation) or the testator dying (second interpretation). The author explains both and then discusses the broader ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The key dispute: when a person dies after setting out for Hajj and bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him, Abu Hanifa says Hajj must be performed from his hometown (where he resided), while the two say it should be performed from the place where he died. This difference applies also to multiple agents dying in succession: under Abu Hanifa, each subsequent agent must start from the deceased's hometown, using a third of the remaining estate each time, until no funds suffice. The passage then details the views of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding how to determine the amount to be spent from the estate when the bequest is partially lost: Muhammad looks at what remains of the specific payment; Abu Yusuf calculates based on the third of the entire estate. The text cuts off during the explanation of Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
الحج عن الميت (al-hajj 'an al-mayyit): Performing Hajj on behalf of a deceased person as a fulfilment of his obligation.
الوصية بالحج (al-wasiyya bi al-hajj): A bequest ordering that Hajj be performed for the deceased from his estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Abu Hanifa says from his hometown; Sahibayn say from where he died.
B) Abu Hanifa says from the miqat; Sahibayn say from his hometown.
C) Both agree it is from the hometown.
D) Both agree it is from the place of death.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa holds that Hajj for a deceased must be from his hometown, while Sahibayn hold it from his place of death, affecting funding from the estate.

Interpreting Pronoun Reference in Proxy Hajj Rulings
Explaining two possible meanings of a key phrase in Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding proxy hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible referents of the pronoun in the matn phrase 'if he dies on his way' and state the resulting rulings for proxy hajj when the appointee or testator dies.

Core Idea
The pronoun's referent changes the ruling: appointee's death vs testator's death.

In Hanafi fiqh, precise understanding of pronoun references is crucial for correct rulings. This lesson explores a classic example from Kanz al-Daqa'iq where the phrase 'if he dies on his way' admits two interpretations, leading to different applications of the one-third rule in proxy hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible subjects
Read the matn phrase and note that 'māta' (died) can refer to either the appointed pilgrim (al-ma'mur) or the testator (al-muṣī).
The Arabic pronoun is ambiguous.
2
Derive the ruling for each interpretation
If the appointee dies, hajj is performed for the testator from his house with one-third of the remaining money. If the testator dies after setting out, hajj is performed for him from his house with one-third of his estate after expenses.
The 'remaining' refers to the estate after travel expenses.
3
Distinguish when the testator is alive vs dead
If the testator is alive at hiring, he can send another person if the appointee dies; if he is dead, the ruling differs as per al-Walwaljiyyah.
This distinction resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن مات في طريقه يحج عنه من منزله بثلث ما بقي) هذه العبارة تحتمل شيئين : الأول أن يكون فاعل مات المأمور بالحج فمعنى المسألة أن الوصي إذا أحج رجلاً عن الميت فمات الرجل في الطريق فإنه يحج عن الميت الموصي من منزله بثلث ما بقي من المال كله، وعلى هذا الوجه اقتصر الشارحون مع ما فيه من التعقيد في الضمائر فإن ضمير «مات» يرجع إلى المأمور، وضمير عنه ومنزله يرجع إلى الموصي الثاني أن يكون فاعل «مات» هو الموصي فيتحد مرجع الضمائر وهو صحيح فإنه إذا مات بعدما خرج حاجاً وأوصى بالحج فإنه يحج عنه من منزله بثلث تركته ويصدق عليه أنه بثلث ما بقي أي بعد الإنفاق في الطريق. فالحاصل أن الأمر إما أن يكون حياً وقت الإحجاج أو ميتاً، فإن كان حياً ومات المأمور في الطريق فإنه يحج إنساناً آخر من منزله على كل حال لأنه حي يرجع إليه، ولهذا لو أمر إنساناً بأن يحج عنه ودفع له مالاً فلم تبلغ النفقة من بلده لم يحج عنه من حيث تبلغ كالميت لأنه يمكن الرجوع إليه فيحصل الاستدراك بخلاف الميت كذا في الولوالجية.
His statement: (If he dies on his way, hajj is performed on his behalf from his house with one-third of what remains) This expression admits two possibilities: First, that the subject of 'dies' is the person commanded to perform hajj, so the meaning of the issue is that if the executor hires a man to perform hajj on behalf of the deceased, and the man dies on the way, then hajj is performed on behalf of the testator from his house with one-third of what remains of the entire wealth. The commentators limited themselves to this interpretation, despite the complexity in the pronouns, for the pronoun of 'died' refers to the commanded person, and the pronoun of 'on his behalf' and 'his house' refer to the testator. Second, that the subject of 'died' is the testator, so the reference of the pronouns is unified, and this is valid, for if he dies after having set out as a pilgrim and bequeathed hajj, then hajj is performed on his behalf from his house with one-third of his estate, and it is true regarding him that it is with one-third of what remains, i.e., after the expenditure on the road. The conclusion is that the testator is either alive at the time of hiring or dead. If he is alive and the commanded person dies on the way, then he hires another person from his house in any case, because he is alive and can be referred to. For this reason, if he commands a man to perform hajj on his behalf and pays him money, and the expenses from his town are not sufficient, hajj is not performed on his behalf from where it is sufficient, like the deceased, because it is possible to refer back to him, thus correction occurs, unlike the deceased. Thus in al-Walwaljiyyah.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a phrase from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author clarifies two possible interpretations regarding the pronoun 'he' in 'if he dies on his way'. The first interpretation is that the appointee (the person hired to perform hajj) dies, and the ruling is that hajj is performed for the testator from his home with one-third of the remaining money. The second interpretation is that the testator himself dies after setting out, and hajj is performed for him from his home with one-third of his estate. The author then summarizes the rule: if the testator is still alive when the appointee dies, he can send another person; if he is already dead, the ruling differs. The commentary emphasizes that the pronoun ambiguity is resolved by context and that both interpretations lead to valid rulings.

Key Terms
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person appointed by the executor to perform hajj on behalf of the deceased (or the living testator).
الموصي (al-muṣī): The testator who makes a will (wasiyyah) for hajj to be performed on his behalf.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the testator's estate, which is the maximum amount that can be bequeathed for charitable purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The executor dies on the way; the appointee dies on the way
C) The testator dies on the way; the executor dies on the way
D) The appointee dies on the way; the executors dies on the way

Key Takeaway
The pronoun 'he' in proxy hajj rulings can refer to either the appointee or the testator, and the correct interpretation determines the execution of the will.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Proxy Hajj Starting Point When the Testator Dies En Route
Intra-Hanafi dispute on proxy hajj location and financial management.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the starting point for proxy hajj, explain the reasoning behind each view, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: hajj from the testator's home town; Sahibayn: from where he died — the dispute affects cost and feasibility.

When a testator makes a bequest for hajj but dies en route after having set out, from where should the proxy begin the journey? This lesson examines the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on this question. The disagreement also extends to cases where multiple appointed proxies die successively, affecting how the one-third of the estate is managed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Issue
The core dispute is about the starting point for proxy hajj when the testator had already departed for hajj but died on the way. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on whether to use the testator's home town or the place of death.
The text also covers a scenario where the testator set out for a non-hajj purpose, which is treated differently.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that hajj must be performed from the testator's home town (بلده). His reasoning, though not explicitly stated in the passage, is that the obligation of hajj originated from the home town, as the testator was bound to begin his journey from there.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that hajj should be performed from the place where the testator died, as that is the location of the missed obligation.
Their reasoning likely focuses on the practical reality that the testator's intention to perform hajj effectively began from his departure point at death.
4
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence (ثمرة الخلاف) is that if the home town is far from Mecca, performing hajj from there may be more expensive than from the death location. This affects the cost, which must be covered by one-third of the estate.
Later Hanafi practice often adopts the Sahibayn's view as more practical, but the disagreement remains valid.
5
Extend to Multiple Proxy Deaths
The passage also addresses a further sub-dispute: if the appointed proxy dies en route, how should the remaining money be handled? Under Abu Hanifa, the process continues using one-third of what remains of the estate; Muhammad and Abu Yusuf differ on whether to use leftover funds or recalculate from the original estate.
This shows the depth of the intra-madhhab difference, covering both location and financial management.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان ميتاً وأوصى بأن يحج عنه فلا يخلو إما أن يكون قدم خرج حاجا بنفسه ومات في الطريق أو لا، وفي كل منهما لا يخلو إما أن أطلق الوصية أو عين المال والمكان، فإن أوصى عنه يحج وأطلق يحج عنه من ثلث ماله لأنه بمنزلة التبرعات، فإن بلغ ثلثه أن يحج من بلده وجب الإحجاج من بلده لأن الواجب عليه الحج من بلده الذي يسكنه، وكذا إن خرج لغير الحج ومات في الطريق وأوصى . وأما إذا خرج للحج ومات في الطريق وأوصى فإنه يحج عنه من بلده عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يحج من حيث مات. وعلى هذا الخلاف المأمور في الحج إذا مات في الطريق فإنه يحج عن الموصي من منزله بثلث ما بقي من التركة، وكذا لو مات الثاني أو الثالث إلى أن لا يبقى شيء يمكن أن يحج بثلثه عند أبي حنيفة. وإن كان بأن عنه جوابه عن المقدسي قوله ويصدق عليه أنه بثلث ما بقي الخ قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن المتبادر من ثلث ما بقي يعني من التركة على أن المصنف رمز على صحة الخلاف بقوله من منزلة وبثلث ما بقي» وعلى ما ادعى لا خلاف أنه يحج عنه بثلث تركته .اهـ. والمراد بالخلاف ما سنذكره عن الفتح قوله (وعلى هذا الخلاف المأمور بالحج الخ) أي يحج عنه من منزله عنده وعندهما من حيث مات، ثم عنه عنده يحج من ثلث ما بقي. وقال محمد ينظر إن بقي من المدفوع شيء حج به وإلا بطلت الوصية. وقال أبو يوسف : إن كان المدفوع تمام الثلث كقول محمد، وإن كان بعضه يكمل فإن بلغ باقيه ما يحج به وإلا بطلت مثلاً كان المخلف أربعة آلاف دفع الوصية ألفاً فهلكت يدفع إليه ما يكفيه من ثلث الباقي أو كله وهو ألف فإن هلكت الثانية دفع إليه من ثلث الباقي بعدها هكذا مرة بعد مرة إلى أن لا يبقى ما ثلثه يبلغ الحج فيبطل وعند أبي يوسف : يأخذ ثلثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث مع تلك الألف ثلث الأربعة آلاف فإن كفت وإلا بطلت الوصية وعند محمد : إن فضل من الألف الأولى ما يبلغ وإلا بطلت فالخلاف في موضعين فيما يدفع ثانياً وفي المحل الذي يجب الإحجاج منه ثانياً وتمامه في الفتح.
And if he is dead and made a bequest that hajj be performed on his behalf, then it is not free from either that he had previously set out as a pilgrim himself and died on the way or not. In each of these, it is not free from either that he made the bequest absolutely or specified the money and the place. For if he bequeathed that hajj be performed on his behalf absolutely, hajj is performed on his behalf from one-third of his wealth, because it is like voluntary donations. If one-third of it suffices for performing hajj from his town, then hiring must be done from his town, because the obligation upon him was to perform hajj from his town, which he inhabited. Similarly, if he set out for other than hajj and died on the way and made a bequest. But if he set out for hajj and died on the way and made a bequest, then hajj is performed on his behalf from his town according to Abu Hanifa. And both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He performs hajj from where he died. Based on this disagreement is the matter of the appointed person in hajj: if he dies on the way, then hajj is performed on behalf of the testator from his house with one-third of what remains of the estate. Similarly, if the second or third dies, until there remains nothing by which hajj can be performed with one-third thereof, according to Abu Hanifa. And if... [some unclear] his answer from al-Maqdisi... his statement: 'And it is true concerning him that it is with one-third of what remains...' etc. He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that the apparent meaning of 'one-third of what remains' means from the estate, since the author symbolized the validity of the disagreement by his statement 'from his house and with one-third of what remains.' Based on what he claimed, there is no disagreement that he performs hajj for him with one-third of his estate. End. And what is meant by the disagreement is what we will mention from al-Fath. His statement: (And based on this disagreement is the appointed person in hajj... etc.) i.e., he performs hajj on his behalf from his house according to him, and according to both of them from where he died. Then according to him, he performs hajj from one-third of what remains. And Muhammad said: He looks: if something remains of what was paid, he performs hajj with it; otherwise the bequest is void. And Abu Yusuf said: If what was paid is the complete one-third, it is like Muhammad's statement; but if it is part of it, it is completed. Then if what remains suffices for hajj, he performs hajj; otherwise it is void. For example, if the left wealth was four thousand, he paid one thousand as bequest, and it perished. Then he pays to him what suffices from one-third of the remaining, or all of it, which is one thousand. If the second perishes, he pays to him from one-third of the remaining after it, and so on, time after time, until there remains nothing whose one-third suffices for hajj, then it becomes void. According to Abu Yusuf, he takes three hundred and thirty-three and one-third along with that one thousand, which is one-third of the four thousand. If it suffices, otherwise the bequest is void. According to Muhammad, if something remains from the first thousand that suffices, otherwise it is void. So the disagreement is in two places: regarding what is paid secondly, and regarding the place from which hajj must be performed secondly. And its completion is in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on proxy hajj when the testator dies en route. The key disagreement is between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Hanifa holds that hajj should be performed from the testator's home town (بلده). The Sahibayn hold that it should be performed from the place where he died. This extends to the case where the appointed proxy dies multiple times: under Abu Hanifa, the hajj continues to be performed from the testator's home using the one-third of the remaining estate each time, until no more is sufficient. The text also discusses the opinions of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding how to handle the payments when the proxy dies and the money is lost or insufficient. Muhammad's view is that if any of the originally paid money remains, it is used; otherwise the bequest becomes void. Abu Yusuf qualifies this by whether the paid amount was the full one-third or part of it. The author notes that the disagreement encompasses both the amount to be paid secondarily and the location for the new proxy. The reference to 'al-Fath' indicates that the full discussion is found in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will, specifically for hajj, which is executed from one-third of the estate.
البلدة (al-baladah): The testator's home town or place of residence at the time of death.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion that can be bequeathed to non-heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Abu Yusuf regarding the financial treatment when the first payment for proxy hajj is lost and the proxy dies en route?
A) The bequest becomes void immediately.
B) He recalculates the one-third of the remaining estate and pays if it suffices.
C) He uses the original one-third of the total estate, regardless of loss.
D) He only uses whatever remains of the original payment.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on proxy hajj starting point and financial management demonstrates the school's flexibility and the importance of knowing the mufta bihi for practical application.
