6 min
Lost Expense and Recourse in Proxy Hajj
Opens with lost expense and ends with executor's right to reclaim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the proxy hajj expense is lost in Mecca and the appointee spends his own money, and explain the executor's right to reclaim funds before ihram.

Core Idea
The appointee can recover lost expenses; the executor can reclaim given money before ihram.

This lesson addresses two common scenarios in executing a hajj bequest: what happens if the allocated expense is lost, and whether the executor can take back money already given to the appointee. Understanding these rulings ensures proper execution of the deceased's will and protects the estate from unjust loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of lost expense
Note that the expense is lost in or near Mecca, or no money remains, and the appointee uses personal funds.
2
Determine the appointee's right to recourse
The appointee can claim reimbursement from the estate because the expense was the estate's obligation.
This applies only when the bequest was absolute (mutlaq).
3
Understand the executor's right to reclaim money
If the executor gave dirhams to the appointee, he can take them back as long as ihram has not been entered.
The money is a trust until the hajj rites begin.
4
Recognize the scope
These rulings are limited to cases where the bequest is absolute; specification of place or amount may alter them.
Further lessons cover specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فهلكت النفقة الخ) قال في الخانية: ولو ضاع مال النفقة بمكة أو بقرب منها أو لم يبق مال النفقة فأنفق المأمور من مال نفسه كان له أن يرجع في مال الميت . وهذا كله إذا أطلق، وأما إذا عين مكاناً اتبع لأن الإحجاج لا يجب بدون الوصية فيجب بمقدارها. وهذا كله إذا كان الثلث يكفي لحجة واحدة، فإن كان يكفي لحجج فهو على ثلاثة أقسام : إما أن يعين حجة واحدة أو يطلق أو يطلق أو يعين في كل سنة حجة ؛ ففي الأول يحج عنه واحدة وما فضل فهو لورثته، وفي الثاني خير الوصي إن شاء أحج عنه في كل سنة حجة وإن شاء أحج في سنة واحدة حججاً وهو الأفضل لأنه تعجيل تنفيذ الوصية لأنه ربما هلك المال، وفي الثالث كالثاني ولم يذكر في الأصل لأن شرط التفريق لا يفيد فصار كالإطلاق كما لو أمر الموصي رجلاً بالحج في هذه السنة فأخره المأمور إلى القابل فإه يجوز عن الميت، ولا يضمن النفقة لأن ذكر السنة للاستعجال لا للتقييد . ولو أوصى بأن يحج عنه بثلث ماله أو أطلق فهلكت النفقة في يد المأمور ؛ قال أبو حنيفة : يحج عنه بثلث ماله. وقال أبو يوسف: بما بقي من ثلث ماله. وأبطله محمد. وهذا كله إذا لم يعين الموصي قدراً فإن عين قدراً من المال فإن بلغ ذلك أن يحج عنه من بلده وجب وإلا فمن حيث يبلغ ولو عين أكثر الثلث من يحج عنه بالثلث من حيث يبلغ بخلاف الوصية بشراء عبد بأكثر من الثلث وإعتاقه عنه فإنها باطلة لأن في العتق لا يجوز النقصان عن المسمى . كذا في المحيط وغيره. وذكر الولوالجي في فتاواه: لو أوصى بأن يحج ثلث ماله ولم يقل حجة حج عنه من جميع الثلث لأنه أوصى بصرف جميع الثلث إلى الحج لأن كلمة «من» للتمييز عن أصل المال. ولو دفع الوصي الدراهم إلى رجل ليحج عن فأراد أن يسترد كان له ذلك ما لم يحرم لأن المال أمانة في يده، فإن استرده فنفقته إلى الميت.
His statement (And if the expense is lost... etc.) He said in al-Khaniyyah: And if the money for expenses is lost in Mecca or near it, or no money for expenses remains, and the appointee spends from his own money, he has the right to recourse against the estate of the deceased. And all this is if he made an absolute bequest. But if he specified a place, it is followed, because hiring for hajj is not obligatory without the bequest, so it becomes obligatory to the extent of the bequest. And all this is if one-third suffices for one hajj. If it suffices for multiple hajjs, then it is of three divisions: either he specifies one hajj, or makes an absolute bequest, or specifies a hajj every year. In the first, one hajj is performed for him and what remains is for his heirs. In the second, the executor has a choice: if he wishes, he may perform one hajj every year, and if he wishes, he may perform multiple hajjs in one year, and the latter is better because it hastens the execution of the bequest, since perhaps the wealth may perish. In the third, it is like the second, and it was not mentioned in the original because the condition of spreading does not benefit, so it becomes like an absolute bequest, just as if the testator commanded a man to perform hajj in this year, and the appointee delayed it to the next year, it is valid on behalf of the deceased, and he is not liable for the expense, because mentioning the year is for urgency, not for restriction. And if he bequeathed that hajj be performed for him with one-third of his wealth, or made an absolute bequest, and the expense is lost in the hand of the appointee, Abu Hanifa said: He performs hajj for him with one-third of his wealth. Abu Yusuf said: With what remains of his one-third. And Muhammad invalidated it. And all this is if the testator did not specify an amount. If he specified an amount of money, and if that suffices for performing hajj from his town, it is obligatory; otherwise, from where it suffices. And if he specified more than one-third, he performs hajj for him from the one-third from where it suffices, unlike the bequest to buy a slave for more than one-third and then free him on his behalf, for that is invalid, because in manumission, reduction from the named amount is not permissible. Thus in al-Muhit and others. And al-Walwalji mentioned in his Fatawa: If he bequeathed that hajj be performed with one-third of his wealth and did not say 'one hajj', hajj is performed from the entire one-third, because he bequeathed the expenditure of the entire one-third on hajj, since the word 'min' is for distinction from the principal wealth. And if the executor handed over dirhams to a man to perform hajj on behalf of the deceased, and then wished to take them back, he has that right as long as he has not entered ihram, because the money is a trust in his hand. If he takes it back, then its expense is upon the deceased.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage covers several scenarios in proxy hajj will execution. First, if the money is lost after the appointee has spent his own funds, he can recover from the estate. Second, if the testator specified a place for the hajj, it must be followed. Third, if the one-third can cover multiple hajjs, the executor has a choice: perform them sequentially or all at once (the latter being preferred as quicker execution). Fourth, if money is lost in the appointee's hands, Abu Hanifa says to perform hajj with the full one-third, Abu Yusuf says with the remaining one-third, and Muhammad invalidates the bequest entirely. Fifth, if the testator specified a certain amount less than one-third, it is used; if more than one-third, only one-third is used and must be the maximum to reach from the nearest location. Sixth, the difference from a bequest to buy a slave: if the amount is exceeded, the whole bequest is invalid for the slave case, but for hajj it is valid up to one-third. Seventh, if the testator said 'perform hajj with one-third of my wealth', the entire one-third is used for a single hajj unless specified otherwise. Finally, the executor can retrieve money given to an appointee as long as ihram has not been entered.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): The money allocated for the travel and living expenses of the proxy performing hajj.
الحرمان (al-ihram): The state of consecration for hajj; entering ihram signifies the start of the pilgrimage rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can the executor reclaim money given to the appointee for proxy hajj?
A) At any time before the hajj is completed
B) Only before the appointee enters ihram
C) Only if the appointee agrees
D) Never, because the money is a gift

Key Takeaway
The executor can reclaim money given to the appointee for proxy hajj as long as the appointee has not entered ihram.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Lost Expense in Appointee's Hands
Focuses on the ikhtilaf portion about lost expense in appointee's hands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the consequence of lost expense in the appointee's hands, and evaluate which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
If expense is lost in appointee's hands, three Hanafi imams differ: full one-third, remaining one-third, or invalid bequest.

This lesson focuses on a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement when the money for proxy hajj is lost after being given to the appointee. Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad each have distinct rulings. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for a mufti to know which opinion is operative today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The testator bequeaths hajj with one-third of his wealth, or makes an absolute bequest, but the expense is lost in the appointee's hands.
This is after giving the money to the appointee, not a general loss.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa says: perform hajj with the full one-third, as if the loss did not occur.
The bequest remains valid; the loss is on the estate.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf says: perform hajj with what remains of the one-third after the loss.
The loss reduces the available funds, so only the remainder is used.
4
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad says: the bequest is invalid (batil) because the expense is lost.
The bequest fails entirely.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The later preference is for Abu Hanifa's or Abu Yusuf's view; Muhammad's view is considered weak.
Tarjih is based on the principle that a loss should not invalidate the bequest.

Source Text

Specification of Place, Amount, and Multiple Hajj Cycles
Covers specification of place, amount, and multiple hajjs, and contrast with slave bequest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for executing a hajj bequest when the testator specifies a place, an amount, or multiple hajjs, and distinguish the ruling from a slave bequest situation.

Core Idea
Specification of place, amount, or number of hajjs must be followed; if one-third covers multiple hajjs, the executor can choose to do them all at once or yearly.

This lesson handles the details of executing a hajj bequest when the testator provides specific instructions. Whether he specifies the location of departure, the exact amount to be spent, or the number of hajjs, the executor must follow the testator's wishes within the limits of the one-third. The passage also compares a hajj bequest to a bequest for purchasing and freeing a slave, highlighting a key difference.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish absolute vs. specified bequest
If the testator specifies a place (e.g., 'from his town'), it must be followed. If he specifies an amount (less than one-third), that amount is used.
If the specified amount exceeds one-third, only one-third is used from the nearest location.
2
Multiple hajjs when one-third suffices for more than one
Identify the three divisions: (1) specifies one hajj, (2) absolute, (3) specifies a hajj every year.
In case (2), the executor has a choice: perform one per year or multiple in one year.
3
Override when condition of spreading is ineffective
If the testator says 'hajj every year' but the condition does not benefit, it becomes like an absolute bequest.
Condition is for urgency, not restriction.
4
Specification of amount and its limit
If the testator specifies an amount equal to or less than one-third, use it. If more than one-third, use the full one-third from the nearest point.
This contrasts with a slave bequest where the entire gift becomes invalid if the amount is exceeded.
5
Interpretation of 'hajj with one-third of my wealth'
Al-Walwalji: if the testator says this without specifying one hajj, the entire one-third is used for a single hajj.
The word 'min' indicates the source, not a limit.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

In the second, the executor has a choice: if he wishes, he may perform one hajj every year, and if he wishes, he may perform multiple hajjs in one year, and the latter is better because it hastens the execution of the bequest, since perhaps the wealth may perish. In the third, it is like the second, and it was not mentioned in the original because the condition of spreading does not benefit, so it becomes like an absolute bequest, just as if the testator commanded a man to perform hajj in this year, and the appointee delayed it to the next year, it is valid on behalf of the deceased, and he is not liable for the expense, because mentioning the year is for urgency, not for restriction. And if he bequeathed that hajj be performed for him with one-third of his wealth, or made an absolute bequest, and the expense is lost in the hand of the appointee, Abu Hanifa said: He performs hajj for him with one-third of his wealth. Abu Yusuf said: With what remains of his one-third. And Muhammad invalidated it. And all this is if the testator did not specify an amount. If he specified an amount of money, and if that suffices for performing hajj from his town, it is obligatory; otherwise, from where it suffices. And if he specified more than one-third, he performs hajj for him from the one-third from where it suffices, unlike the bequest to buy a slave for more than one-third and then free him on his behalf, for that is invalid, because in manumission, reduction from the named amount is not permissible. Thus in al-Muhit and others. And al-Walwalji mentioned in his Fatawa: If he bequeathed that hajj be performed with one-third of his wealth and did not say 'one hajj', hajj is performed from the entire one-third, because he bequeathed the expenditure of the entire one-third on hajj, since the word 'min' is for distinction from the principal wealth. And if the executor handed over dirhams to a man to perform hajj on behalf of the deceased, and then wished to take them back, he has that right as long as he has not entered ihram, because the money is a trust in his hand. If he takes it back, then its expense is upon the deceased.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage covers several scenarios in proxy hajj will execution. First, if the money is lost after the appointee has spent his own funds, he can recover from the estate. Second, if the testator specified a place for the hajj, it must be followed. Third, if the one-third can cover multiple hajjs, the executor has a choice: perform them sequentially or all at once (the latter being preferred as quicker execution). Fourth, if money is lost in the appointee's hands, Abu Hanifa says to perform hajj with the full one-third, Abu Yusuf says with the remaining one-third, and Muhammad invalidates the bequest entirely. Fifth, if the testator specified a certain amount less than one-third, it is used; if more than one-third, only one-third is used and must be the maximum to reach from the nearest location. Sixth, the difference from a bequest to buy a slave: if the amount is exceeded, the whole bequest is invalid for the slave case, but for hajj it is valid up to one-third. Seventh, if the testator said 'perform hajj with one-third of my wealth', the entire one-third is used for a single hajj unless specified otherwise. Finally, the executor can retrieve money given to an appointee as long as ihram has not been entered.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): The money allocated for the travel and living expenses of the proxy performing hajj.
الإطلاق (al-itlaq): An absolute bequest without specification of place, amount, or number of hajjs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the testator specifies a hajj every year, what is the ruling?
A) The executor must perform one hajj per year for the specified number of years.
B) The executor cannot perform more than one hajj per year.
C) The condition of spreading does not benefit, so the bequest is treated as absolute.
D) The bequest is invalid because conditions are not allowed in hajj wills.

Key Takeaway
Specifications in a hajj bequest must be followed, but a condition like 'every year' is not binding and the executor can perform multiple hajjs in one year.

The Location for Performing Hajj on Behalf of the Deceased
Establishing the ruling for the place from which the deceased's Hajj should be performed and the executor's liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the place from which a deceased's Hajj must be performed, identify the executor's liability if he violates the will, and apply the exception for close locations and insufficient funds.

Core Idea
The deceased's Hajj must be performed from the nearest homeland to Makkah; the executor deviating at his own cost.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical issue in performing Hajj on behalf of a deceased person: the location. The default rule is certainty—use the nearest homeland. The executor must follow this; otherwise, he becomes liable. However, necessity allows flexibility when funds are insufficient or the location is very close.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deceased's status
Determine whether the deceased had a homeland (watan) or not. If yes, the Hajj must be performed from the nearest of those homelands to Makkah. If no homeland, it is performed from the place of death.
One homeland is considered; multiple homelands require choosing the nearest to Makkah.
2
Apply the example of a Makkan dying elsewhere
If the deceased is a Makkan but dies elsewhere (e.g., Kufa), the Hajj must be performed from Makkah, not from the place of death. However, if the will specifies a Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah), it must be performed from the miqat (e.g., Kufa) because starting Ihram from Makkah is invalid for Qiran.
The principle of certainty (yaqin) governs: the nearest homeland ensures discharge of obligation.
3
Determine the executor's liability for deviation
If the executor performs Hajj from a place other than the deceased's homeland when it is possible to do so from the homeland using one-third of the estate, the executor becomes liable. The Hajj performed counts as his own, and he must perform another Hajj for the deceased at his own expense.
Liability (daman) attaches because the executor violated the will without necessity.
4
Identify the exception for close locations
If the place from which the executor performs is so close to the homeland that one can go and return before nightfall, the executor is not liable. The Hajj is considered valid for the deceased.
Proximity makes the location essentially equivalent to the homeland.
5
Apply istihsan for insufficient funds
If one-third of the estate is insufficient to cover the cost of Hajj from the homeland, the executor should perform it from wherever the available funds suffice. This is by istihsan (juristic preference) to fulfill the will as much as possible.
Istihsan overrides the default rule because the purpose of the will is prioritized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الحج عن الغير للموصي أوطان عنه من أقرب أوطانه إلى مكة لأنه متيقن به وإن لم يكن له وطن فمن حج عنه من حيث مات فلو مات مكي بالكوفة وأوصى بحجة حج مكة وإن أوصى بالقران قرن من الكوفة لأنه لا يصح من مكة، فإن أحج عنه الوصي من غير وطنه مع ما يمكن الإحجاج من وطنه من ثلث ماله فإن الوصي يكون ضامناً ويكون الحج له ويحج عن الميت ثانياً إلا إذا كان المكان الذي أحج منه قريباً إلى وطنه من حيث يبلغ إليه ويرجع إلى الوطن قبل الليل، فحينئذ لا يكون ضامناً مخالفاً. هذا كله إن بلغ ثلث ماله فإن لم يبلغ الإحجاج من بلده حج عنه من حيث يبلغ استحساناً
Book of Hajj, Chapter: Hajj on behalf of another. For the testator who has homelands, [the Hajj should be performed] from the nearest of his homelands to Makkah because that is certain. If he has no homeland, then from where he dies. So if a Makkan dies in Kufa and wills a Hajj, he should be performed Hajj from Makkah. If he wills a Qiran, he should perform Qiran from Kufa because it is not valid from Makkah. If the executor performs Hajj on his behalf from other than his homeland while it is possible to perform from his homeland from one-third of his wealth, then the executor becomes liable, and the Hajj is for him [the executor], and he must perform Hajj for the deceased a second time, unless the place from which he performed is near his homeland such that he arrives and returns before night—then he is not liable for the violation. All this if one-third of his wealth suffices. If it is not sufficient to perform Hajj from his homeland, then he should perform Hajj from where it suffices, by istihsan.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on the place from which a deceased person's Hajj should be performed when a will has been made for it. The author begins by stating that if the person had a homeland (watan), the Hajj must be performed from the nearest homeland to Makkah, because certainty is achieved in fulfilling the obligation. If there is no known homeland, the Hajj is performed from the place of death. The example given: if a Makkan dies in Kufa and wills a Hajj, the Hajj must be performed from Makkah, not Kufa, because the person is considered a Makkan. If he wills a Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah), the Qiran should be performed from Kufa because starting the Hajj from Makkah is not valid for a Qiran (the Ihram for Qiran must be from the miqat). The text then discusses the executor (wasi). If the executor performs the Hajj from a place other than the deceased's homeland, even though it was possible to do so from the homeland from one-third of the estate, the executor becomes liable (damin). The Hajj performed counts as the executor's own Hajj, and he must perform a second Hajj for the deceased. However, there is an exception: if the place from which he performed is so close to the homeland that the traveler can go there and return before night, then the executor is not liable. This exception is based on the closeness to the homeland. Finally, the passage mentions the case when one-third of the estate is insufficient to perform the Hajj from the deceased's homeland. In such a case, the Hajj should be performed from wherever the available funds suffice, by way of istihsan (juristic preference). Istihsan here overrides the default rule of performing from the homeland because the purpose of fulfilling the will is prioritized.

Key Terms
الحج عن الغير (al-hajj 'an al-ghayr): Performing the pilgrimage to Makkah on behalf of another person, usually a deceased person who was obligated but unable to perform it before death.
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor of a will, entrusted with carrying out the deceased's testamentary instructions, including arranging for Hajj.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability; here, the executor becomes financially responsible if he violates the will by performing Hajj from a different location without necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person from Makkah dies in Kufa and wills a Hajj, from which place should the Hajj be performed?
A) From Kufa, because that is where he died
B) From Makkah, because it is his homeland and closer
C) From any place the executor chooses
D) From the nearest miqat

Key Takeaway
The nearest homeland to Makkah is the default location for a deceased's Hajj; deviation incurs executor liability unless the alternative location is near or the funds are insufficient.

Hajj Will After Loss of Funds: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj will when funds are lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on executing a Hajj will when the expense money is lost and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When the Hajj expense money is lost, the three Hanafi imams differ: perform with full one-third, with what remains, or void the will.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a will for Hajj when the allocated funds are lost before the journey. The three eponymous imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—offer distinct rulings. Understanding their reasoning is essential for grasping the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The will is made for Hajj from one-third of the estate, and the expense money (nafaqa) is lost while with the appointee.
2
List the three positions
State each imam's view: Abu Hanifa (full one-third), Abu Yusuf (remaining amount), Muhammad (invalidation).
3
Note the key distinction
The text clarifies that this dispute applies only when the testator did not specify a fixed amount. If an amount was specified, different rules apply.
4
Understand the analogy with slave purchase
The passage draws a contrast with a will to buy a slave worth more than one-third and manumit him, which is void because manumission requires the full amount.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
How does each position affect the estate and the heirs? In practice, if Abu Hanifa's view is followed, the executor must use a new one-third; if Abu Yusuf's, only the remaining part; if Muhammad's, the will is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أوصى بأن يحج عنه بثلث ماله أو أطلق فهلكت النفقة في يد المأمور؛ قال أبو حنيفة: يحج عنه بثلث ماله. وقال أبو يوسف: بما بقي من ثلث ماله. وأبطله محمد. وهذا كله إذا لم يعين الموصي قدراً فإن عين قدراً من المال فإن بلغ ذلك أن يحج عنه من بلده وجب وإلا فمن حيث يبلغ ولو عين أكثر الثلث من يحج عنه بالثلث من حيث يبلغ بخلاف الوصية بشراء عبد بأكثر من الثلث وإعتاقه عنه فإنها باطلة لأن في العتق لا يجوز النقصان عن المسمى. كذا في المحيط وغيره.
And if he willed that Hajj be performed on his behalf with one-third of his wealth, or he made an absolute will, and the expense money perished in the hand of the appointee: Abu Hanifa said: He performs Hajj on his behalf with one-third of his wealth. Abu Yusuf said: With what remains of one-third of his wealth. And Muhammad invalidated it. And all this is if the testator did not specify an amount. If he specified an amount from the wealth, then if that amount suffices for performing Hajj from his homeland, it is obligatory; otherwise, from where it suffices. And if he specified more than one-third, he performs Hajj on his behalf with one-third from where it suffices, contrary to the will to buy a slave for more than one-third and manumit him, which is void because in manumission, reduction from the named amount is not permitted. Thus in Al-Muhit and others.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when money set aside for a deceased's Hajj is lost. The scenario: a person wills that a Hajj be performed on his behalf from one-third of his wealth, or he makes an absolute will (without specifying the amount). The expenses (nafaqa) are given to an appointee (ma'mur), but the money is lost before the Hajj is performed. Three opinions are given: Abu Hanifa holds that the Hajj should be performed with the original one-third amount (i.e., the will is still valid, and the executor must use a new one-third from the estate). Abu Yusuf says to use whatever remains of the one-third (i.e., if part was lost, use the remainder). Muhammad invalidates the will entirely (the obligation is aborted). The text then explains that these differences apply when the testator did not specify a particular amount. If an amount was specified, then if that amount suffices for Hajj from the homeland, it must be done; otherwise, from where it suffices. If the specified amount exceeds one-third, the executor is limited to one-third and should perform Hajj from a place affordable with one-third. This is distinguished from a will to buy a slave worth more than one-third and then free him—such a will is batil (void) because manumission requires the full value, and one cannot reduce it. The passage references Al-Muhit and other sources. The practical consequence of this khilaf is that depending on which imam's view is followed, the Hajj may or may not be performed, and the heirs' rights differ.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): The expenses allocated for the Hajj journey, including travel costs and provisions.
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person appointed by the executor or the will to actually perform the Hajj on behalf of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Imam Muhammad regarding a will for Hajj when the expense money is lost?
A) The Hajj must be performed with the original one-third
B) The Hajj should be performed with what remains of the one-third
C) The will is invalidated
D) The executor must use his own money

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the fate of a Hajj will when funds are lost depends on which imam's view is followed: it may be performed fully, partially, or voided.

Dismissal of a Hajj Proxy and Expense Allocation
Rulings on expense allocation when a Hajj proxy is dismissed, and executor's authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on who bears the expense when a Hajj agent is dismissed, and identify when the executor may perform Hajj himself.

Core Idea
Expense liability for a dismissed Hajj agent depends on the reason for dismissal: fault, no cause, or benefit of deceased.

When a person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another is dismissed, the allocation of expenses incurred is not uniform. It depends on the reason for dismissal and the executor's role. This lesson examines the three scenarios outlined in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and the subsidiary rulings from Fath al-Qadir and al-Zahiriyya concerning the executor's own authority and the validity of the bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three dismissal scenarios
List the three causes for dismissal: treachery, no cause, and incompetence/ignorance.
The passage explicitly sets these apart.
2
Determine expense liability for each
For each scenario, state who bears the expense: agent's own wealth, executor's own wealth, or deceased's estate.
The ruling is strict: fault of agent → agent pays; no fault → executor pays; benefit of deceased → estate pays.
3
Examine the executor's authority to perform Hajj
From Fath al-Qadir, note when the executor may perform Hajj himself: only if he is not an heir and the testator did not specify another person.
If the testator said 'pay the money to someone,' the executor cannot do it himself.
4
Apply the rule on insufficient bequest
If the bequest (one-third of estate) is insufficient to cover Hajj expenses, the bequest becomes void.
This is from al-Zahiriyya and serves as a boundary condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بلده على من تكون إن استرد بخيانة ظهرت منه فالنفقة في ماله خاصة، وإن استرد لا بخيانة ولا تهمة فالنفقة على الوصي في ماله خاصة، وإن استرد لضعف رأي فيه أو لجهله بأمور المناسك فأراد الدفع إلى أصلح منه فنفقته في مال الميت لأنه استرد لمنفعة الميت اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: لو أوصى أن يحج عنه ولم يزد على ذلك كان للوصي أن يحج بنفسه إلا أن يكون وارثاً، وإن دفعه إلى وارث ليحج فإنه لا يجوز إلا أن تجيز الورثة وهم كبار لأن هذا كالتبرع بالمال فلا يصح للوارث إلا بإجازة الباقين ولو قال الميت للوصي ادفع المال لمن يحج عني لم يجز له أن يحج بنفسه مطلقاً. وفي الظهيرية : ولو كان ثلث ماله قدر ما لا يمكن الإحجاج عنه بطلت الوصية.
His city? depends on who it is: if he is dismissed due to treachery that appeared from him, then the expense is from his own wealth specifically. And if he is dismissed without treachery or suspicion, then the expense is on the executor from his own wealth specifically. And if he is dismissed due to weakness of opinion in him or his ignorance of the matters of the rites, and he wanted to pay to someone more suitable, then his expense is from the deceased's wealth because he dismissed him for the benefit of the deceased. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: If he bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him and did not add to that, the executor may perform Hajj himself unless he is an heir. And if he pays it to an heir to perform Hajj, it is not permissible unless the heirs who are major consent, because this is like donating wealth, so it is not valid for an heir except with the permission of the rest. And if the deceased said to the executor: 'Pay the money to someone who will perform Hajj for me,' it is not permissible for him to perform Hajj himself absolutely. And in al-Zahiriyya: If his third of the property is of an amount that cannot enable Hajj to be performed for him, the bequest is void.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the legal rulings concerning the dismissal of a person appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of someone else. The author presents three scenarios: First, if the appointed agent is dismissed due to proven treachery (khiyanah), the expenses he incurred are from his own wealth, as he was at fault. Second, if he is dismissed without any treachery or even suspicion, the expenses fall on the executor (wasi) personally, because the dismissal was for no reason. Third, if the dismissal is due to the agent's incompetence or ignorance of Hajj rituals, and the executor appoints a more suitable person, then the expenses are from the deceased's estate because the dismissal was to benefit the deceased. The passage then quotes from Fath al-Qadir rulings on executors: an executor may perform Hajj himself unless he is an heir; paying an heir to perform Hajj requires consent of other major heirs; and if the testator specifically instructs to pay the money to someone, the executor cannot do it himself. Finally, from al-Zahiriyya, if the bequest amount is insufficient to cover Hajj expenses, the bequest is void.

Key Terms
الاسترداد (al-istirdād): Dismissal of an appointed agent or proxy, returning the task to the executor.
الوصي (al-waṣī): Executor of a will, appointed by the testator to manage the bequest and perform tasks like Hajj on behalf of the deceased.
ثلث المال (thulth al-māl): One-third of the deceased's estate, the maximum that can be bequeathed for non-heirs in Hanafi law.
الوصية (al-waṣiyyah): The bequest or will; in this context, the instruction to perform Hajj on behalf of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the executor dismisses the appointed Hajj agent due to the agent's ignorance of the rituals, on whom does the expense fall?
A) On the agent himself
B) On the executor from his own wealth
C) On the deceased's estate
D) On the heir who inherits

Key Takeaway
The expense liability for a dismissed Hajj agent varies with the reason for dismissal, and the executor's own authority to perform Hajj depends on whether he is an heir and the testator's explicit instructions.

Son's Hajj for Father: Reimbursement and Validity
Ruling on son performing Hajj for father with intention to reclaim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a son's performance of Hajj for his deceased father is valid and explain the ruling on reimbursement from the estate.

Core Idea
Hajj for a deceased is valid only if the performer seeks reimbursement; voluntary performance does not fulfill the deceased's obligation.

The famous Hanafi text al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a case: a man bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him, and his son does so. The ruling depends on the son's intention regarding reimbursement. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its basis in the deceased's purpose of gaining reward through spending.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between a son performing Hajj with the intention to reclaim from the estate, and performing it without that intention (voluntarily).
2
Understand the basis for validity
The validity for the deceased depends on achieving the deceased's purpose: reward from spending. If the son does not reclaim, no spending occurs from the deceased's side.
The text says: 'لأنه لم يصحل مقصود الميت وهو ثواب الإنفاق'
3
Compare with debt payment
The ruling is analogous to paying a debt voluntarily: it is valid because the debt is discharged regardless of intention. But Hajj requires expenditure, so intention matters.
Debt: 'قضاء الدين بغير أمره في حالة الحياة يجوز فكذا بعد الموت'
4
Extend to zakah and kaffarah
The same principle applies to zakah and kaffarah: voluntary performance without reclaiming does not fulfill the obligation.
The text says: 'وعلى هذا الزكاة والكفارة'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التجنيس : رجل أوصى بأن يحج عنه فحج عنه ابنه ليرجع في التركة فإنه يجوز كالدين إذا قضاه من مال نفسه، ولو حج على أن لا يرجع فإنه لا يجوز عن الميت لأنه لم يصحل مقصود الميت وهو ثواب الإنفاق، وعلى هذا الزكاة والكفارة، ومثله لو قضي عنه دينه متطوعاً جاز لأن الحج عن الكبير العاجز بغير أمره لا يجوز وقضاء الدين بغير أمره في حالة الحياة يجوز فكذا بعد الموت رجل مات وعليه حجة الإسلام فحج عنه رجل بإذنه ولم ينو فرضاً ولا نفلاً فإنه يجوز عن حجة الإسلام، ولو نوى تطوعاً لا يجوز عن حجة الإسلام اهـ. وفي عمدة الفتاوى للصدر الشهيد لو قال حجوا من ثلثي حجتين يكتفي بواحدة والباقي للورثة إن فضل .اهـ. وهو مشكل على ما تقدم من المحيط والولوالجية وهو مبني على الفرق : أن بين الثلث وبين يوصي بجميع الثلث. وذكر في آخر من الوصايا : لو أوصى بأن يحج عنه بالألف من ماله فأحج الوصي من مال نفسه ليرجع ليس له ذلك لأن الوصية باللفظ فيعتبر لفظ الموصي وهو أضاف المال إلى نفسه فلا يبدل اهـ. وفي العدة: امرأة تركت مهرها على الزوج ليحج بها وحج بها فعليه المهر لأنه بمنزلة الرشوة وهي حرام .اهـ.
And in al-Tajnīs: A man bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him; his son performed Hajj for him intending to reclaim from the estate; it is permissible, like a debt if he paid it from his own wealth. But if he performed Hajj intending not to reclaim, it is not valid for the deceased, because the deceased's purpose—the reward of spending—was not achieved. And similarly for zakāt and kaffārah. Similarly, if someone paid his debt voluntarily, it is valid, because performing Hajj for an elderly incapable person without his order is not valid, but paying a debt without his order during life is valid; likewise after death. A man died owing Hajj al-Islam; another man performed Hajj for him with his permission without intending obligatory or voluntary; it counts for Hajj al-Islam. But if he intended voluntary, it does not count for Hajj al-Islam. End. And in 'Umdat al-Fatāwā of al-Sadr al-Shahīd: If he said 'Perform two Hajjs from my third,' one suffices, and the remainder goes to the heirs if any. End. This is problematic based on what preceded from al-Muhīt and al-Walwālijiyya; it is based on the difference between giving a third and bequeathing all of the third. And it is mentioned at the end of al-Waṣāyā: If he bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him with one thousand from his wealth, and the executor performed Hajj from his own wealth intending to reclaim, he does not have that right, because the bequest is by wording, so the testator's words are considered, and he attributed the wealth to himself, so it cannot be changed. End. And in al-'Uddah: A woman left her dowry with her husband to perform Hajj with it, and he performed Hajj with it; the dowry is due upon him because it is like a bribe, which is forbidden. End.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq collects several rulings related to performing Hajj on behalf of another, especially regarding reimbursement. The first ruling from al-Tajnīs: if a son performs Hajj for his father with the intention of reclaiming expenses from the estate, it is valid and he may reclaim, just as one who pays a debt from his own pocket can reclaim. But if he performs Hajj voluntarily without intention to reclaim, it does not benefit the deceased because the deceased's purpose was to gain reward through spending, and that is lost. This analogy extends to zakāt and kaffārah. The passage then mentions a case where a man dies owing Hajj al-Islam, and another performs it with permission; if he does not specify intention (whether obligatory or voluntary), it counts as the obligatory Hajj. But if he intends voluntary, it does not. The next ruling from 'Umdat al-Fatāwā: if someone bequests that 'two Hajjs be performed from my third,' only one is required, and any remaining wealth goes to the heirs. The author notes this is problematic and explains it depends on the distinction between donating the third itself versus bequeathing all of the third. Then from al-Waṣāyā: if the testator specifies 'from his wealth,' the executor cannot perform Hajj from his own money and reclaim; the testator's wording limits the source. Finally, from al-'Uddah: if a woman leaves her mahr (dowry) with her husband to perform Hajj, and he does so, he owes the mahr because it constitutes a bribe, which is haram.

Key Terms
التركة (al-tarikah): The estate of the deceased, from which expenses and debts are paid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a son performs Hajj for his father without intending to reclaim expenses from the estate, what is the ruling?
A) It is valid and the son can still reclaim
B) It is valid for the deceased but the son does not reclaim
C) It is not valid for the deceased
D) It is invalid unless the father explicitly ordered it

Key Takeaway
The validity of Hajj performed for a deceased depends on achieving the deceased's purpose of reward through expenditure; intention to reclaim is essential.

Hajj for Deceased: Intention Determines Obligatory or Voluntary
Ruling on performer's intention when performing Hajj for deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a Hajj performed on behalf of a deceased counts as the obligatory Hajj based on the performer's intention.

Core Idea
If the performer does not specify intention, the Hajj counts as obligatory; if he intends voluntary, it does not.

The passage addresses a scenario where a man dies owing Hajj al-Islam, and another person performs Hajj with his permission. The ruling hinges on the performer's state of mind: if he does not specify whether it is obligatory or voluntary, it is accepted as the obligatory Hajj; but if he explicitly intends voluntary, it does not fulfill the deceased's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the deceased's status
The deceased owed Hajj al-Islam (obligatory Hajj). Another person performs Hajj with the deceased's permission (given during life or by executor).
2
Consider the two scenarios of intention
If the performer does not have a specific intention (neither fard nor nafl), the Hajj is valid for the deceased's obligatory Hajj. If he intends nafl (voluntary), it does not count for the obligation.
Text: 'لم ينو فرضاً ولا نفلاً فإنه يجوز عن حجة الإسلام، ولو نوى تطوعاً لا يجوز'
3
Understand the rationale
The default when performing with permission is that it is for the deceased's obligation; a voluntary intention overrides that default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
حجة الإسلام (Hajjat al-Islam): The obligatory Hajj that every able Muslim must perform once in a lifetime.

D) It is valid only if the deceased was wealthy

Key Takeaway
The performer's intention determines whether Hajj on behalf of a deceased fulfills the obligatory Hajj or counts as voluntary.

Bequest for Multiple Hajjs from One-Third: One Suffices
Ruling on bequest to perform two Hajjs from one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a bequest for multiple Hajjs from one-third is interpreted as requiring only one Hajj, with the remainder to heirs.

Core Idea
If a testator says 'perform two Hajjs from my third,' only one is required, and the surplus goes to heirs.

Al-Sadr al-Shahid in 'Umdat al-Fatāwā addresses a bequest: 'Perform two Hajjs from my third.' The ruling is that only one Hajj is sufficient, and any leftover wealth returns to the heirs. This is based on a distinction between donating the third itself versus bequeathing all of the third.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest
The testator says 'Perform two Hajjs from my third.' The third refers to one-third of the estate, permissible for bequests to non-heirs.
2
Understand the ruling
Only one Hajj needs to be performed; the remainder of the third (if any) goes to the heirs.
Text: 'يكتفي بواحدة والباقي للورثة إن فضل'
3
Note the problematic nature
The author notes this is problematic based on earlier texts (al-Muhīt and al-Walwālijiyya) and explains it rests on a distinction: between giving the third as a donation and bequeathing all of the third.
It is built on the difference between donating the third and bequeathing all of the third.

Source Text

Executor Cannot Substitute Own Money if Testator Specified 'From His Wealth'
Ruling on executor using own money when testator specified 'from his wealth'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an executor cannot perform a bequest from his own money and seek reimbursement when the testator specified the source as 'from his wealth'.

Core Idea
If the testator says 'perform Hajj from his wealth', the executor must use the testator's money, not his own, even with intent to reclaim.

The passage from the end of al-Waṣāyā addresses a scenario where a testator bequeaths that Hajj be performed for him with one thousand from his wealth. The executor performs the Hajj from his own money intending to reclaim. The ruling is that this is not permissible because the testator's wording specifies the source, which cannot be changed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and action
Testator: 'Perform Hajj for me with one thousand from my wealth.' Executor uses his own money intending to reclaim from estate.
2
Understand the ruling
The executor does not have the right to do this; he cannot reclaim from the estate because the testator's words ('from my wealth') are binding.
Text: 'ليس له ذلك لأن الوصية باللفظ فيعتبر لفظ الموصي وهو أضاف المال إلى نفسه فلا يبدل'
3
Grasp the rationale
The bequest is verbal; the testator's specification of the source (his wealth) must be respected. The executor cannot substitute his own money and later claim reimbursement.
Changing the source would alter the testator's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The author notes this is problematic and explains it depends on the distinction between donating the third itself versus bequeathing all of the third. Then from al-Waṣāyā: if the testator specifies 'from his wealth,' the executor cannot perform Hajj from his own money and reclaim; the testator's wording limits the source. Finally, from al-'Uddah: if a woman leaves her mahr (dowry) with her husband to perform Hajj, and he does so, he owes the mahr because it constitutes a bribe, which is haram.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): Bequest; a legal declaration by a person regarding the disposal of his property after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator says 'perform Hajj with one thousand from his wealth,' can the executor perform from his own money and reclaim?
A) Yes, because the act is done
B) Yes, with permission of heirs
C) No, because the testator's wording is binding
D) No, because the executor must be a relative

Key Takeaway
The testator's specification of the source in a bequest is binding; the executor cannot substitute his own funds.

Woman's Mahr Used for Hajj by Husband: Ruling
Ruling on husband using wife's mahr for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that if a woman leaves her mahr with her husband to perform Hajj, and he does so, the mahr is still due as a debt because it constitutes a bribe.

Core Idea
Using a woman's mahr for Hajj without her true consent is like a bribe; the husband owes the mahr.

The passage from al-'Uddah addresses a case where a woman leaves her mahr (dowry) with her husband to perform Hajj. The husband performs Hajj with that money. The ruling is that the husband still owes the mahr to the wife because the arrangement is akin to a bribe, which is forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A woman leaves her mahr with her husband to perform Hajj. The husband performs Hajj using the mahr money.
2
Understand the ruling
The husband is still liable to pay the mahr. The act is considered a bribe (rishwa), which is haram.
Text: 'فعليه المهر لأنه بمنزلة الرشوة وهي حرام'
3
Grasp the rationale
The mahr is the wife's property; using it to benefit the husband (even for a pious act) without clear, voluntary consent is problematic. The transaction is tainted as a bribe because the husband uses the wife's money to fulfill his own religious duty (if he had permission) or as a corrupt inducement.
The husband performing Hajj with the wife's money may be seen as a benefit to him, making it akin to a bribe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التجنيس : رجل أوصى بأن يحج عنه فحج عنه ابنه ليرجع في التركة فإنه يجوز كالدين إذا قضاه من مال نفسه، ولو حج على أن لا يرجع فإنه لا يجوز عن الميت لأنه لم يصحل مقصود الميت وهو ثواب الإنفاق، وعلى هذا الزكاة والكفارة، ومثله لو قضي عنه دينه متطوعاً جاز لأن الحج عن الكبير العاجز بغير أمره لا يجوز وقضاء الدين بغير أمره في حالة الحياة يجوز فكذا بعد الموت رجل مات وعليه حجة الإسلام فحج عنه رجل بإذنه ولم ينو فرضاً ولا نفلاً فإنه يجوز عن حجة الإسلام، ولو نوى تطوعاً لا يجوز عن حجة الإسلام اهـ. وفي عمدة الفتاوى للصدر الشهيد لو قال حجوا من ثلثي حجتين يكتفي بواحدة والباقي للورثة إن فضل .اهـ. وهو مشكل على ما تقدم من المحيط والولوالجية وهو مبني على الفرق : أن بين الثلث وبين يوصي بجميع الثلث. وذكر في آخر من الوصايا : لو أوصى بأن يحج عنه بالألف من ماله فأحج الوصي من مال نفسه ليرجع ليس له ذلك لأن الوصية باللفظ فيعتبر لفظ الموصي وهو أضاف المال إلى نفسه فلا يبدل اهـ. وفي العدة: امرأة تركت مهرها على الزوج ليحج بها وحج بها فعليه المهر لأنه بمنزلة الرشوة وهي حرام .اهـ.
And in al-Tajnīs: A man bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him; his son performed Hajj for him intending to reclaim from the estate; it is permissible, like a debt if he paid it from his own wealth. But if he performed Hajj intending not to reclaim, it is not valid for the deceased, because the deceased's purpose—the reward of spending—was not achieved. And similarly for zakāt and kaffārah. Similarly, if someone paid his debt voluntarily, it is valid, because performing Hajj for an elderly incapable person without his order is not valid, but paying a debt without his order during life is valid; likewise after death. A man died owing Hajj al-Islam; another man performed Hajj for him with his permission without intending obligatory or voluntary; it counts for Hajj al-Islam. But if he intended voluntary, it does not count for Hajj al-Islam. End. And in 'Umdat al-Fatāwā of al-Sadr al-Shahīd: If he said 'Perform two Hajjs from my third,' one suffices, and the remainder goes to the heirs if any. End. This is problematic based on what preceded from al-Muhīt and al-Walwālijiyya; it is based on the difference between giving a third and bequeathing all of the third. And it is mentioned at the end of al-Waṣāyā: If he bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him with one thousand from his wealth, and the executor performed Hajj from his own wealth intending to reclaim, he does not have that right, because the bequest is by wording, so the testator's words are considered, and he attributed the wealth to himself, so it cannot be changed. End. And in al-'Uddah: A woman left her dowry with her husband to perform Hajj with it, and he performed Hajj with it; the dowry is due upon him because it is like a bribe, which is forbidden. End.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq collects several rulings related to performing Hajj on behalf of another, especially regarding reimbursement. The first ruling from al-Tajnīs: if a son performs Hajj for his father with the intention of reclaiming expenses from the estate, it is valid and he may reclaim, just as one who pays a debt from his own pocket can reclaim. But if he performs Hajj voluntarily without intention to reclaim, it does not benefit the deceased because the deceased's purpose was to gain reward through spending, and that is lost. This analogy extends to zakāt and kaffārah. The passage then mentions a case where a man dies owing Hajj al-Islam, and another performs it with permission; if he does not specify intention (whether obligatory or voluntary), it counts as the obligatory Hajj. But if he intends voluntary, it does not. The next ruling from 'Umdat al-Fatāwā: if someone bequests that 'two Hajjs be performed from my third,' only one is required, and any remaining wealth goes to the heirs. The author notes this is problematic and explains it depends on the distinction between donating the third itself versus bequeathing all of the third. Then from al-Waṣāyā: if the testator specifies 'from his wealth,' the executor cannot perform Hajj from his own money and reclaim; the testator's wording limits the source. Finally, from al-'Uddah: if a woman leaves her mahr (dowry) with her husband to perform Hajj, and he does so, he owes the mahr because it constitutes a bribe, which is haram.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): Dowry given by husband to wife, obligatory in marriage.
الرشوة (al-rishwa): Bribe; something given to influence a decision or action illegitimately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a woman leaves her mahr with her husband to perform Hajj, and he does so, what is the ruling on the mahr?
A) The husband owes the mahr
B) The mahr is considered a gift
C) The mahr is forfeited
D) The mahr goes to the wife's heirs

Key Takeaway
A conditional arrangement where the wife's mahr is used for the husband's Hajj is akin to a bribe; the husband remains liable for the mahr.

Hiring for Hajj: Invalid Contract, Expense Reimbursement Only
Detailed discussion on permissibility of hiring for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring for Hajj, explain why the 'wage' is actually expense reimbursement, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute over Qādīkhān's terminology.

Core Idea
Hiring for Hajj is invalid; the agent receives only expense reimbursement, not a wage, because worship requires personal intention.

The Hanafi school firmly holds that hiring someone to perform Hajj or any act of worship is invalid, as worship requires personal intention. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its practical consequences. You'll examine the key dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding whether the 'wage' is a true wage or merely reimbursement, and explore the exceptions allowed for teaching and leading prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Hiring for Hajj (isti'jar). What is the Hanafi hukm? It is invalid (la yajuz). Confirm this from the text: 'لا يجوز الاستئجار على الحج ولا على شيء من الطاعات'.
The ruling applies to all acts of obedience (ta'at).
2
Trace the practical consequences if hiring occurs anyway
Even if a hiring contract is made and the agent performs Hajj, what happens? The Hajj is valid for the deceased, but the agent only receives travel expenses (nafaqat al-mithl), not the full wage. Any surplus is returned to the heirs. Understand why: because the contract is void, the payment is not a wage but reimbursement.
The agent does not get the contracted 'ujr; only actual expenses.
3
Analyze the dispute over Qādīkhān's wording
Qādīkhān used the term 'ujr al-mithl (like wage). How did the majority respond? They clarified he meant nafaqat al-mithl (like expense), due to rhetorical similarity. Why is this distinction important? Because 'ujr implies a valid hiring, while nafaqah does not. Understand the response to objections on this point.
The issue is semantic but has legal consequences.
4
Examine the exceptions
What acts are excepted from the prohibition? Teaching Qur'an, fiqh, leading prayers (imāma), and adhān. These are considered permissible to hire for. Why? Because they are not purely devotional? Note the textual support from al-Matn, al-Mukhtār, etc.
Exceptions are limited; Hajj is not among them.
5
Consider the evidence from authoritative Hanafi texts
The author cites multiple reliable sources (al-Matn, al-Mukhtār, al-Majma') to reinforce the prohibition. Recognize that the burden of proof is on those who claim permissibility, and the author refutes the lone opinion of al-Qahustānī.
The majority view is well-established; isolated opinions are not relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

على الورثة لأنه لا يجوز الاستئجار عليه، ولا يحل له أن يأخذ الفضل لنفسه إلا إذا تبرع الورثة به وهم من أهل التبرع، أو أوصى الميت بأن الفضل للحاج. وقال بعض مشايخنا لا تجوز هذه الوصية لأن الموصى له مجهول إلا أن الأول أصح لأن الموصى له يصير معروفاً بالحج كما لو أوصى بشراء عبد بغير عينه ويعتق ويعطى له مائة درهم فإنها جائزة. وقال بعضهم : لا تجوز اهـ. وأراد المصنف بموته في الطريق موته قبل الوقوف بعرفة ولو الأرحام فتبطل بالموت ويرجع المال إلى الورثة اهـ. ذكر أن ما ينفقه المأمور إنما هو على حكم ملك الميت لأنه لو كان ملكه لكان بالاستئجار ولا يجوز الاستئجار على الطاعات، وعن هذا قلنا لو أوصى أن يحج عنه ولم يزد على ذلك إلى آخر المسألة التي قدمها المؤلف عنه ثم قال : وإذا علم هذا فما في فتاوى قاضيخان من قوله «إذا استأجر المحبوس رجلاً ليحج عنه حجة الإسلام جازت الحجة عن المحبوس إذا مات في الحبس وللأجير أجر ينتفع به المستأجر. هذا وإنما جاز الحج عنه لأنه لما بطلت الإجارة بقي الأمر بالحج فتكون له نفقة مثله .اهـ. وأجيب عن قاضيخان بأنه أراد ما قاله الحاكم . عبر عن نفقة المثل بأجر المثل لمشاكلة صفة العبارة المناسبة للفظ الإجارة، واعترض بأن المشاكلة إنما تحسن في المقامات الخطابية لا في إفادة الأحكام الشرعية قيل : وينبغي جواز الاستئجار بناء على المفتي به من جواز الاستئجار على الطاعات .اهـ. وفيه نظر يظهر رد الزائد من النفقة إلا بالشرط السابق ومنها اشتراط الإنفاق مال الأمر أو أكثره وغيرها مما يظهر للمتأمل المتتبع إذ لو صحت الإجارة لما لزم شيء من ذلك . هذا ما ظهر لي والله تعالى أعلم
And al-Asbījābī mentioned that hiring for Hajj is not permissible, nor for any acts of obedience. So if someone is hired for Hajj and the wage is paid to him, and he performs Hajj for the deceased, it is valid for the deceased, and he gets from the wage the amount of the expenses of the road going and coming, and he returns the surplus to the heirs, because hiring for it is not permissible. And it is not lawful for him to take the surplus for himself unless the heirs donate it and they are people of donation, or the deceased bequeathed that the surplus goes to the pilgrim. And some of our scholars said: This bequest is not permissible because the legatee is unknown, except that the first view is more correct because the legatee becomes known by performing Hajj, just as if one bequeaths to buy an unspecified slave and free him and give him one hundred dirhams—it is permissible. And some said: It is not permissible. End. And the author intended by his death on the road: his death before standing at 'Arafah, even if he was in Mecca. And in al-Muhīt: If he gave money to a man to perform Hajj for him, and he entered ihram for Hajj, then the orderer died, the heirs may take what remains of the money with him and make him liable for what he spent after his death. And the heirs are not like the orderer in this, because the expense of Hajj is like the expense of relatives through women, so it is invalidated by death, and the money returns to the heirs. End. It is mentioned that what the appointed person spends is under the ruling of the deceased's ownership, because if it were his own ownership, it would be by hiring, and hiring for acts of obedience is not permissible. And from this we said: If he bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him and did not add more, up to the end of the issue that the author presented about him. Then he said: And when this is known, what is in Fatāwā Qādīkhān from his statement: 'If a imprisoned man hires a man to perform Hajj al-Islam for him, the Hajj is valid for the imprisoned if he dies in prison, and the hired man gets his like wage' is problematic? No, what is in al-Kāfī of al-Hākim Abī al-Fadl on this issue said: He gets his like expense, confirmed. And he added clarification in al-Mabsūṭ: This expense he does not deserve by way of compensation but by way of sufficiency, because he devoted himself to a work from which the hirer benefits. This, and the Hajj is valid for him because when the hiring became invalid, the command to perform Hajj remained, so he gets his like expense. End. And the answer about Qādīkhān is that he meant what al-Hākim said; he used 'like wage' for 'like expense' due to the similarity of the expression suitable for the term 'hiring'. And it was objected that similarity is only good in rhetorical contexts, not in conveying legal rulings. It was said: Hiring should be permitted based on what is given as fatwa of the permissibility of hiring for acts of obedience. End. And there is consideration in it, as appears from what we presented at the beginning of the chapter. And it is stated in al-Matn, al-Mukhtār, al-Mawāhib, al-Majma', and other reliable texts that it is not permissible for Hajj and other acts of obedience. Al-Matn excepted teaching the Qur'an; Sadr al-Sharī'ah added fiqh; al-Majma' and al-Mukhtār added imāma; some added the adhān. And the four are collected in Matn al-Tanwīr. And al-Shurnubālālī stated in his treatise Bulūgh al-Arab that he did not find any of our scholars permitting hiring for Hajj. And what is said that al-Qahustānī stated it is incorrect; rather, the beginning of his speech may give that impression, but the reasoning removes it, as is known from referring to it. And even if it were accepted, one who is famous for being alone is not considered; just as what al-Zāhidī alone is not considered. Moreover, if it were correct, it would necessitate the demolition of many branches, such as ... this is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed discussion on the permissibility of hiring someone to perform Hajj (isti'jar). The Hanafi school's established position is that hiring for acts of worship like Hajj is not valid because worship requires personal intention (niyyah) and cannot be delegated by contract. However, if a person is given money to perform Hajj and does so, it counts for the deceased, but the hired person only receives the actual travel expenses, not the full wage; any surplus must be returned to the heirs. A dispute among later scholars: Qādīkhān used the term 'like wage' (ujr al-mithl), but the majority clarify it means 'like expense' (nafaqat al-mithl), as explained by al-Hākim. The passage also discusses the fate of expenses if the orderer dies during the journey: the heirs reclaim unused money. The author strongly defends the prohibition of hiring for Hajj, citing multiple reliable texts (al-Matn, al-Mukhtār, etc.) and refuting any contrary claims. Exceptions are made only for teaching Qur'an, fiqh, leading prayers (imāma), and adhān, as per some scholars.

Key Terms
الاستئجار (al-isti'jār): Hiring someone to perform a task for a specified wage; used in context of hiring for Hajj or other acts.
نفقة المثل (nafaqat al-mithl): The equivalent expense, not a contractual wage; given to the person who performed Hajj as reimbursement for actual costs.
الإجارة (al-ijārah): A contract of hire for services; in this context, invalid for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The surplus if the heirs donate it

Key Takeaway
Hiring for Hajj is invalid in the Hanafi school; the agent receives only expense reimbursement, not a wage, and any surplus must be returned to the heirs.

Validity of Ihram on Behalf of Parents
Ruling statement from Kanz al-Daqā'iq affirming validity of proxy Hajj for parents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that entering ihram for Hajj on behalf of one's parents is valid and explain that the reward is intended for them.

Core Idea
Hajj performed on behalf of parents is valid because the reward is transferable to them.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqā'iq establishes a key rule in Hanafi fiqh: performing Hajj on behalf of another person—specifically one's parents—is valid. The basis is that the pilgrim intends the reward for them, and reward can be transferred. This ruling is part of the broader topic of proxy Hajj (al-hajj 'an al-ghayr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Determine exactly what action is being ruled upon. Here, it is entering ihram for Hajj on behalf of one's parents.
2
State the Ruling
The text states it is valid (sahīh). Confirm this from the Arabic: 'فعين صح'.
3
Understand the Reason
The validity rests on the intention to transfer the reward to the parents. The rewards of worship can be dedicated to others.
This principle is affirmed elsewhere in Hanafi fiqh, e.g., giving charity on behalf of the deceased.
4
Identify the Scope
The ruling here specifically mentions parents, but by extension, proxy Hajj for other deceased or incapable persons is also valid if properly intended.
Conditions apply: the person being represented must be Muslim and unable to perform Hajj themselves (deceased or physically incapable).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن أهل بحج عن أبويه فعين صح) قال في
His statement: (And whoever enters ihram for Hajj on behalf of his parents, then it is valid.) He said in [the commentary]...
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This brief snippet from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is the beginning of the commentary on a line from Kanz al-Daqā'iq. The matn states that if a person enters ihram for Hajj on behalf of his parents (i.e., performing Hajj on their behalf), it is valid. The reason is that he intends the reward for them, and the reward can be transferred to others. The commentary continues to explain the conditions and details, but the OCR ends here. In the Hanafi school, performing Hajj on behalf of another is valid if the person being represented is deceased or incapable, and the person performing the Hajj must intend to represent them. The ruling here confirms its validity for parents.

Key Terms
أهل بحج (ahalla bi-hajj): Entered the state of ihram for Hajj, indicating the commencement of the pilgrimage rites.
عن أبويه (an abawayhi): On behalf of his parents, i.e., performing the Hajj for them as a proxy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Invalid because the intention must be for oneself

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Surplus Funds for a Deceased Pilgrim Agent
Ruling with proof on surplus funds for a deceased Hajj agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on surplus travel funds when a hired Hajj agent dies, and apply the exceptions (heirs' donation or testator's bequest) to determine who receives the surplus.

Core Idea
Surplus from a deceased Hajj agent's fee returns to heirs; the agent keeps only actual expenses.

This lesson deals with a practical scenario: you hire someone to perform Hajj on behalf of a deceased relative, but the agent dies en route. What happens to the leftover money? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that hiring for acts of worship is impermissible, making the agent a trustee of the funds. The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the basic rule and the exceptions: the agent may keep the surplus only if the heirs donate it or if the deceased bequeathed it. It also addresses a disagreement among Hanafi scholars about the validity of such a bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties
The case involves a hirer (employer) who gave money to an agent to perform Hajj on his behalf. The agent dies before completing the Hajj (before standing at Arafah). The question: what happens to the surplus money after deducting travel expenses?
The agent is considered a trustee, not a hired wage-earner, because hiring for Hajj is not valid in the Hanafi school.
2
State the ruling for the surplus
The agent is entitled only to the actual expenses for going and coming back. The surplus must be returned to the heirs of the employer (the hirer). The agent cannot keep it for himself.
This is based on the principle that the agent acts voluntarily (tatawwu') and the money is a trust (amanah).
3
Recognize the exceptions
The agent (or his heirs) may keep the surplus only if: (a) the employer's heirs donate the surplus to the agent, provided they are legally competent to donate, OR (b) the employer bequeathed in his will that the surplus should go to the agent.
If the bequest is valid, the surplus becomes a gift from the estate, not payment for Hajj.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the bequest's validity
Some early Hanafi scholars said the bequest is invalid because the legatee (the agent) is unknown at the time of the will. The preferred view (al-awlah) is that it is valid, because the agent becomes known through the act of Hajj, analogous to a bequest to purchase an unspecified slave, emancipate him, and give him money.
The analogy (qiyas) shows that uncertainty about identity is resolved by the subsequent action.
5
Understand the reasoning from al-Muhit
If the employer dies after the agent has entered ihram, the heirs can take the remaining money and hold the agent liable for what he spent after the death. This is because the expense of Hajj becomes void upon the employer's death, similar to expenses for relatives by marriage (which cease upon death).
This reinforces that the agency terminates at death; the agent is a trustee for any unspent funds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الميت وله من الأجر مقدار نفقة الطريق في الذهاب والمجيء ويرد الفضل على الورثة لأنه لا يجوز الاستئجار عليه، ولا يحل له أن يأخذ الفضل لنفسه إلا إذا تبرع الورثة به وهم من أهل التبرع، أو أوصى الميت بأن الفضل للحاج. وقال بعض مشايخنا لا تجوز هذه الوصية لأن الموصى له مجهول إلا أن الأول أصح لأن الموصى له يصير معروفاً بالحج كما لو أوصى بشراء عبد بغير عينه ويعتق ويعطى له مائة درهم فإنها جائزة. وقال بعضهم : لا تجوز اهـ. وأراد المصنف بموته في الطريق موته قبل الوقوف بعرفة ولو كان بمكة وفي المحيط : ولو دفع إلى رجل مالاً ليحج به عنه فأهل يحجة ثم مات الآمر فللورثة أن يأخذوا ما بقي من المال معه ويضمنونه ما أنفق منه بعد موته ولا يشبه الورثة الآمر في هذا لأن نفقة الحج كنفقة ذوي الأرحام فتبطل بالموت ويرجع المال إلى الورثة اهـ.
The deceased [agent] has from the fee the amount of travel expenses for going and coming, and the surplus is returned to the heirs because hiring for it is not permissible. It is not lawful for him to take the surplus for himself unless the heirs donate it—and they are qualified to donate—or the deceased bequeathed that the surplus be for the pilgrim. Some of our shaykhs said: This bequest is not valid because the legatee is unknown, but the first opinion is more correct because the legatee becomes known through the Hajj, just as if one bequeaths to purchase a slave without specification and emancipate him and give him one hundred dirhams, that is valid. And some said: It is not valid, end. The author intended by 'his death on the way' his death before standing at Arafah, even if he were in Mecca. And in al-Muhit: If one gave money to a man to perform Hajj on his behalf, and he entered ihram for Hajj, then the commander died, then the heirs may take what remains of the money with him and they hold him liable for what he spent after his death, and the heirs are not like the commander in this because the expense of Hajj is like the expense of relatives by marriage, so it becomes void upon death, and the money returns to the heirs, end.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses the scenario where a person hires an agent to perform Hajj on his behalf, and the agent dies en route. The ruling: the agent is entitled only to the actual travel expenses (going and returning). Any surplus must be returned to the heirs of the deceased employer. The agent may not keep the surplus for himself unless the heirs donate it (and they are legally competent to do so) or the deceased had explicitly bequeathed the surplus to the agent. There is a disagreement among Hanafi scholars about the validity of such a bequest: some say it is invalid because the legatee (the agent) is unknown at the time of the bequest, but the preferred opinion (al-awlah) is that it is valid because the identity becomes known through the act of Hajj, analogous to bequeathing to purchase an unspecified slave and then emancipate him and give him money. The author clarifies that 'death on the way' means before standing at Arafah, even if in Mecca. The text from al-Muhit adds: if the employer dies after the agent has entered ihram, the heirs may take the remaining money and hold the agent liable for what he spent after the death, because the expense of Hajj becomes void upon the employer's death, similar to expenses for relatives by marriage, so the money reverts to the estate.

Key Terms
الفضل (al-fadl): The surplus money remaining after deducting actual travel expenses from the fee given to the pilgrim agent.
الاستئجار على الطاعات (al-isti'jar 'ala al-ta'at): Hiring a person to perform an act of worship (like Hajj) for payment.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest made by a testator that becomes effective after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a bequest by the employer that the surplus of the Hajj agent fee should go to the agent?
A) Invalid because the agent is unknown at the time of the will.
B) Valid only if the agent performed the Hajj successfully.
C) The preferred view is valid, analogous to a bequest for purchasing an unspecified slave.
D) Valid only if the agent is a relative of the employer.

Key Takeaway
The surplus from a deceased Hajj agent's fee must be returned to the employer's heirs unless the heirs donate it or the employer validly bequeathed it to the agent.
