Ambiguous Intention and Post-Performance Specification in Hajj
Explaining the validity of specifying the beneficiary after ambiguous intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying the beneficiary of Hajj after an ambiguous intention, and distinguish it from contradictory intention during ihram.

Core Idea
An ambiguous intention for two persons is void, but specifying after performance is valid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a subtle point: if someone intends to perform Hajj on behalf of two persons (e.g., both parents) without specifying which one, the intention for both is void because it is contradictory. However, after completing the Hajj, he may validly assign the reward to one of them. This flexibility does not apply if he entered ihram with a specific intention and then changed it; that would be invalid. The key principle is that specification after ambiguity is not a condition; the act itself is valid and the reward can be redirected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The act is performing Hajj with the intention to dedicate it to two persons simultaneously. The Hanafi ruling is that such an intention is void (laghw) because it is contradictory—one cannot physically act for two different persons with a single intention.
The intention for both is void, but the Hajj itself may still be valid if the person had a valid intention for his own act? Actually, the text implies the Hajj is valid because he can later assign the reward.
2
Determine the post-performance option
After completing the Hajj, the person may assign the reward to either of the two persons. This is valid and permissible according to the text.
This shows that the ambiguity does not render the entire act invalid; rather, it only affects the initial intention's effect.
3
Compare with the contradictory intention during ihram
The text contrasts this with a case where someone entered ihram on behalf of a specific commander (i.e., with a clear intention), then later specified a different person. That is invalid because it contradicts the original intention.
The key difference: in the first case, the intention was ambiguous from the start; in the second, it was clear but then changed, which is a break of consistency.
4
Extract the principle
The author deduces that specification after ambiguity is not a condition (shart). Rather, the ruling is derived a fortiori: if one can redirect the reward to one person after making it for both, then keeping it for both is even more appropriate.
This principle helps in analogous cases in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد الأداء فالنية قبله لهما لغو ، فإذا فرغ وجعله لأحدهما أولهما فإنه يجوز بخلاف ما إذا أهل عن آمريه ثم عين لما تقدم أنه صار مخالفاً. وبهذا علم أن التعيين بعد الإبهام ليس بشرط وإنما ذكره ليعلم منه حكم عدم التعيين بالأولى لأنه بعد أن جعله لهما يملك صرفه أحدهما عن فلأن يبقيه لهما أولى.
After performance, the intention before it for both is void. So when he finishes and assigns it to one of them, his first is that it is permissible, unlike if he assumed ihram for his two commanders then specified, because it was previously stated that he became contradictory. And by this it is known that specification after ambiguity is not a condition; rather he mentioned it to derive from it the ruling of non-specification a fortiori, because after he has made it for both, he has the power to direct it to one of them, so it is more appropriate that he keeps it for both.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling on someone who intends Hajj on behalf of two persons ambiguously. The author states that if one performs Hajj with the intention that it is for both (e.g., parents) without specifying, the intention for both is void because it is contradictory. However, after completing the Hajj, he may assign the reward to either one, and this is valid. This is unlike the case where he entered ihram on behalf of a specific commander, then changed his mind—that is not valid because it contradicts his original intent. The key principle is that specification after ambiguity is not a condition; the rule is deduced a fortiori: if he can direct the reward to one after making it for both, then keeping it for both is even more appropriate.

Key Terms
نيته لهما لغو (niyyatuhu lahumā laghw): The intention for both is void/ invalid because it is contradictory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on assigning the reward after performing Hajj with an ambiguous intention for two persons?
A) It is not allowed because the intention was void.
B) It is permissible to assign it to either one.
C) The reward must be split equally.
D) The Hajj must be repeated with a clear intention.

Key Takeaway
An ambiguous intention for two persons in Hajj is void, but the act is valid and the reward can be assigned to either after performance.

Voluntary Hajj by Heir Without Will: Ruling and Proof
Comparing the ruling of a stranger and a heir performing Hajj voluntarily

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary Hajj by an heir without a will and explain the proof from the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah.

Core Idea
Voluntary Hajj by an heir without will suffices, but its acceptance rests with Allah.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from Abu Hanifa regarding an heir performing Hajj voluntarily for a deceased who left no will. The passage compares this to a stranger's voluntary Hajj and draws on the famous hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah. We will unpack the proof and the significant qualification 'insha' Allah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is an heir voluntarily performing Hajj (or hiring someone) for a deceased who did not leave a will for obligatory Hajj. The ruling from Abu Hanifa is that it suffices (yujzi') with the qualification 'insha' Allah'.
This is contrasted with the case where the deceased left a will for Hajj, in which case voluntary performance by the heir is invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, where the Prophet likened performing Hajj on behalf of another to repaying a debt.
This hadith is a khabar al-wahid (single-narrator hadith), which Hanafis accept for establishing rules of action.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's analogy establishes that, just as a voluntary repayment of a debt by an heir is valid, so too is voluntary performance of Hajj. The central link is that both involve discharging an obligation or fulfilling a duty on behalf of another.
4
Note the ikhtilaf in interpretation of 'insha' Allah'
Scholars differ on the meaning of the qualification. Al-Mabsut holds it relates to the uncertainty of acceptance by Allah (i.e., whether the Hajj is accepted). Al-Walwālijī holds it relates to acceptance by the family (analogous to a creditor's discretion in accepting repayment). Both agree the permissibility itself is certain.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the Hajj suffices, and the qualification concerns acceptance, not validity. This is based on the strength of the analogy to debt.
The reliance on khabar al-wahid for action and the need for caution in matters of divine acceptance justify the qualification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا علم أن الأجنبي كالوارث في هذا فإن من تبرع عن أجنبيين بالحج فهو كالولد عن الأبوين لأن المجعول إنما هو الثواب فله أن يجعله لمن شاء. وعلم أيضاً أنه في الوارث المتبرع من غير وصية، أما إذا أوصى بحجة الفرض فتبرع الوارث بالحج فقد قدمنا أنه لا يجوز. وإن لم يوص فتبرع الوارث إما بالحج بنفسه أو بالإحجاج عنه رجلاً فقد قال أبو حنيفة : يجزئه إن شاء الله تعالى لحديث الخثعمية فإنه شبهه بدين العباد وفيه لو قضى الوارث من غير وصية يجزئه فكذا هذا وفي المبسوط : فإن قيل فقد أطلق أبو حنيفة الجواب في كثير من الأحكام الثابتة بخبر الواحد ولم يقيده بالمشيئة قلنا: إن خبر الواحد يوجب العمل فيما طريقه العمل فأطلق الجواب فيه، فأما سقوط حجة الإسلام عن الميت بأداء الورثة طريقه العلم فإنه أمر بينه وبين ربه تعالى فلهذا قيد الجواب بالاستثناء اهـ. وذكر الولوالجي أن قوله إن شاء الله تعالى على القبول لا على الجواز لأنه شبهه بقضاء الدين، ومن تبرع بقضاء دين رجل كان صاحب الدين بالخيار إن شاء قبل وإن شاء لم يقبل فكذا في باب الحج اهـ .
And by this it is known that the stranger is like the heir in this matter. For if someone voluntarily performs Hajj on behalf of two strangers, it is like a son on behalf of parents, because what is assigned is only the reward; so he may assign it to whomever he wishes. It is also known that it applies to the heir who volunteers without a will. As for if he bequeaths the obligatory Hajj, and the heir volunteers to perform it, we have already stated that it is not valid. But if he did not bequeath, and the heir volunteers either by performing Hajj himself or hiring a man to perform it on his behalf, Abu Hanifa said: It suffices him, Allah willing, due to the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, for he likened it to the debt of servants. And in it: If the heir discharges a debt without a will, it suffices. So likewise this. And in al-Mabsut: If it is said: Abu Hanifa gave an absolute answer in many rulings established by khabar al-wahid and did not qualify it with 'mashiyyah', we say: Khabar al-wahid necessitates action in matters whose way is action, so he gave an absolute answer. As for the dropping of the Hajj of Islam from the deceased by the performance of the heirs, its way is knowledge, for it is a matter between him and his Lord, so he qualified the answer with the exception. And al-Walwālijī mentioned that his saying 'Allah willing' pertains to acceptance, not permissibility, because he likened it to the repayment of debt. Anyone who voluntarily repays a person's debt, the creditor has the choice: if he wishes, he accepts, and if he wishes, he does not. Similarly in the chapter of Hajj.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage draws an analogy between a stranger and an heir regarding performing Hajj voluntarily on behalf of another. The author explains that if someone voluntarily performs Hajj for two strangers, it is like a son performing for parents because the reward can be assigned to any beneficiary. The key distinction is whether the deceased left a will for Hajj: if so, the heir's voluntary performance is invalid because it contravenes the specified executor. Without a will, the heir may perform Hajj himself or hire someone, and Abu Hanifa rules it suffices with the qualification 'Allah willing' (insha' Allah). This qualification is explained differently: al-Mabsut states it is due to the uncertainty of acceptance in the sight of Allah, as the matter is between the deceased and his Lord. Al-Walwālijī interprets it as referring to acceptance by the deceased's family or creditor analogy, not permissibility. The proof is the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah where the Prophet likened Hajj on behalf of the deceased to repaying a debt.

Key Terms
الخثعمية (al-Khath'amiyyah): A famous hadith where a woman asked about performing Hajj for her father, and the Prophet said to perform it for him, likening it to repaying a debt.
يُجْزِئُهُ (yujzi'uhu): It suffices him; meaning the act is valid and fulfills the obligation.
المشيئة (al-mashiyyah): The will of Allah; used in the qualification 'insha' Allah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if an heir performs Hajj voluntarily for a deceased who did not leave a will?
A) It is not valid because the heir cannot act without explicit permission.
B) It suffices, but with the qualification 'if Allah wills'.
C) It suffices absolutely without any qualification.
D) It is only valid if the heir performs Hajj himself, not by hiring.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary Hajj by an heir without a will is valid and suffices; the qualification 'insha' Allah' relates to divine acceptance, not permissibility.

Ruling on Hiring a Novice (Sarrurah) for Hajj
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hiring a novice for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on hiring a novice for Hajj and distinguish the degree of dislike for the hirer versus the hired agent.

Core Idea
Hiring a novice is permissible but disliked: tanzih for the hirer, tahrim for the agent who delays his own Hajj.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute about hiring a person who has not yet performed his own obligatory Hajj. The author reconciles two seemingly conflicting positions by distinguishing between the degree of dislike for the hirer and the agent. Understanding this nuanced ruling sharpens your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence and practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? It is hiring someone (ajir) to perform Hajj on behalf of another when the hired person has not performed his own Hajj. The initial ruling from the matn is that it is permissible (ja’iz) but disliked (makruh).
The term 'sarrurah' (novice) refers to anyone who has never performed Hajj.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement on the type of dislike: Fath al-Qadir (al-Marghinani) says it is karahah tahrīmiyyah (prohibition-level) due to ahadith prohibiting delaying one’s own Hajj. Al-Bada’i‘ (al-Kāsānī) implies it is karahah tanzīhiyyah (light dislike) because the preferred agent is a free, knowledgeable person who has already performed Hajj.
The dispute hinges on the strength of the prohibition and the capacity of the hired agent.
3
Analyze each position’s evidence
The tahrim view relies on ahadith that command performing Hajj immediately and warn against delay. The tanzih view emphasizes that hiring a novice is still permissible and the dislike is only due to the absence of a better option, not a prohibition.
Note that both positions consider the act permissible, but differ on its moral weight.
4
Understand the author’s reconciliation
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra’iq reconciles by differentiating between the hirer (commander) and the hired agent. For the hirer, it is tanzih because he is not directly sinning. For the agent who is obligated to perform Hajj and delays, it is tahrim because he is sinning by postponing his own obligation.
This reconciliation is the 'haqq' (correct) view according to the author.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that hiring a novice is makruh tanzih for the hirer and makruh tahrim for the agent. In practice, a hirer should prefer an agent who has already performed his own Hajj, but if a novice is hired, the contract is valid, though the agent should perform his own Hajj first if possible.
This ruling reflects the balance between necessity and religious recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن حج الولد عن والده ووالدته مندوب للأحاديث كما في فتح القدير، ثم المصنف رحمه الله تعالى لم يقيد الحاج عن الغير بشيء ليفيد أنه يجوز إحجاج الضرورة وهو الذي لم يحج أولاً عن نفسه لكنه مكروه كما صرحوا به واختار في فتح القدير أنها كراهة تحريم للنهي الوارد في ذلك. وفي البدائع : يكره إحجاج المرأة والعبد والصرورة والأفضل إحجاج الحر العالم بالمناسك الذي حج عن نفسه وهو يدل على أنها كراهة تنزيه وإلا قال : ويجب إحجاج الحر إلى آخره والحق أنها تنزيهية على الآمر تحريمية على الضرورة المأمور الذي اجتمعت فيه شروط الحج ولم يحج عن نفسه لأنه آثم بالتأخير والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب
Then know that a son performing Hajj for his father and mother is recommended (mandub) according to ahadith, as in Fath al-Qadir. Then the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not restrict the one performing Hajj on behalf of another to any condition, to indicate that it is permissible to hire a novice (al-ḍarūrah) — one who has not first performed Hajj for himself — but it is disliked (makruh) as they explicitly stated. And al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir chose that it is a prohibition-level dislike (karahah tahrīm) due to the prohibition reported therein. In al-Bada'i': It is disliked to hire a woman, a slave, and a novice; the better is to hire a free person knowledgeable in rituals who has performed Hajj for himself. This indicates that the dislike is tanzihi (light), otherwise he would have said: it is obligatory to hire a free person... etc. The truth is that it is tanzihi for the commander, but prohibition-level for the novice agent who meets the conditions of Hajj and has not performed it for himself, because he is sinful by delaying. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of hiring someone (ajir) to perform Hajj on behalf of another when the hired person has not yet performed his own obligatory Hajj. Such a person is called a ḍarūrah (novice). The author notes that the original text (Kanz al-Daqā’iq) did not restrict the agent, implying it is permissible, but scholars explicitly state it is makruh. There is a dispute about the type of dislike: In Fath al-Qadir, al-Marghinani considers it karahah tahrīmiyyah (prohibition-level) because of ahadith prohibiting delaying one's own Hajj. In al-Bada'i', it is considered karahah tanzīhiyyah (light dislike) because the preferred agent is a free, knowledgeable person who has already performed Hajj. The author reconciles by stating the dislike is tanzihi for the person paying (the commander) but tahrīmi for the hired agent who is capable but delayed his own Hajj, as he is sinful.

Key Terms
الضرورة (الصرورة) (al-ḍarūrah (al-ṣarūrah)): A person who has never performed Hajj, i.e., a novice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what is the correct ruling on hiring a person who has not performed his own Hajj?
A) It is absolutely prohibited (haram).
B) It is permissible but disliked with tanzih for the hirer and tahrim for the hired agent.
C) It is absolutely permissible without any dislike.
D) It is only permissible if the hired person is a relative.

Key Takeaway
Hiring a novice for Hajj is permissible but disliked; the dislike is tanzih for the hirer and tahrim for the agent who delays his own obligation.

Must the Novice Agent Stay in Mecca to Perform Hajj?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the obligation of a hired novice to perform his own Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether a hired novice must perform his own Hajj immediately and evaluate the evidence for each.

Core Idea
A hired novice's own Hajj is not automatically obligatory upon reaching Mecca; hardship and engagement in the hired Hajj justify delay.

When a person who has never performed Hajj is hired to perform Hajj on behalf of another, a practical question arises: does he become obligated to perform his own Hajj immediately upon arriving in Mecca? This lesson explores the divergent Hanafi fatwas on this issue, focusing on the tension between immediate obligation and the hardship of staying in Mecca without means.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
Determine what exactly is disputed: whether the hired novice's own Hajj becomes wajib upon his arrival in Mecca, given that he is already in ihram for the hired Hajj.
The dispute is about the timing and condition of obligation, not the validity of the hire.
2
State the position of immediate obligation
Several Hanafi scholars (e.g., Ali al-Qari, Ibn Hamza) hold that upon seeing the Ka'ba, Hajj becomes obligatory for the novice, and he must stay until next year or perform it after returning with his own wealth.
This view relies on the general principle that Hajj is immediately obligatory when conditions are met.
3
State the position of non-obligation due to hardship
Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi and others argue that it is not obligatory because the novice is already engaged in ihram for another and would face undue hardship (haraj) if forced to stay until the next year without funds.
This view invokes the maxim 'no harm and no reciprocating harm' and the concept of hardship removal.
4
Analyze the evidence for each position
For obligation: the general command of Hajj and the hadith 'Hajj is once for everyone.' For non-obligation: the hadith 'There is no travel for Hajj except with difficulty' and the practical hardship of staying a whole year.
The author notes that a clear textual proof (nass sarih) for immediate obligation is lacking.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If obligatory, the agent must stay in Mecca, possibly in poverty. If not, he may return home and perform Hajj later when able.
The author leans toward the non-obligation view due to hardship but does not give a definitive tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا ورأيت في فتاوى العلامة حامد أفندي العمادي مفتي دمشق ما نصه: وهل يجب على حاج الصرورة أن يمكث بمكة حتى يحج عن نفسه؟ لم أره إلا في فتاوى أبي السعود المفسر بما صورته مسألة كعبة شريفة به وارمين زيد فقير عمرك حج شريف إيجون تعيين إيتدوكي اقجه أولوب عمر ونيتنه حج إيليسه شرعا جائزا ولو رمى الجواب اكرجه جائز دراما ير. دفعه حج أيده نه إيتدرمك كركدر زير ابو ندن واروب حج اشمك لازمم الورانده مجاورا وليجق عمرك لأنه حجنى اتمام اتمش أولور اهـ أقول وفي هذا الكلام بحث إن لم يوجد نقل صريح بقدرة الغير لا بقدرة نفسه وماله وإذا أتم الحج يمضي أشهر الحج فإنها شوال وذو القعدة وعشر ذي الحجة، فكيف يجب عليه المكث حتى تأتي أشهره؟ فإذا كان فقيراً وله عائلة في بلده يجب عليه المكث إلى السنة الآتية بلا نفقة مع. تركه عياله يحتاج إلى نقل صريح في ذلك فتأمل. ثم بعد ذلك رأيت بخط بعض الفضلاء ناقلاً عن مجمع الأنهر على ملتقى الأبحر ما صورته: ويجوز إحجاج الصرورة ولكن يجب عليه عند رؤية الكعبة الحج لنفسه وعليه أن يتوقف إلى عام قابل ويحج لنفسه أو أن يحج بعد عودة أهله بماله وإن فقيراً فلتحفظ والناس عنها غافلون. وصرح علي القاري في شرح مناسكه الكبير بأنه بوصوله لمكة وجب عليه الحج .اهـ. وفي نهج النجاة لابن حمزة هذه المسألة من كلام حسن فلتراجع اهـ ما رأيته في الحامدية ورأيت في بعض حواشي الدر المختار أنه أفتى بعدم وجوب الحج عليه مولانا العارف بالله تعالى الشيخ عبد الغني النابلسي لتلبسه بالإحرام عن الغير ووجود الحرج المرفوع لو أقام إلى قابل وألف في ذلك رسالة، وأفتى بخلافه مولانا السيد أحمد بادشاه في رسالة له ويدل له قول منلا عليه القاري في شرحه : لو حج الفقير نفلاً يجب عليه أن يحج حجاً ثانياً اهـ .
This: I saw in the fatwas of the scholar Hamid Afandi al-Imadi, Mufti of Damascus, its text: 'Is it obligatory for the novice pilgrim to stay in Mecca until he performs Hajj for himself? I have only seen it in the fatwas of Abu al-Su'ud al-Mufassir in the form: ...' He says: 'I say: There is discussion in this statement unless there is an explicit transmission [obligating] based on the ability of another, not his own ability and wealth. When he completes Hajj, the months of Hajj pass—they are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah—so how can it be obligatory for him to stay until its months come? If he is poor and has a family in his country, he would have to stay until the next year without expenses while leaving his family. This requires an explicit transmission; so reflect.' Then afterwards I saw in the handwriting of some scholars, quoting from Majma' al-Anhur on Multaqa al-Abhur, its text: 'It is permissible to hire a novice, but upon seeing the Ka'ba, Hajj becomes obligatory for himself, and he must wait until next year to perform Hajj for himself, or he may perform Hajj after returning to his family with his wealth, even if poor, so preserve this, for people are heedless of it.' And 'Ali al-Qari explicitly stated in his large commentary on the Manasik that upon his arrival in Mecca, Hajj becomes obligatory for him. In Nahj al-Najat of Ibn Hamza, this issue is good speech, so refer to it. I saw in al-Hamidiyyah and also in some glosses on al-Durr al-Mukhtar that he gave a fatwa of non-obligation, Mawlana al-'Arif billah Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, because he is engaged in ihram for another and due to the hardship that is removed if he stays until next year. He wrote a treatise on that. And contrary fatwa was given by Mawlana al-Sayyid Ahmad Bāshā in his treatise, supported by the saying of Mulla 'Ali al-Qari in his commentary: 'If a poor person performs a voluntary Hajj, he must perform a second Hajj.'
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical dispute: If a person who has not performed his own obligatory Hajj is hired to perform Hajj for another, does he become obligated to perform Hajj for himself upon reaching Mecca? Many scholars argue that he must, because once he is in Mecca during the Hajj season, Hajj becomes immediately obligatory upon him if he has the means. However, others, like Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, argue that since he is already in ihram for another, and it would cause hardship to stay until the next year, it is not obligatory. The author notes the diversity of opinions and cites various sources: some say he must wait and perform Hajj the following year; others say he can go back and later perform Hajj with his own wealth. The author seems to lean toward the view that it is not obligatory due to hardship, but acknowledges the strength of the opposing view. This is a classic issue of conflict between a current obligation (his own Hajj) and the discharge of a contract (hired Hajj).

Key Terms
الصرورة (al-sarrurah): A person who has never performed Hajj.
حج الصرورة (hajj al-sarrurah): The Hajj performed by a novice, often in the context of hiring.
الحرج المرفوع (al-haraj al-marfu'): Hardship that is removed by Islamic law, based on the principle of removing difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, why is a hired novice not obligated to perform his own Hajj immediately upon reaching Mecca?
A) Because he is not yet able financially.
B) Because he is in ihram for another and would face hardship if forced to stay.
C) Because the hired Hajj is invalid.
D) Because he can perform Hajj on behalf of himself later without staying.

Key Takeaway
A hired novice's obligation to perform his own Hajj immediately is not absolute; the hardship of staying in Mecca and being engaged in the hired Hajj can justify postponement.

intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Sarura Performing Hajj for Others Before Oneself
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sarura performing Hajj for others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi positions on a sarura performing Hajj for others, distinguish between makruh tahrime and tanzihi, and state the mufta bihi and its practical implication.

Core Idea
A sarura who performs Hajj for others delays his own fard, making it makruh tahrime; the act is valid but he must perform his own Hajj as soon as possible.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: can a person who has never performed Hajj (sarura) act as a proxy Hajj for another? The text moves between two levels of dislike (karahah tahrime vs tanzihi) and later fatwa positions on whether such a person must immediately perform his own Hajj. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes obligatory duties over voluntary proxy acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the actors
The act is 'ihjaj' – sending someone to perform Hajj on behalf of another. The two actors are the commissioner (amir) and the agent (the sarura, who has not performed his own fard Hajj).
The dispute focuses on the agent’s state.
2
State the two Hanafi views on the ruling
One view (from al-Bada'i) considers it makruh tanzihi for both amir and agent. Another view (from Fath al-Qadir) considers it makruh tahrime for the agent because he sins by delaying his fard.
The key is whether the prohibition is on the act itself or on the delay.
3
Distinguish between the prohibition on the act vs delay of fard
The prohibition is not for the essence of Hajj on behalf of another, but for the delay of the agent’s own obligatory Hajj. Thus the act is valid but sinful due to delay.
This is why the act is not batil but makruh tahrime.
4
Analyze the practical difference after delegated Hajj
Later authorities debate whether the sarura must stay in Mecca to perform his own Hajj immediately (after seeing the Ka'ba) or may return home and perform it later. The stricter view requires staying.
The text records opinions from Hamid al-Imadi, Ali al-Qari, Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, etc.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and the tarjih authority
The author leans towards the view from Fath al-Qadir: it is makruh tahrime for the sarura, and he must perform his own Hajj as soon as possible (upon seeing the Ka'ba). This is the relied-upon position.
Authority: The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq supports Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text

عن نفسه وهو يدل على أنها كراهة تنزيه وإلا قال : ويجب إحجاج الحر إلى آخره والحق أنها تنزيهية على الآمر تحريمية على الضرورة المأمور الذي اجتمعت فيه شروط الحج ولم يحج عن نفسه لأنه آثم بالتأخير والله القاري في شرحه : لو حج الفقير نفلاً يجب عليه أن يحج حجاً ثانياً اهـ . حج
The one who has not performed Hajj first for himself, but [does so for others] is makruh as they stated. And in Fath al-Qadir he chose that it is karahah tahrime due to the prohibition reported on that. In al-Bada'i: It is makruh to send a woman, a slave, and a first-time Hajj pilgrim (sarura), and the best is to send a free man knowledgeable in rituals who has performed Hajj for himself. This indicates that it is karahah tanzihiyya; otherwise he would have said: It is obligatory to send a free man etc. The truth is that it is tanzihi for the one who orders, tahrimi for the one being sent (the sarura) who meets the conditions of Hajj and has not performed Hajj for himself because he is sinful by delaying. Allah knows best and to Him is the return. Al-Qadir: And it is unlikely that it is said to be acceptable for both, as the apparent meaning of the last hadith might suggest, so reflect. His statement: (And he chose in Fath that it is karahah (tahrimi) - its apparent meaning is that the words of Fath are about the karahah of sending for Hajj, but that is not so; rather it is about Hajj itself. For he said: What is required by consideration is that the sarura [acting] for another, if after the obligation is established upon him by possessing the journey provisions and mount and health, then it is makruh tahrimi for him because he is constrained and in this situation in the first years of ability, so he sins by leaving it. Likewise if he performs supererogatory Hajj for himself, and it is valid because the prohibition is not for the essence of the performed Hajj but for something else, namely fear that he may not catch up with the obligatory Hajj since death in that year is not rare. End. And by this is supported what he mentioned of the investigation. This: And I saw in the fatawa of Allama Hamid Afandi al-Imadi, mufti of Damascus, the text: Is it obligatory upon the sarura pilgrim to stay in Mecca until he performs Hajj for himself? I have not seen it except in the fatawa of Abu l-Su'ud the commentator in the form: Mas'ala: ... Zaid poor ... your age Hajj ... designated ... money ... it is permissible legally ... Answer: I permit it ... but he should ... because ... he completed his Hajj. End. I say: In these words there is discussion unless there is an explicit transmission [that he has] ability of others not ability of himself and his property. And when he completes Hajj, the months of Hajj pass, which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'da, and the ten of Dhu al-Hijjah. So how is it obligatory upon him to stay until its months come? If he is poor and has a family in his country, must he stay until the next year without sustenance? Leaving his family needs an explicit transmission on that, so reflect. Then after that I saw in the handwriting of some virtuous one, quoting from Majma' al-Anhur on Multaqa al-Abhar, the text: It is permissible to send the sarura for Hajj, but when he sees the Ka'ba, it is obligatory upon him to perform Hajj for himself, and he must stop until the next year and perform Hajj for himself, or perform Hajj after his family returns with his property even if poor. So memorize, and the people are heedless of it. And Ali al-Qari in his commentary on al-Manāsik al-Kabīr explicitly stated that upon his arrival in Mecca, Hajj becomes obligatory upon him. End. And in Nahj al-Najat of Ibn Hamza, this issue is from good words, so refer to it. End. What I saw in al-Hamidiyya: And I saw in some commentaries on al-Durr al-Mukhtar that our master the knower of Allah, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, gave a fatwa that Hajj is not obligatory upon him due to his being engaged in ihram for another and the existence of hardship (haraj) that is removed if he stays until next year, and he wrote a treatise on that. And our master Sayyid Ahmad Badshah gave a fatwa contrary to that in his treatise, and supporting him is the saying of Mulla Ali al-Qari in his commentary: If a poor person performs supererogatory Hajj, he must perform a second Hajj. End. Hajj.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person (sarura) who has not performed his own obligatory Hajj but performs Hajj on behalf of someone else. The text first presents the differing views on whether this is makruh tahrime or tanzihi, referencing Fath al-Qadir and al-Bada'i. A key point is the distinction between the person commissioning (amir) and the commissioned (ma'mur): for the amir it is tanzihi, for the sarura it is tahrime because he is sinning by delaying his own fard. The passage then discusses opinions from later Hanafi authorities: Hamid al-Imadi, Abu al-Su'ud, the author of Majma' al-Anhur, Ali al-Qari, Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, and Ahmad Badshah, on whether the sarura must stay in Mecca to perform his own Hajj after completing the delegated one. The text does not settle definitively; it records the ikhtilaf and encourages reflection. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position seems to be that it is allowed but with caution; the sarura should immediately perform his own Hajj if possible.

Key Terms
صرورة (sarura): A person who has never performed Hajj in their life.
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrime): A level of disapproval that is close to haram; the act is sinful but not invalid.
إحجاج (ihjaj): The act of sending someone to perform Hajj on behalf of another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is the ruling for a sarura who performs Hajj on behalf of another person?
A) It is completely prohibited (haram).
B) It is permissible but makruh tahrime for the sarura, and he must perform his own Hajj as soon as possible.
C) It is perfectly permissible and recommended.
D) It is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
A sarura may perform Hajj for another, but it is makruh tahrimi due to delay of his own fard, and he must perform his own Hajj as soon as possible.
